Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
The Disputed Verse for Sajdat al-Tilawah: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Discussion of where sajdah becomes wajib in specific Quranic verses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the critical verse for prostration in Surahs Fussilat and Saad, and explain the Hanafi reliance on the principle of ihtiyat.

Core Idea
Precaution (ihtiyat) guides Hanafis to delay the sajdah to a later verse, avoiding premature obligation.

Sajdat al-tilawah is a wajib act upon reciting or hearing certain Quranic verses. However, the exact verse that triggers the obligation can be disputed, especially in Surahs Fussilat and Saad. This lesson examines the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions, focusing on the evidence and the principle of precaution used by Hanafi jurists to resolve the difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested surahs
Two surahs are the focus: Fussilat and Saad. For each, locate the specific verses mentioned.
Fussilat: verses 37-38. Saad: verses 24-25.
2
State the Hanafi position and proof
Hanafis hold the sajdah is at the end of the passage in Fussilat ('la yas'amun') and at 'wa kharr raaki'an' in Saad. Their evidence comes from Ibn Abbas and the Prophet's practice.
In Saad, the hadith from Ibn Abbas and the action of the Prophet are cited.
3
State the Shafi'i position and proof
Shafi'is place the sajdah at 'in kuntum iyyahu ta'budun' in Fussilat (following Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn Umar) and consider Saad's prostration as sunnah (sajdat shukr), not wajib.
For Saad, Shafi'i prohibits it in prayer.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response and ihtiyat
Hanafis argue that delaying to the later verse (la yas'amun) is precautionary: if the obligation is at the earlier verse, delay does not harm; if it is at the later, early prostration would be deficient. This reasoning is deemed a sign of juristic depth.
The principle of ihtiyat (precaution) when Companions differ.
5
Determine the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf: In prayer, Hanafis prostrate at the later verse (la yas'amun for Fussilat, wa kharr raaki'an for Saad); Shafi'is prostrate at the earlier verse in Fussilat and do not prostrate in Saad during prayer.
This affects the act of prostration during recitation and prayer.

Book of Prayer: (Ar-Rahman: 'Shall we prostrate to what you command us?' and it increased them in aversion.) (An-Naml: 'That they do not prostrate to Allah...' This is according to the general qira'ah with tashdid. And at His statement 'Ala ya'sjudu' according to the qira'ah of al-Kisa'i with takhfif. In al-Mujtaba, al-Farra' said: The sajdah in An-Naml is only obligatory according to the qira'ah of al-Kisa'i, i.e., with takhfif, and it should not be obligatory with tashdid because its meaning is 'Satan made them think it attractive not to prostrate.' The correct view is obligation on both qira'at because it was written in the mushaf of Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him). Thus in al-Dirayah. (As-Sajdah: 'Only those believe in Our verses who, when they are reminded of them, fall in prostration...') (Saad: 'And David knew that We had tested him, so he sought forgiveness of his Lord and fell down bowing [in prostration] and repented...' This is preferred over what al-Zayla'i said: It is obligatory at His statement 'wa kharr raaki'an wa anaab' and according to some at His statement 'husna ma'ab' as we will mention. (Fussilat: The prostration is at: 'Then if they are arrogant, those near your Lord exalt Him by night and day and they do not grow weary.' From His statement: 'And of His signs are the night and day and the sun and moon...' This is our madhhab, transmitted from Ibn Abbas and Wa'il ibn Hujr. According to al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him), it is at His statement 'in kuntum iyyahu ta'budun.' It is the madhhab of Ali and transmitted from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn Umar. Our imams preferred the first as a precaution. He said: 'If the sajdah were obligatory at 'ta'budun', delaying to 'la yas'amun' does not harm and fulfills the obligation. If it were obligatory at 'la yas'amun', then the sajdah intended before would have occurred before its obligation, causing a deficiency in prayer if it were a prayer prostrations. There is no deficiency in what we said.' This is a sign of deep knowledge in fiqh. (An-Najm: At His statement 'Afamin hadha al-hadithi ta'jabun...' (Al-Inshiqaq: At His statement 'Fama lahum la yu'minun...' (Al-Alaq: At His statement 'Kalla la tuti'hu wasjud waqtarib.' And we will mention the benefit of this combination. The prostration is obligatory on the one who hears...
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement of the rulings on sajdat al-tilawah (prostration of recitation) in several surahs. The author discusses the correct verse at which prostration becomes wajib according to the Hanafi school, addressing differences in qira'at and the opposing view of Imam al-Shafi'i. For Surah An-Naml, the general qira'ah has tashdid on 'ala ya'sjudu', but al-Kisa'i reads with takhfif. Al-Farra' argued that only the takhfif reading requires prostration, but the Hanafi position is that it is obligatory on both readings because the Prophet's mushaf included it. The same reasoning applies to Surah As-Sajdah. For Surah Saad, the Hanafis hold that the sajdah is at the verse 'wa kharr raaki'an wa anaab' (he fell bowing and repented), based on hadith from Ibn Abbas and Ahmad. Imam al-Shafi'i considers this a prostration of thanks (sajdat shukr), not obligatory, and prohibits it in prayer. The text then discusses Surah Fussilat, where Hanafis follow Ibn Abbas and Wa'il ibn Hujr in placing the sajdah at the end of the passage ('la yas'amun'), while Shafi'i follows Ali and others at 'in kuntum iyyahu ta'budun'. The Hanafis argue for precaution (ihtiyat): delaying to the later verse ensures fulfillment, whereas prostrating earlier might cause deficiency. This approach, derived from al-Kasani's Bada'i', is considered a sign of juristic depth. The passage also notes the sajdah locations in Surahs An-Najm, Al-Inshiqaq, and Al-Alaq, and promises to explain the benefit of combining these rulings.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing specific verses of the Quran, considered wajib in the Hanafi school.
عزائم السجود (aza'im al-sujud): The verses where prostration is firmly obligatory (wajib) according to the Hanafi school, as opposed to prostration of thanks.
الاحتياط (al-ihtiyat): The juridical principle of choosing the more cautious ruling when there is difference among Companions or uncertainty, to ensure the obligation is fulfilled.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Surah Fussilat, at which verse does the Hanafi school hold that sajdat al-tilawah becomes obligatory?
A) 'in kuntum iyyahu ta'budun'
B) 'la yas'amun'
C) 'fa in istakbaru'
D) 'wa min ayatihi al-laylu wa al-nahar'

Key Takeaway
Hanafis locate sajdat al-tilawah in disputed surahs at the later verse out of precaution, to ensure the obligation is fulfilled without causing deficiency in prayer.

Linguistic Analysis of the Word Jumu'ah
Linguistic and historical analysis of the word Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three variant pronunciations of 'Jumu'ah', explain their grammatical derivation, and describe the historical origin of the name.

Core Idea
The word Jumu'ah, rooted in 'gathering', has three classical pronunciations tied to different Arabic dialects.

Before delving into the rulings of Friday prayer, the commentator al-Tahtawi clarifies the word itself. This linguistic foundation prevents confusion: the term 'Jumu'ah' carries nuances of active and passive meanings, and its variant pronunciations reflect regional Arabic dialects. Understanding these distinctions enriches our appreciation of the term's usage in Sharia texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three pronunciations
Note the three vowel patterns on the meem (damma, fatha, sukun) and their affiliations: Hijaz (damma), Tamim (fatha), 'Uqayl (sukun).
The text states the damma is the most eloquent.
2
Understand the root and grammatical form
Recognize that 'Jumu'ah' is an ism masdar derived from ijtama'a (to gather), and that the vowel pattern indicates active or passive sense.
Damma (Hijazi) = active; sukun = passive; fatha = active with exaggeration (like dahkah).
3
Distinguish active vs passive interpretations
Based on the vowel: damma (active = the day that gathers people), sukun (passive = the day when people gather), fatha (active with ta for exaggeration).
Al-A'mash recited with sukun (passive).
4
Learn the pre-Islamic name and the dispute
Read about the name 'Aruubah and the disagreement between Ibn Hazm (Islamic name) and the majority (pre-Islamic).
The text cites authorities like al-Zajjaj and al-Farra' supporting pre-Islamic usage.
5
Note the historical origin of Friday prayer
The Ansar in Medina initiated Friday prayer before the Hijrah, calling it 'Aruubah; the Prophet later led the first official Jumu'ah in Banu Salim mosque.
This demonstrates the communal nature from the earliest days.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة الحجاز وفتحها لغة تميم، وإسكانها لغة عقيل صلاة الجمعة فرض عين بالكتاب والسنة من يوم تنوف (1) على أربعين، وقال النبي : إن يوم الجمع سيد الأيام، وأعظمها عند الله الأضحى والفطر، وقال : اليوم الموعود يوم القيامة والمشهود يوم عرفة والشاهد يوم الجمعة وقال ابن المسيب : الجمعة أحب إلى الله تعالى من حج التطوع، وعن ابن عباس مرفوعاً الجمعة حج المساكين، وفي رواية حج الفقراء قوله : (هي من الاجتماع) وهي اسم مصدر لاجتمع. قوله : ( بسكون الميم) للمفعول لأن فعلة بالسكون للمفعول كهمزة أي اليوم المجموع فيه وبها قرأ الأعمش قوله : ( والقراء يضمونها) أي يضمون الميم اتباعاً لضمة الجيم. قوله: (لغة الحجاز) وهي المشهورة الفصحى قوله وفتحها لغة تميم) بمعنى فاعل أي اليوم الجامع كضحكة وهمزة ولمزة للمكثر من ذلك، وتاؤها للمبالغة كما في علامة لا للتأنيث وإلا لما وصف بها اليوم وبه ،قرى كالسكون وهما قراءتان شاذتان، وحكى الزجاج الكسر كما في شروح البخاري، وشرح المشكاة والنهر ، وأنكر لأن فعلة بالكسر ليس من قاله الأوزان العربية، ومن قاله بالتسكين جمعه على جمع، ومن بالضم جمعه على جمعات، وهي بغير السكون اسم لليوم وبالسكون اسم لأيام الأسبوع وأولها السبت، وأول الأيام يوم الأحد، واختلف في هذه التسمية . مع الاتفاق أنه كان يدعي في الجاهلية عروبة بفتح العين المهملة، وضم الراء وبالموحدة، فقال: الزجاج والفراء، وأبو عبيدة، وأبو عمر وكانت العرب العاربة تقول ليوم السبت شيار وللأحد أول، وللإثنين أهون والثلاثاء جبار وللأربعاء دبار، وللخميس مؤنس وللجمعة ،عروبة أي، ثم نقلوها إلى تلك الأسماء المشهورة وجزم ابن حزم أنه اسم إسلامي، ولم يكن في الجاهلية وورد أنّ أهل المدينة صلوها قبل أن يقدم رسول الله ، وذلك أن الأنصار قالوا لليهود يوم يجتمعون فيه كل سبعة أيام، وكذلك للنصارى : فهلم فلنجعل يوماً نجتمع فيه، ونذكر الله تعالى ونصلي ونشكره، فجعلوه يوم العروبة، وهي أول جمعة في الإسلام وأما أول جمعة جمعها رسول الله ، فكانت في مسجد بني سالم بن عوف فخطب، وصلى فيه .
Book of Prayer. (Jumu'ah) with a damma on the jim and sukun on the meem: the language of the Hijaz; and with a fatha on the meem: the language of Tamim; and with a sukun on the meem: the language of 'Uqayl. Friday prayer is individual obligation by the Book and the Sunnah. From a day that exceeds forty... And the Prophet said: Indeed, the day of assembly (Jumu'ah) is the master of days, and the greatest of them in the sight of Allah are (the days of) al-Adha and al-Fitr. And he said: The promised day is the Day of Resurrection, and the witnessed day is the Day of Arafah, and the witness is the day of Jumu'ah. And Ibn al-Musayyib said: Jumu'ah is more beloved to Allah Almighty than supererogatory Hajj. And from Ibn Abbas, raised to the Prophet: Jumu'ah is the Hajj of the poor; in another narration: the Hajj of the needy. His statement: (It is from 'ijtima') meaning it is a verbal noun of ijtama'a. His statement: (with sukun on the meem) is for the passive, because fa'lah with sukun is for the passive object, like humzah, meaning the day in which one gathers. And al-A'mash recited it that way. His statement: (and the reciters put a damma on it) i.e., they put a damma on the meem following the damma of the jim. His statement: (the language of the Hijaz) which is the well-known and most eloquent. His statement: 'and with a fatha, the language of Tamim' is in the sense of the active participle, i.e., the day that gathers, like dahkah and humzah and lumzah for one who does that a lot; and its ta is for exaggeration, as in 'allamah, not for femininity, otherwise it could not be used to describe the day. And it was recited with a fatha like the sukun, and both are irregular recitations. Al-Zajjaj reported a kasrah as in the commentaries of al-Bukhari, Sharh al-Mishkat, and al-Nahr, but he denied it because fa'lah with kasrah is not among the Arabic measures. And those who say it with sukun pluralize it as jumu'; those who say it with damma pluralize it as jumu'at. And it without sukun is a name for the day, and with sukun is a name for the days of the week, the first of which is Saturday. And the first of the days (i.e., of the week) is Sunday. And there is disagreement about this naming. Despite agreement that it was called in the Jahiliyyah 'Aruubah (with a fatha on the 'ayn, a damma on the ra, and a ba). Al-Zajjaj, al-Farra', Abu 'Ubayda, and Abu 'Umar said: The pure Arabs used to say for Saturday: Shiyar; for Sunday: Awwal; for Monday: Ahwan; for Tuesday: Jabbar; for Wednesday: Dubar; for Thursday: Mu'nis; and for Friday: 'Aruubah. Then they changed them to these well-known names. And Ibn Hazm firmly held that it is an Islamic name and did not exist in the Jahiliyyah. And it is reported that the people of Medina prayed it before the arrival of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). That was because the Ansar said to the Jews: you have a day you gather every seven days, and similarly the Christians; so come let us make a day we gather, remember Allah Almighty, pray, and thank Him. So they made it the day of 'Aruubah, and that was the first Friday in Islam. As for the first Friday that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) led, it was in the mosque of Banu Salim ibn 'Awf; he delivered a sermon and prayed in it.
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage is a linguistic and historical introduction by the commentator (al-Tahtawi) to the word 'Jumu'ah'. He begins by noting the different Arabic pronunciations (damma, fatha, sukun on the meem) and their regional affiliations, explaining that the damma is the most eloquent and common. The root meaning is 'gathering' (ijtima'). The commentator then delves into the pre-Islamic name 'Aruubah', citing various authorities, and notes Ibn Hazm's view that the name 'Jumu'ah' is Islamic. Finally, he relates the historical origin of Friday prayer in Medina before the Hijrah. This lesson is purely linguistic and historical, establishing the terminology before the legal discussion.

Key Terms
الجمعة (al-Jumu'ah): The name for Friday, derived from social gathering (ijtima'), with variant readings indicating different grammatical senses.
عروبة ('Aruubah): The pre-Islamic name for Friday, meaning the day of gathering or the 'Arab day'.
صلاة الجمعة (Salat al-Jumu'ah): The Friday prayer, a fard ayn obligation performed in congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The Ansar in Medina
B) The Muhajirun in Mecca
C) The Jews in Arabia
D) The Christians in Najran

Key Takeaway
The name 'Jumu'ah' has multiple classical pronunciations but its root meaning of 'gathering' remains central to understanding the communal nature of Friday prayer.

Ruling on Trimming Nails and Shaving Hair on Friday
Discussion of recommended and disliked timings for nail and hair grooming on Friday

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on trimming nails on Friday and distinguish when it is mustahabb versus makruh based on the degree of delay.

Core Idea
Trimming nails on Friday is mustahabb for blessing, but makruh if delayed beyond the normal period.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi completes the discussion of cleanliness by addressing the specific timing of nail trimming and hair shaving on Friday. The author quotes earlier Hanafi sources to clarify the ruling, emphasizing that the intention and degree of delay determine whether the act is recommended or disliked. Understanding this nuance helps the believer maximize rewards and avoid disapproval.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling category
The act is trimming nails and shaving hair on Friday. The ruling is not absolute; it depends on the degree of delay. Determine whether the person delayed excessively or not.
2
Locate the proof from Sunnah
The passage cites a marfu' hadith of Aisha (RA) mentioning expiation from one Friday to the next with three extra days. This makes the act mustahabb when done with proper intention.
The hadith is ahad, thus zanni in transmission, but supports the recommendation.
3
Examine the condition of excessive delay
If the delay is 'fahish' (excessive) – meaning the nails have grown beyond the normal limit – then postponing to Friday becomes makruh. The passage mentions that long nails constrict provision, which is disliked.
Normal limit is typically considered within 40 days; exceeding 40 days is sinful per another narration.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
Some Hanafi scholars consider trimming nails on Friday unconditionally mustahabb, while others condition it on not being excessively overdue. The text resolves this by stating the latter view as the relied-upon position.
The authority of the resolution comes from later Hanafi works like al-Khaniyya and al-Khulasa.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The operative ruling is: trimming nails on Friday is mustahabb if done within a reasonable time frame; if excessively delayed, it becomes makruh. One should aim for weekly grooming, with Friday as the best day.
This is derived from the combination of the hadith and the principle of istihsan.

Completion of complete cleanliness: trimming nails and shaving hair. He said in al-Khaniyya and al-Khulasa from the book of Istihsan: A man delayed cutting his nails or shaving his head on Friday. They said: If he delayed it to Friday excessively, meaning he exceeded the limit, it is disliked because if his nail is long, his provision is constricted. If he did not exceed the limit and delayed it seeking blessing from the reports, then it is mustahabb due to what 'A'isha narrated as marfu': '... from affliction to the next Friday and an increase of three days.' In the Istihsan of al-Qahistani from al-Zahidi: It is mustahabb to trim his nails, cut his mustache, shave his pubic area, and clean his body once every week, and Friday is best, then every fifteen days, and exceeding forty days is sinful. And it is reported: Whoever trims his nails on Friday, Allah removes illness from him and brings in cure. And it is reported: Whoever uses the miswak on Friday, cuts his mustache, trims his nails, plucks his armpit, and bathes, then he has ... (the text ends abruptly). Footnote: In one copy, 'his nails' (azfar) is written as 'azfar'.

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya completes the discussion of cleanliness by addressing nail trimming and shaving on Friday. It quotes rulings from al-Khaniyya and al-Khulasa: If one delays cutting nails or shaving until Friday excessively (beyond the normal period), it is makruh (disliked) because long nails constrict provision. However, if one keeps them within normal limits and delays to Friday out of seeking blessing, it is mustahabb. The proof is a hadith from Aisha that it expiates sins. Al-Qahistani relates that it is mustahabb to groom weekly, with Friday being best; exceeding forty days is sinful. The passage also mentions that trimming nails on Friday brings cure, and that combining miswak, mustache cutting, nail trimming, armpit plucking, and ghusl completes the cleanliness. The footnote notes a variant spelling.

Key Terms
قص الظفر (qas al-zufr): Trimming fingernails and toenails as part of personal hygiene.
حلق الشعر (halq al-sha'r): Shaving hair, particularly head or pubic area.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference used to derive rulings based on ease and custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Trimming nails on Friday is a recommended sunnah, but becomes disliked if delayed beyond the normal grooming period.

Trimming Nails and Hair on Friday: Ruling and Recommended Practice
Explains ruling, evidence, and critique of baseless customs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on trimming nails and hair before Friday, identify the primary evidence, and distinguish between authentic sunnah and baseless customs.

Core Idea
Trimming nails before Friday is sunnah, not fard; its virtue is based on ahadith, not fabricated days-of-the-week claims.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies the Islamic etiquette of grooming before Friday. It distinguishes between the authentic recommendation rooted in the Sunnah and the baseless poetic attributions that associate each day of the week with specific outcomes. The lesson will equip you to confidently apply the Hanafi position and avoid common innovations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central ruling
Determine the hukm level for trimming nails and hair before Friday: it is mustahabb (sunnah), not obligatory. Note that excessive delay (beyond forty days) is sinful.
The text mentions dislike if delayed to Friday excessively without reason.
2
Locate the primary evidence
Find the hadith evidence cited: the marfu' hadith of Aisha about forgiveness from Friday to Friday plus three days, and the hadith about removing disease. Classify these as ahad, zanni al-thubut.
These are not mutawatir, so they indicate recommendation, not obligation.
3
Analyze the strength of the dalil
Explain why the evidence proves sunnah and not fard: the imperative is not explicit for obligation, and the context of reward shows virtue rather than command.
The phrase 'akhraja Allāh minhu al-dā'' indicates reward, not legal obligation.
4
Note the textual/interpretive issue
Some claim trimming should be after Friday prayer, but the ahadith indicate before. Why is the claim against the text rejected? Because it contradicts the apparent meaning and has no strong evidence.
The text states 'ظاهر الأحاديث' – the apparent meaning is before prayer.
5
Critique the poetic order claims
Evaluate the alleged poetic order linking days to outcomes. Ibn Daqiq al-'Id rejected it as baseless. The only established order is beginning with the right hand and right foot based on tayāmun, with hands before feet by analogy with wudu.
The poetic order is considered an innovation; no authentic evidence supports it.

Completion of cleanliness: trimming nail and shaving hair. He said in al-Khaniya and al-Khulasa from Kitab al-Istihsan: A man's time for trimming his nails or shaving his head on Friday. They said: If he delays it to Friday excessively, meaning he has exceeded the limit, it is disliked because a person with long nails has his sustenance restricted. If he did not exceed the limit and delayed it seeking blessing through reports, then it is mustahabb, because of what Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) narrated marfu'an: '...from affliction to the next Friday, and an increase of three days.' And in the Istihsan of al-Qahistani from al-Zahidi: It is mustahabb to trim his nails, trim his mustache, shave his pubic hair, and clean his body once a week, and Friday is best, then every fifteen days, and exceeding forty days is sinful. And it is reported: Whoever trims his nails on Friday, Allah removes disease from him and brings in cure. And it is reported: Whoever uses a toothstick on Friday, trims his mustache, trims his nails, plucks his armpit hair, and performs ghusl, has indeed obligated. And it is transmitted from al-Thawri the recommendation of trimming nails on Thursday, and some scholars made it a cause of wealth, but the ahadith about Friday are more numerous, so this does not oppose it. The apparent meaning of the ahadith indicates that the trimming is before the prayer. So what is in some books that it is after the prayer so that he may bear witness to the prayer is not relied upon because it is a reasoning in opposition to the text. And the statement of some: 'The recommendation of trimming nails on a specific day is not established' means 'not authentic'—not that it is not established at all. Some said: They are trimmed according to the well-known poetic order. This is in Sharh al-Shur'a. In Fath al-Bari: Imam Ahmad explicitly stated this manner. Al-Sharaf al-Dimyati narrated from some of his shaykhs: Whoever trims his nails contrary (to the order) will not suffer from ophthalmia, and he claimed to have tried it over a long period. But Ibn Daqiq al-'Id rejected the mentioned manner and said: All this has no basis, and initiating a recommendation without evidence is ugly in my view. Yes, beginning with the right hand and right foot is established because he (the Prophet) liked to begin with the right in his purification, combing, and all his affairs—agreed upon. Likewise, beginning with the hands before the feet is by analogy with wudu. What is attributed to 'Ali and others concerning the poetic order is false, like 'appearance of leprosy in cutting on Saturday', 'loss of blessing on Sunday', 'attaining honor and dignity on Monday', 'destruction on Tuesday', 'bad character on Wednesday', 'wealth on Thursday', and 'forbearance and knowledge on Friday'. Then, trimming nails is removing the part that exceeds the fingertip from the nail with scissors, a knife, or other tools. It is disliked to use teeth because it causes leprosy and madness. Similarly for hair removal because of the hadith of Khalid marfu'an: 'Whoever uses depilatory lime before bathing, every hair comes and says: O Lord, ask him why he wasted me and did not wash me.' This is in Sharh Shari'at al-Islam from Majma' al-Fatawa and others. The meaning of trimming nails is that dirt collects under them and becomes filthy, and it may reach a limit that prevents water reaching what must be washed in purification. Exaggeration in removing nails to a limit that does not harm the finger is recommended, as in Fath al-Bari. As for shaving the head, in al-Tatarkhaniyya from al-Tahawi that it is sunnah according to our three imams. In Rawdat al-Zand: 'The sunnah concerning hair of the head is either parting or shaving it all.' Meaning: shaving all, if he intends cleaning, or leaving all to oil, comb, and part because of what is in Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i from Ibn 'Umar that...
Source pages p. 524

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi addresses the rulings related to trimming nails and removing hair in the context of Friday. The author begins by stating that trimming nails and shaving hair is part of complete cleanliness. He references al-Khaniya and al-Khulasa from Kitab al-Istihsan, stating that if a person delays trimming his nails or shaving his head to Friday excessively, it is makruh because long nails constrict sustenance. However, if the delay is not excessive and is done to seek blessing from reports, it is mustahabb. The proof is a hadith from Aisha (marfu') that connects trimming nails to forgiveness from one Friday to the next, with an extra three days. The author then cites al-Qahistani that it is mustahabb to trim nails, mustache, pubic hair, and clean the body weekly, with Friday being best, and exceeding forty days is sinful. He also quotes a hadith that trimming nails on Friday removes disease. The text notes a report that using a toothstick, trimming mustache and nails, plucking armpit hair, and performing ghusl on Friday 'obligates' something—interpreted as demonstrating strong recommendation. Al-Thawri recommended Thursday, but the Friday ahadith are more numerous. The apparent meaning of ahadith indicates trimming before the prayer; any claim that it should be after is not relied upon. The author then discusses the order of trimming, noting that beginning with the right hand and right foot is established by the Prophet's practice, and hands before feet by analogy with wudu. He rejects alleged poetic orders attributing specific days to specific effects as baseless. The legal ruling: trimming nails is recommended (mustahabb), done with scissors or knife; using teeth is makruh because it causes leprosy and madness. The rationale is to remove dirt that may prevent water reaching the skin in wudu. Exaggeration is recommended as long as it does not harm the finger. Finally, shaving the head is sunnah according to the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad).

Key Terms
قص ظفر (qas zufr): Trimming the part of the nail that protrudes beyond the fingertip.
سنة (sunnah): A recommended practice; omission is not sinful but commendable to do.
تيامن (tayāmun): Beginning with the right side in all good actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is haram (forbidden) because it resembles non-Muslims.

Key Takeaway
Trimming nails before Friday is a recommended sunnah based on authentic ahadith; the only established order is beginning with the right due to tayāmun.

Rulings on Cutting Nails and Hair Removal Before Ghusl
Rulings on nail cutting and hair removal in janaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cutting nails (sunnah), identify the disliked method (teeth), and explain why removing hair before ghusl is makruh with its dalil.

Core Idea
Cutting nails is sunnah, but order and day are not obligatory; removing hair before ghusl is makruh.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi clarifies several rulings related to nail cutting and hair removal. It discusses the preferred day (Friday), the correct order of cutting, the prohibition of using teeth, and the special ruling for janaba. Understanding these helps a Muslim perform these acts in accordance with the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the preferred day for cutting nails
The author states that the hadiths for Friday are more numerous, so Friday is recommended over Thursday. Note the difference with al-Thawri.
The Friday recommendation is stronger due to more ahadith.
2
Understand the established order and the dispute
The sunnah is to start with the right hand and right foot, and hands before feet. Some narrate a specific order from Ali, but Ibn Daqiq al-'Id rejected it as baseless.
Only the right-side precedence and hand-before-foot order are confirmed.
3
Define nail cutting and the disliked method
Nail cutting is removing the excess beyond the fingertip. It is makruh to use teeth because it can cause leprosy and insanity.
Using scissors, knife, or clippers is fine; teeth are disliked.
4
State the ruling on hair removal in janaba
It is makruh to remove pubic or underarm hair before ghusl, based on the hadith that each hair will complain.
The hadith of Khalid is used as evidence.
5
Extract the wisdom behind nail cutting
The purpose is to remove dirt and ensure water reaches the skin during purification.
Thorough cutting is recommended, but not to the point of harming the finger.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أوجب، ونقل عن الثوري استحباب تقليم الأظفار يوم الخميس، وجعله بعض العلماء سبباً للغنى، وأحاديث يوم الجمعة أكثر فلا يعارضه هذا، وظاهر الأحاديث يدل على أن القلم قبل الصلاة فما في بعض الكتب أنه بعدها ليشهد له بالصلاة لا يعوّل عليه لأنه تعليل في مقابلة النص، وقول بعضهم لم يثبت في استحباب قص الأظفار يوم معين مراد لم يصح لا أنه لم يثبت أصلاً. قال بعضهم وتقص على ترتيب النظم المشهور. أصل، وهو [؟] أظـفـاركم [؟] . كذا في شرح الشرعة، وفي فتح الباري: إن الإمام أحمد قد نص على هذه الكيفية، ونقل الشرف الدمياطي عن بعض مشايخه أن من قص أظفاره مخالفاً لا يرمد، وانه جرب ذلك مدة طويلة اهـ لكن أنكر الهيئة المذكورة ابن دقيق العيد فقال : كل ذلك لا أصل له وإحداث استحباب لا دليل عليه وهو قبيح عندي بالعالم نعم البداءة بيمنى اليدين ويمني الرجلين لها أنه كان يعجبه التيامن في طهوره وترجله وفي شأنه كله متفق عليه وكذا تقديم اليدين على الرجلين قياساً على الوضوء، وما يعزى من النظم في قص الأظفار، لعلي وغيره باطل كظهور الأكلة في قص يوم السبت، وذهاب البركة في الأحد وحصول العز والجاه في الاثنين، والهلكة في الثلاثاء وسوء الأخلاق في الأربعاء، والغنى في الخميس، والحلم والعلم في الجمعة، ثم قص الأظفار هو إزالة ما يزيد على ما يلابس رأس الإصبع من الظفر بمقص، أو سكين أو غيرهما ويكره بالأسنان لأنه يورث البرص والجنون وفي حالة الجناية وكذا إزالة الشعر لما روى خالد مرفوعاً من تنوّر قبل أن يغتسل جاءته كل شعرة فتقول : يا رب سله لم ضيعني ، ولم يغسله كذا في شرح شرعة الإسلام عن مجمع الفتاوى وغيره والمعنى في قص الأظفار أن الوسخ تجتمع تحتها فيستقذر، وقد ينتهي إلى حد يمنع وصول الماء إلى ما يجب غسله في الطهارة، وتستحب المبالغة في إزالة الأظفار إلى حد لا يضر بالإصبع كذا في فتح الباري
He made it obligatory, and it is narrated from al-Thawri that trimming nails on Thursday is recommended, and some scholars made it a cause of wealth, but the hadiths of Friday are more numerous so this does not contradict them. The apparent meaning of the hadiths indicates that the trimming is before prayer, so what is in some books that it is after it so that it may testify for him in prayer is not relied upon because it is a reasoning in opposition to the text. And the statement of some that the recommendation of cutting nails on a specific day has not been established means it has not been authentically reported, not that it has not been established at all. Some said: and they are cut according to the well-known order. An origin, and it is [؟] your nails [؟]. Thus in Sharh al-Shar'a, and in Fath al-Bari: Imam Ahmad has stated this manner, and al-Sharaf al-Dimyati narrated from some of his shaykhs that whoever cuts his nails contrary to this will not suffer from ophthalmia, and he tested that for a long time. But Ibn Daqiq al-'Id denied the mentioned form and said: all of that has no basis and inventing a recommendation without evidence is ugly in my view for a scholar. Yes, beginning with the right hand and right foot because he used to like right-sidedness in his purification, combing, and all his affairs, agreed upon. Likewise, giving precedence to hands over feet by analogy with wudu. And what is attributed of the order in cutting nails to 'Ali and others is false, like the appearance of a sore in cutting on Saturday, loss of blessing on Sunday, attaining honor and status on Monday, destruction on Tuesday, bad character on Wednesday, wealth on Thursday, and forbearance and knowledge on Friday. Then cutting nails is removing what exceeds what touches the tip of the finger of the nail with scissors, a knife, or other than them, and it is disliked with teeth because it causes leprosy and insanity. And in the state of janaba, similarly the removal of hair, because of what Khalid narrated marfu'an: whoever uses depilatory before he bathes, every hair will come and say: O Lord, ask him why he wasted me and did not wash me. Thus in Sharh Shar'at al-Islam from Majma' al-Fatawa and others. And the meaning in cutting nails is that dirt collects under them and becomes unpleasant, and it may reach a limit that prevents water from reaching what must be washed in purification. And it is recommended to be thorough in removing nails to an extent that does not harm the finger, thus in Fath al-Bari.
Source pages p. 525

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi discusses the rulings related to cutting nails and removing hair before ghusl. The author begins by mentioning the difference of opinion regarding the preferred day for trimming nails: al-Thawri considers Thursday recommended, but the majority of hadiths point to Friday, so the Friday recommendation is stronger. He then notes that the apparent meaning of the hadiths is that trimming should be done before the prayer, not after. Then he discusses the order of cutting nails, citing a well-known order attributed to 'Ali, which Imam Ahmad confirmed, but Ibn Daqiq al-'Id rejected as baseless. The author asserts that the only established sunnah is to start with the right hand and right foot, and to give precedence to hands over feet, by analogy with wudu. He then defines cutting nails as removing the part extending beyond the fingertip, using scissors, a knife, or similar. Using teeth is makruh because it causes leprosy and insanity. Then he adds a ruling for janaba: it is makruh to remove hair (pubic and underarm) before bathing, because of the hadith that each hair will complain on the Day of Judgment. Finally, he explains the wisdom behind cutting nails: to prevent dirt from accumulating under them, which could prevent water from reaching the skin during purification. It is recommended to cut nails thoroughly without harming the finger.

Key Terms
تقليم الأظفار (taqlim al-azfar): Trimming or cutting the nails to remove the excess portion beyond the fingertip.
الجناية (al-janabah): State of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on cutting nails with teeth according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is mustahabb (recommended) because it is easier.
B) It is makruh (disliked) because it can cause leprosy and insanity.
C) It is haram (forbidden) because it harms the teeth.
D) It is mubah (permissible) without any dislike.

Key Takeaway
Cutting nails is a sunnah; Friday is preferred but not obligatory; using teeth and removing hair before ghusl are both makruh.

Rulings on Shaving the Head and Nape
Rulings on shaving the head and nape of the neck

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shaving the head and nape, explain the hadith evidence, and identify the exception for cupping.

Core Idea
Shaving the head is sunnah; shaving only the nape is makruh unless for cupping.

The Hanafi school considers shaving the entire head a sunnah act, based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the Companions. However, shaving only the nape of the neck (al-qafa) is disliked, except when done for a medical purpose such as cupping (hijama). This lesson unpacks the textual evidence from a hadith in Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i, and clarifies the distinction between these two rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage gives two distinct rulings: shaving the entire head (halq al-ra's) and shaving only the nape (qafa). Determine the hukm level for each: shaving the head is sunnah; shaving the nape alone is makruh, except for cupping.
The ruling on shaving the head is based on the consensus of the three Hanafi imams.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is a hadith from Ibn 'Umar: the Prophet saw a boy with partially shaved hair and commanded to shave all or leave all. This hadith is reported by Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i.
This hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), but it is accepted as evidence for the ruling.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's command to 'shave all or leave all' indicates that partial shaving is not allowed, but both complete shaving and complete leaving are permissible. The permissibility of complete shaving is derived from the absence of prohibition; the Hanafis treat it as sunnah due to the Prophet's own practice and the fact that he used to have long hair at times but also shaved.
The hadith does not directly command shaving; it only prohibits partial shaving, thus allowing both complete shaving and complete leaving.
4
Identify the distinction for the nape
The text from Sharh al-Niqaya states that shaving the nape alone is makruh unless done for cupping. This is because shaving the nape in isolation is considered contrary to the sunnah of either keeping hair fully or shaving it fully. The exception for cupping shows that medical necessity can override the general dislike.
Cupping (hijama) is a legitimate reason to shave the nape, as it requires access to the skin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما حلق الرأس ففي التتارخانية عن الطحاوي أنه سن عند أئمتنا الثلاثة اهـ وفي روضة الزند ويستى السنة في شعر الرأس أما الفرق، وأما الحلق اهـ يعني حلق الكل، إن أراد التنظيف، أو ترك الكل ليدهنه ويرجله ويفرقه لما في أبي داود والنسائي عن ابن عمران أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم رأى صبياً حلق بعض رأسه وترك بعضه فقال : احلقوه كله أو اتركوه كله؟ وفي الغرائب يستحب حلق الشعر في كل جمعة وفي شرح النقاية عن الإمام يكره أن يحلق قفاه إلا عند الحجامة ،أهـ
As for shaving the head, in al-Tatarkhaniyya from al-Tahawi: it is sunnah according to our three imams. And in Rawdat al-Zand: the sunnah is in the hair of the head, either parting or shaving, meaning shaving all of it, if he intends cleaning, or leaving all of it to oil, comb, and part it, because of what is in Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i from Ibn 'Umar that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) saw a boy who had shaved part of his head and left part, so he said: 'Shave all of it or leave all of it.' And in al-Ghara'ib: it is recommended to shave the hair every Friday. And in Sharh al-Niqaya from al-Imam: it is disliked to shave the nape except at the time of cupping.
Source pages p. 525

Commentary
This section discusses the rulings on shaving the head. The author cites al-Tahawi's statement that shaving the head is sunnah according to the three Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad). Then he mentions that the sunnah in the hair of the head is either to part it or to shave it all. The hadith from Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i indicates that it is not allowed to shave only part of the head; one must either shave all or leave all. It is recommended to shave every Friday. However, it is disliked to shave only the nape (back of the neck) except in the case of cupping (hijama).

Key Terms
حلق الرأس (halq al-ra's): Shaving all the hair on the head.
القفا (al-qafa): The nape of the neck.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on shaving only the nape of the neck (qafa) according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is sunnah to do it every Friday.
B) It is makruh except for cupping.
C) It is haram because it imitates non-Muslims.
D) It is mustahabb because it is part of grooming.

Key Takeaway
Shaving the entire head is sunnah; shaving only the nape is disliked except for medical necessity like cupping.

Rulings on Trimming the Mustache and Beard
Rulings on mustache and beard trimming

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on trimming the mustache and beard, and apply the sunnah of a fist-length to the beard while distinguishing the exception for a mujahid.

Core Idea
The Hanafi sunnah: trim the mustache short, keep the beard to a fist's length.

This lesson covers two related grooming practices: the mustache and the beard. The Hanafi school has detailed recommendations based on reports from the Companions, particularly 'Umar (RA). The core principle is that moderation is beloved, and extreme length is discouraged. An important exception is made for the warrior (mujahid) who may keep his mustache and nails long for practical reasons.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for the mustache
Find the statement of Al-Tahawi and the Imam regarding mustache trimming. Note that it is sunnah to trim closely (ihfa') but not to shave completely.
The mustache should be trimmed so that it aligns with the upper edge of the upper lip.
2
Identify the ruling for the beard
Locate the report from Muhammad in al-Athar that the sunnah is to cut what exceeds a fist's length. Also note that the width should be trimmed to avoid excessive length.
The measure is a fist-length from the chin.
3
Examine the proof
Look at the narration from 'Umar (RA) where he trimmed a man's beard beyond a fist and then criticized him, saying, 'Do you leave yourself until you become like a wild beast?' This is taken as evidence for the sunnah.
The proof is an Athar (companion report) and is considered zanni in both transmission and meaning.
4
Note the exception for the mujahid
Read the statement that the scholars excepted the mujahid: it is recommended for him to keep his nails long and his mustache long because these are weapons and awe-inspiring.
This is an application of the principle 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (matters are judged by their intentions).
5
Apply the rulings
Summarize that for a normal person, trimming the mustache and beard to a fist-length is sunnah. For a mujahid, the recommendation is reversed for practical reasons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الطحاوي: يستحب إحفاء الشوارب ونراه أفضل من قضاه، وفي شرح شرعة الإسلام قال الإمام : الإحفاء قريب من الحلق وأما الحلق فلم يرد، بل كرهه بعض العلماء ورآه بدعة اهـ وفي الخانية وينبغي أن يأخذ من شاربه حتى يوازي الطرف الأعلى من الشفة العليا، ويصير مثل الحاجب .اهـ. وعن الشعبي كان يقص شاربه حتى يظهر طرف الشفة العليا، وما قاربه من أعلاه، ويأخذ ما شد مما فوق ذلك وينزع ما قارب الشفة من جانبي الفم ولا يزيد على ذلك اهـ قال في فتح الباري: وهذا أعدل ما وقفت عليه من الآثار، ويشرع قص مع الشارب لأنهما منه كما استظهره في فتح الباري، واستثنى مشايخنا المجاهد فقالوا : تندب له توفير أظفاره لأنها سلاح، وشاربه لأنه أهيب في عين العدو وأما اللحية فذكر محمد في الآثار عن الإمام أن السنة أن يقطع ما زاد على قبضة يده قال : نأخذ كذا . وبه في محيط السرخسي، وكذا يأخذ من عرضها ماطال وخرج عن السمت التقرب من التدوير من جميع الجوانب لأن الإعدال محبوب والطول المفرط قد يشوه الخلقة ويطلق ألسنة المغتابين وأخرج الطبراني عن عمر أنه أخذ من لحية رجل ما زاد على القبضة، ثم قال له: يترك أحدكم نفسه حتى يكون كأنه سبع من السباع
Al-Tahawi said: It is recommended to trim the mustache closely, and we consider it better than cutting it. In Sharh Shar'at al-Islam, al-Imam said: 'Closely trimming is close to shaving, but shaving has not been reported; rather, some scholars disliked it and considered it an innovation.' In al-Khaniyya: It is recommended to take from his mustache until it aligns with the upper edge of the upper lip, and it becomes like an eyebrow. And from al-Sha'bi: He used to trim his mustache until the edge of the upper lip appeared, and what was close to it from above, and he would take what grew above that and remove what was near the lip from the sides of the mouth, and not exceed that. In Fath al-Bari: This is the most balanced of what I have found of reports. And it is legislated to trim along with the mustache because they are from it, as al-'Asqalani asserted. Our shaykhs excepted the mujahid and said: It is recommended for him to keep his nails long because they are weapons, and his mustache because it is more awe-inspiring in the eyes of the enemy. As for the beard, Muhammad mentioned in al-Athar from al-Imam that the sunnah is to cut what exceeds a fist's length. He said: We take this. And it is in Muhit al-Sarakhsi. Likewise, take from its width what is long and exceeds the proper appearance, approaching rounding from all sides because moderation is beloved, and extreme length may disfigure the appearance and unleash the tongues of backbiters. And al-Tabarani narrated from 'Umar that he took from a man's beard what exceeded a fist, then said to him: 'Do you leave yourself until you become like a wild beast?'
Source pages p. 526

Commentary
This passage addresses the trimming of the mustache and beard. Al-Tahawi states that trimming the mustache closely (ihfa') is recommended and better than just trimming. The Imam (Abu Hanifa) says that closely trimming is close to shaving, but shaving the mustache is not reported and disliked. The guidance is to trim it so that it aligns with the upper lip, making it like an eyebrow. For the beard, the sunnah according to Imam Muhammad from Abu Hanifa is to cut whatever exceeds a fist's length. This is also the position in al-Muhit. Additionally, one should trim the width of the beard to avoid excessive length that looks unkempt. An exception is made for the mujahid (warrior) who is recommended to keep his nails and mustache long for martial reasons.

Key Terms
الإحفاء (al-ihfa'): Shaving or trimming the mustache very close to the skin.
القبضة (al-qabdah): A fist-length, used as measure for beard trimming.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how should a man's beard be trimmed?
A) It should not be trimmed at all.
B) It should be trimmed to a fist's length.
C) It should be completely shaved.
D) It should be trimmed only on the sides.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends closely trimming the mustache and cutting the beard to a fist's length, with an exception for the mujahid.

Rulings on Plucking Gray Hairs, Nose Hair, and Eyebrows
Rulings on various hair removal practices

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on various hair removal practices, distinguish between permissible, disliked, and prohibited actions, and cite the relevant evidence.

Core Idea
Plucking gray hair is disliked when excessive; nose hair should be trimmed; eyebrow plucking for beautification is prohibited.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's commentary gathers several common hair removal rulings, each with its own evidence and nuance. Understanding these distinctions helps avoid both unnecessary restriction and transgression. The rulings range from permissible trimming to disliked plucking and outright prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify each practice
List all hair removal practices mentioned: plucking the finikayn, cleaning/trimming nose hair, plucking gray hair, shaving head and back, shaving throat, removing hair from eyebrows/face.
Each has its own ruling.
2
Determine the hukm for each
For each practice, find the explicit ruling: bid'ah (innovation), mustahabb/permissible, makruh, khilaf al-adab, haram.
Pay attention to conditions like quantity.
3
Locate the evidence
Identify the dalil for each ruling: hadith, qawl of Abu Hanifa, or fatwa.
The hadith for gray hair is from Abu Dawud.
4
Note the distinctions
Observe that gray hair ruling differs by amount (little vs. large), and nose hair is trimmed not plucked.
Abu Hanifa did not dislike a little plucking.
5
Summarize the mufta bihi
State the operative ruling for each practice as per the later Hanafi authorities.
Large amount of gray hair plucking is makruh tanzih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الفتاوى الهندية عن الغرائب : نتف الفنيكين بدعة وهما جانبا العنفقة ،أهـ قال في الصحاح والقاموس الفنيك بالفاء والنون كامير والمثنى فنيكان، وهما مجمع اللحيين أو طرفاهما عند العنفقة وفي الحديث : إذا توضأت، فلا تنس الفنيكين يعني جانبي العنفقة عن يمين وشمال قال بعض ويؤخذ مما تقدم مشروعية تنظيف داخل الأنف، وأخذ شعره إذا طال لأن الأذى كالمخاط يعلق به اهـ وروى الشهاب القليوبي في كتاب البدور المنوّرة في معرفة رتبة الأحاديث المشتهرة: لا تنتفوا شعر الأنف، فأنه يورث الجذام، أنه ولكن قصوه قصاً :وقال ضعيف، وقيل حسن، وروي يورث الأكلة وهي بتثليث (1) الهمزة الحكة ونباته أمان من الجذام وفي الخلاصة عن المنتقى كان أبو حنيفة لا يكره نتف الشيب إلا على وجه التزين اهـ وينبغي حمله على القليل أما الكثير فيكره لخبر أبي داود: لا تنتفوا الشيب، فإنه نور المسلم يوم القيامة، وفي القنية : حلق شعر الرأس والظهر خلاف الأدب : وفي المحيط : لا يحلق شعر حلقه، ولا بأس بأن يأخذ شعر الحاجبين وشعر وجهه ما لم يتشبه بالمخنثين، ومثله في الينابيع والمضمرات والمراد ما يكون مشوّهاً لخبر: لعن الله النامصة
In al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya from al-Ghara'ib: Plucking the 'finikayn' is an innovation, and they are the two sides of the chin. In al-Sihah and al-Qamus: 'finik' with fa and nun like 'amir', and the dual 'finikan', and they are the meeting of the two jaws or their two ends at the chin. In the hadith: 'When you perform wudu, do not forget the finikayn,' meaning the two sides of the chin, right and left. Some said: From what precedes, the legitimacy of cleaning inside the nose is taken, and plucking its hair if it becomes long, because harm like mucus hangs on it. Al-Shihab al-Qalyubi narrated in al-Budur al-Munawwara: 'Do not pluck nose hair, for it causes leprosy; but trim it,' and he said it is weak, and it is said it is hasan. And it is narrated that it causes 'aklah' (itch) and its growth is a protection from leprosy. In al-Khulasa from al-Muntaqa: Abu Hanifa did not dislike plucking gray hair except for adornment. It should be understood as a small amount; for a large amount it is disliked because of the hadith in Abu Dawud: 'Do not pluck gray hair, for it is the light of the Muslim on the Day of Resurrection.' In al-Quniyya: Shaving the hair of the head and back is contrary to good manners. In al-Muhit: He should not shave the hair of his throat, and there is no harm in taking hair from the eyebrows and face as long as he does not imitate effeminate men. The same is in al-Yanabi' and al-Mudamarat, and what is meant is what is disfiguring, because of the hadith: 'Allah has cursed the woman who plucks eyebrows.'
Source pages p. 526

Commentary
This section covers various rulings on hair removal. Plucking the 'finikayn' (the two sides of the chin) is considered an innovation. Cleaning inside the nose and trimming nose hair is recommended because it gathers dirt. Plucking nose hair is reported to cause leprosy, but trimming is acceptable. For gray hair, Abu Hanifa permits plucking a little but dislikes a lot because of the hadith that gray hair is light on the Day of Resurrection. Shaving the head and back is against good manners (khilaf al-adab). It is not allowed to shave the throat hair. Taking hair from the eyebrows is permissible unless it is for beautification that imitates effeminate men, and the hadith curses the woman who plucks eyebrows (namisah).

Key Terms
الفنيكان (al-finikan): The two sides of the chin at the junction of the jaws.
النامصة (al-namisah): A woman who plucks eyebrows for beautification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on plucking gray hair in large quantities according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is mustahabb because it removes signs of aging.
B) It is makruh because of the hadith that it is light for the Muslim.
C) It is haram because it changes Allah's creation.
D) It is mubah with no dislike.

Key Takeaway
Gray hair should be left as a light for the believer; excessive plucking is disliked, while other hair removal practices have specific rules based on evidence.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
8 min
Mustache and Beard: The Hanafi Sunnah
Rulings on mustache and beard with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mustache trimming (ihfa') and beard length (qabdah), and identify the exception for mujahidin.

Core Idea
The sunnah for the mustache is close trimming (ihfa'), not shaving; the beard is cut to a fistful for moderation.

This lesson focuses on two fundamental grooming practices: the mustache and the beard. The Hanafi school recommends ihfa' (close trimming) for the mustache, while the beard should be kept to a fistful in length and trimmed in width. An important exception is made for the mujahid, who may let his nails and mustache grow for martial purposes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for mustache trimming
The text states that ihfa' (close trimming) is recommended and better than simply cutting. Full shaving is disliked and considered an innovation by some scholars.
Ihfa' leaves the mustache very short but not completely shaven.
2
Identify the ruling for beard length
The sunnah is to cut what exceeds a fistful (qabdah) from the length, and also to trim the width for moderation. This is based on the practice of Imam Abu Hanifa as narrated by Muhammad al-Shaybani and the action of Umar.
Excessive length can be disfiguring and invite backbiting.
3
Note the exception for the mujahid
Our scholars (mashayikhuna) excepted the mujahid, recommending that he let his nails grow (as weapons) and his mustache (to appear more fearsome to the enemy).
This shows that rulings can adapt to circumstances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم رأى صبياً حلق بعض رأسه وترك بعضه فقال : احلقوه كله أو اتركوه كله؟ وفي الغرائب يستحب حلق الشعر في كل جمعة وفي شرح النقاية عن الإمام يكره أن يحلق قفاه إلا عند الحجامة ،أهـ قال الطحاوي: يستحب إحفاء الشوارب ونراه أفضل من قضاه، وفي شرح شرعة الإسلام قال الإمام : الإحفاء قريب من الحلق وأما الحلق فلم يرد، بل كرهه بعض العلماء ورآه بدعة اهـ وفي الخانية وينبغي أن يأخذ من شاربه حتى يوازي الطرف الأعلى من الشفة العليا، ويصير مثل الحاجب .اهـ. وعن الشعبي كان يقص شاربه حتى يظهر طرف الشفة العليا، وما قاربه من أعلاه، ويأخذ ما شد مما فوق ذلك وينزع ما قارب الشفة من جانبي الفم ولا يزيد على ذلك اهـ قال في فتح الباري: وهذا أعدل ما وقفت عليه من الآثار، ويشرع قص مع الشارب لأنهما منه كما استظهره في فتح الباري، واستثنى مشايخنا المجاهد فقالوا : تندب له توفير أظفاره لأنها سلاح، وشاربه لأنه أهيب في عين العدو وأما اللحية فذكر محمد في الآثار عن الإمام أن السنة أن يقطع ما زاد على قبضة يده قال : نأخذ كذا . وبه في محيط السرخسي، وكذا يأخذ من عرضها ماطال وخرج عن السمت التقرب من التدوير من جميع الجوانب لأن الإعدال محبوب والطول المفرط قد يشوه الخلقة ويطلق ألسنة المغتابين وأخرج الطبراني عن عمر أنه أخذ من لحية رجل ما زاد على القبضة، ثم قال له: يترك أحدكم نفسه حتى يكون كأنه سبع من السباع، وفي الفتاوى الهندية عن الغرائب : نتف الفنيكين بدعة وهما جانبا العنفقة ،أهـ قال في الصحاح والقاموس الفنيك بالفاء والنون كامير والمثنى فنيكان، وهما مجمع اللحيين أو طرفاهما عند العنفقة وفي الحديث : إذا توضأت، فلا تنس الفنيكين يعني جانبي العنفقة عن يمين وشمال قال بعض ويؤخذ مما تقدم مشروعية تنظيف داخل الأنف، وأخذ شعره إذا طال لأن الأذى كالمخاط يعلق به اهـ وروى الشهاب القليوبي في كتاب البدور المنوّرة في معرفة رتبة الأحاديث المشتهرة: لا تنتفوا شعر الأنف، فأنه يورث الجذام، أنه ولكن قصوه قصاً :وقال ضعيف، وقيل حسن، وروي يورث الأكلة وهي بتثليث (1) الهمزة الحكة ونباته أمان من الجذام وفي الخلاصة عن المنتقى كان أبو حنيفة لا يكره نتف الشيب إلا على وجه التزين اهـ وينبغي حمله على القليل أما الكثير فيكره لخبر أبي داود: لا تنتفوا الشيب، فإنه نور المسلم يوم القيامة، وفي القنية : حلق شعر الرأس والظهر خلاف الأدب : وفي المحيط : لا يحلق شعر حلقه، ولا بأس بأن يأخذ شعر الحاجبين وشعر وجهه ما لم يتشبه بالمخنثين، ومثله في الينابيع والمضمرات والمراد ما يكون مشوّهاً لخبر: لعن الله النامصة، والمتنمصة والسنة في حلق العانة أن يكون بالموسى لأنه يقوّي وأصل السنة يتأدى بكل مزيل لحصول المقصود، وهو النظافة، وإنما جاء الحديث بلفظ الحلق لأنه الأغلب، وسواء في ذلك الرجل والمرأة، وقال النووي: الأولى في حقه الحلق، وفي حقها النتف والإبط أولى فيه النتف لورود الخير ولأن الحلق يغلظ الشعر، ويزيد الرائحة الكريهة بخلاف النتف، ثم العانة هي الشعر الذي فوق الذكر وحواليه، وحوالي فرجها ويستحب إزالة شعر الدبر خوفاً من أن يعلق به شيء من النجاسة الخارجة ، فلا يتمكن من إزالته بالاستجمار وفي الخانية : ينبغي أن يدفن قلامة ظفره ومحلوق شعره، وإن رماه فلا بأس وكره القاؤه في كنيف، أو مغتسل لأن ذلك وروي أن النبي أمر بدفن الشعر والظفر، وقال : لا تتغلب به سحرة بني آدم اهـ، ولأنهما من أجزاء الآدمي فتحترم وروى الترمذي عن عائشة رضي الله عنها كان صلى الله عليه وسلم أمر بدفن سبعة أشياء من الإنسان، الشعر والظفر والحيضة والسن والقلفة والمسحة اهـ، والحيضة بكسر الحاء المهملة خرقة الحيض، والجمع محايض كذا في الصحاح ولعل المسحة الخرقة التي يمسح بها ما خرج من الإنسان من نحو دم وأستغفر الله العظيم والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم .
The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) saw a boy who had shaved part of his head and left part, and he said: 'Shave it all or leave it all.' In al-Ghara'ib: It is recommended to shave the hair every Friday. In Sharh al-Niqayah from Imam [Abu Hanifa]: It is disliked to shave the nape of the neck except for cupping. End. Al-Tahtawi said: It is recommended to trim the mustache closely (ihfa'), and we consider it better than cutting it. In Sharh Shari'ah al-Islam: The Imam said: Ihfa' is close to shaving, but shaving [the mustache] is not reported; rather, some scholars disliked it and considered it an innovation. End. In al-Khaniyah: It is proper that one takes from his mustache until it aligns with the upper edge of the upper lip, becoming like an eyebrow. End. From al-Sha'bi: He used to trim his mustache until the edge of the upper lip appeared, and what was near it from above, and he took what grew beyond that, and removed what was near the lip from the sides of the mouth, and did not exceed that. End. Al-Hafiz ibn Hajar said in Fath al-Bari: This is the most balanced of what I have come across from the traditions. It is prescribed to cut the mustache, as it is part of the mustache, as he inferred in Fath al-Bari. Our scholars excepted the mujahid: they said it is recommended for him to let his nails grow because they are weapons, and his mustache because it is more awe-inspiring in the enemy's eye. As for the beard, Muhammad [al-Shaybani] mentioned in al-Athar from the Imam [Abu Hanifa] that the sunnah is to cut what exceeds a fistful. He said: We take this view. And it is also in Muhit al-Sarakhsi. Similarly, one takes from its width what is long and goes beyond the norm, approaching rounding from all sides because moderation is beloved, and excessive length may disfigure one's appearance and provoke the tongues of backbiters. Al-Tabarani narrated from 'Umar that he took from a man's beard what exceeded the fistful, then said to him: 'Do you leave yourself until you become like a wild beast?' In al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya from al-Ghara'ib: Plucking the fanikayn (the two sides of the goatee) is an innovation; they are the two sides of the 'unfuqah (the beard on the chin). End. He said in al-Sihah and al-Qamus: Al-Fanik (with f and n) like amir, dual fanikan, and they are the meeting of the two jaws or their two ends at the 'unfuqah. In the hadith: 'When you perform wudu, do not forget the fanikayn,' meaning the sides of the 'unfuqah on the right and left. Some said: From the above, the legality of cleaning the inside of the nose and removing its hair if it becomes long is derived, because harm like mucus clings to it. End. Al-Shihab al-Qalyubi narrated in al-Budur al-Munawwirah: 'Do not pluck the hair of the nose, for it causes leprosy; rather, cut it short.' He said it is weak, and some said it is hasan. It is also narrated that it causes akla (which has three pronunciations for the hamzah) meaning itching, and its growth is a protection from leprosy. In al-Khulasah from al-Muntaqa: Abu Hanifa did not dislike plucking gray hair except if done for adornment. End. It should be understood as applying to a small amount; as for much, it is disliked due to the hadith of Abu Dawud: 'Do not pluck gray hair, for it is the light of the Muslim on the Day of Resurrection.' In al-Qunyah: Shaving the head and back is contrary to proper conduct. In al-Muhit: One should not shave the hair of his throat. There is no harm in taking from the eyebrows and facial hair as long as it does not imitate effeminate men. Similar is in al-Yanabi' and al-Mudmarat. What is intended is what is disfiguring, due to the hadith: 'Allah curses the namisah and the mutanammisah.' The sunnah in shaving the pubic area is to use a razor because it strengthens; essentially, the sunnah is fulfilled by any remover that achieves the purpose, which is cleanliness. The hadith mentions shaving because it is most common. This applies equally to men and women. Al-Nawawi said: For a man, shaving is preferable; for a woman, plucking. For the armpit, plucking is preferable because of the reported good, and because shaving thickens the hair and increases unpleasant odor, unlike plucking. The pubic area is the hair above and around the penis and around the female genitals. Removing the hair of the anus is recommended out of fear that something of the exiting impurity may cling to it, making it impossible to remove via istijmar. In al-Khaniyah: It is proper to bury his nail parings and shaved hair; if he throws them away, there is no harm, but it is disliked to throw them into a toilet or bathhouse because of that. It is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded burying hair and nails, saying: 'Lest the sorcerers of the children of Adam overcome you with it.' End. Also because they are parts of a human, so they are respected. Al-Tirmidhi narrated from 'Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded burying seven things from a human: hair, nail, menstrual rag, tooth, foreskin, and the piece of cloth used for wiping. End. Al-haydah (with broken ha) is the menstrual rag, plural mahayid, as in al-Sihah. Perhaps al-mashah is the cloth with which one wipes what comes out of a human like blood. I seek forgiveness from Allah the Great, and Allah (Exalted is He) knows best.
Source pages p. 526

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi compiles various grooming rulings drawn from the Hanafi school. The author begins with a hadith about a boy with partially shaved hair, establishing the principle of uniformity in hair removal. He then discusses the mustache, noting that the recommended practice (sunnah) is ihfa' (close trimming), not full shaving, which some scholars disliked. For the beard, the Hanafi position (from Imam Muhammad in al-Athar) is to cut what exceeds a fistful in length, and also to trim excessive width for moderation. Mujahidin are excepted to leave beard and nails for martial purposes. Plucking the fanikayn (sides of the goatee) is deemed an innovation (bid'ah). Cleaning inside the nose and trimming nose hair is recommended. Plucking gray hair is not disliked if little, but if much it is disliked due to the hadith. Shaving the head and back is against proper adab. Plucking eyebrows is cursed (for women). For pubic hair, the sunnah is shaving with a razor for men, plucking for women; for armpits plucking is better. Finally, nail parings and hair should be buried or disposed respectfully, avoiding toilets or bathhouses, as these are human parts. The passage thus provides a comprehensive overview of Hanafi grooming etiquettes.

Key Terms
الإحفاء (al-ihfa'): Close trimming of the mustache, almost to the root but not complete shaving.
القبضة (al-qabdah): A fistful; the measure of a closed fist used to determine the proper length of the beard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the sunnah for the mustache in the Hanafi school?
A) Shave it completely.
B) Trim it closely (ihfa').
C) Leave it natural and untrimmed.
D) Pluck it all out.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends close trimming (ihfa') for the mustache and cutting the beard to a fistful, with an exception for mujahidin.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
Plucking and Shaving: Bid'ah, Disliked Acts, and Curses
Rulings on plucking and shaving with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which plucking acts are considered bid'ah, which are disliked, and which are cursed, according to Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Plucking the sides of the goatee (fanikayn) is bid'ah; plucking gray hair is disliked if much; plucking eyebrows for beautification is cursed.

This lesson covers rulings on plucking and shaving that go beyond the basic sunnah. The text identifies plucking the fanikayn (sides of the goatee) as an innovation, discusses the disliked nature of plucking gray hair in large amounts, and emphasizes the curse on those who pluck eyebrows for beautification (namisah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on fanikayn
The text states that plucking the fanikayn (sides of the goatee) is an innovation (bid'ah).
Fanikayn are the sides of the 'unfuqah (beard on the chin).
2
Identify the ruling on gray hair
Abu Hanifa did not dislike plucking gray hair unless done for adornment. However, plucking a large amount is disliked due to the hadith: 'Do not pluck gray hair, for it is the light of the Muslim.'
Small amounts for cleanliness are permissible.
3
Identify the ruling on eyebrows (namisah)
The namisah (woman who plucks eyebrows for others) and the mutanammisah (one who has it done) are cursed. This indicates the act is haram.
The context is beautification, not medical necessity.
4
Note other disliked shaving acts
Shaving the head, back, and throat is considered contrary to adab (proper conduct) unless for a valid reason like cupping.
Exceptions exist for medical or martial needs.

Source Text

وفي الفتاوى الهندية عن الغرائب : نتف الفنيكين بدعة وهما جانبا العنفقة ،أهـ قال في الصحاح والقاموس الفنيك بالفاء والنون كامير والمثنى فنيكان، وهما مجمع اللحيين أو طرفاهما عند العنفقة وفي الحديث : إذا توضأت، فلا تنس الفنيكين يعني جانبي العنفقة عن يمين وشمال قال بعض ويؤخذ مما تقدم مشروعية تنظيف داخل الأنف، وأخذ شعره إذا طال لأن الأذى كالمخاط يعلق به اهـ وروى الشهاب القليوبي في كتاب البدور المنوّرة في معرفة رتبة الأحاديث المشتهرة: لا تنتفوا شعر الأنف، فأنه يورث الجذام، أنه ولكن قصوه قصاً :وقال ضعيف، وقيل حسن، وروي يورث الأكلة وهي بتثليث (1) الهمزة الحكة ونباته أمان من الجذام وفي الخلاصة عن في حلق العانة أن يكون بالموسى لأنه يقوّي وأصل السنة يتأدى بكل مزيل لحصول المقصود، وهو النظافة، وإنما جاء الحديث بلفظ الحلق لأنه الأغلب، وسواء في ذلك الرجل والمرأة، وقال النووي: الأولى في حقه الحلق، وفي حقها النتف والإبط أولى فيه النتف لورود الخير ولأن الحلق يغلظ الشعر، ويزيد الرائحة الكريهة بخلاف النتف، ثم العانة هي الشعر الذي فوق الذكر وحواليه، وحوالي فرجها ويستحب إزالة شعر الدبر خوفاً من أن يعلق به شيء من النجاسة الخارجة ، فلا يتمكن من إزالته بالاستجمار وفي الخانية : ينبغي أن يدفن قلامة ظفره ومحلوق شعره، وإن رماه فلا بأس وكره القاؤه في كنيف، أو مغتسل لأن ذلك وروي أن النبي أمر بدفن الشعر والظفر، وقال : لا تتغلب به سحرة بني آدم اهـ، ولأنهما من أجزاء الآدمي فتحترم وروى الترمذي عن عائشة رضي الله عنها كان صلى الله عليه وسلم أمر بدفن سبعة أشياء من الإنسان، الشعر والظفر والحيضة والسن والقلفة والمسحة اهـ، والحيضة بكسر الحاء المهملة خرقة الحيض، والجمع محايض كذا في الصحاح ولعل المسحة الخرقة التي يمسح بها ما خرج من الإنسان من نحو دم وأستغفر الله العظيم والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم .
The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) saw a boy who had shaved part of his head and left part, and he said: 'Shave it all or leave it all.' In al-Ghara'ib: It is recommended to shave the hair every Friday. In Sharh al-Niqayah from Imam [Abu Hanifa]: It is disliked to shave the nape of the neck except for cupping. End. Al-Tahtawi said: It is recommended to trim the mustache closely (ihfa'), and we consider it better than cutting it. In Sharh Shari'ah al-Islam: The Imam said: Ihfa' is close to shaving, but shaving [the mustache] is not reported; rather, some scholars disliked it and considered it an innovation. End. In al-Khaniyah: It is proper that one takes from his mustache until it aligns with the upper edge of the upper lip, becoming like an eyebrow. End. From al-Sha'bi: He used to trim his mustache until the edge of the upper lip appeared, and what was near it from above, and he took what grew beyond that, and removed what was near the lip from the sides of the mouth, and did not exceed that. End. Al-Hafiz ibn Hajar said in Fath al-Bari: This is the most balanced of what I have come across from the traditions. It is prescribed to cut the mustache, as it is part of the mustache, as he inferred in Fath al-Bari. Our scholars excepted the mujahid: they said it is recommended for him to let his nails grow because they are weapons, and his mustache because it is more awe-inspiring in the enemy's eye. As for the beard, Muhammad [al-Shaybani] mentioned in al-Athar from the Imam [Abu Hanifa] that the sunnah is to cut what exceeds a fistful. He said: We take this view. And it is also in Muhit al-Sarakhsi. Similarly, one takes from its width what is long and goes beyond the norm, approaching rounding from all sides because moderation is beloved, and excessive length may disfigure one's appearance and provoke the tongues of backbiters. Al-Tabarani narrated from 'Umar that he took from a man's beard what exceeded the fistful, then said to him: 'Do you leave yourself until you become like a wild beast?' In al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya from al-Ghara'ib: Plucking the fanikayn (the two sides of the goatee) is an innovation; they are the two sides of the 'unfuqah (the beard on the chin). End. He said in al-Sihah and al-Qamus: Al-Fanik (with f and n) like amir, dual fanikan, and they are the meeting of the two jaws or their two ends at the 'unfuqah. In the hadith: 'When you perform wudu, do not forget the fanikayn,' meaning the sides of the 'unfuqah on the right and left. Some said: From the above, the legality of cleaning the inside of the nose and removing its hair if it becomes long is derived, because harm like mucus clings to it. End. Al-Shihab al-Qalyubi narrated in al-Budur al-Munawwirah: 'Do not pluck the hair of the nose, for it causes leprosy; rather, cut it short.' He said it is weak, and some said it is hasan. It is also narrated that it causes akla (which has three pronunciations for the hamzah) meaning itching, and its growth is a protection from leprosy. In al-Khulasah from al-Muntaqa: Abu Hanifa did not dislike plucking gray hair except if done for adornment. End. It should be understood as applying to a small amount; as for much, it is disliked due to the hadith of Abu Dawud: 'Do not pluck gray hair, for it is the light of the Muslim on the Day of Resurrection.' In al-Qunyah: Shaving the head and back is contrary to proper conduct. In al-Muhit: One should not shave the hair of his throat. There is no harm in taking from the eyebrows and facial hair as long as it does not imitate effeminate men. Similar is in al-Yanabi' and al-Mudmarat. What is intended is what is disfiguring, due to the hadith: 'Allah curses the namisah and the mutanammisah.' The sunnah in shaving the pubic area is to use a razor because it strengthens; essentially, the sunnah is fulfilled by any remover that achieves the purpose, which is cleanliness. The hadith mentions shaving because it is most common. This applies equally to men and women. Al-Nawawi said: For a man, shaving is preferable; for a woman, plucking. For the armpit, plucking is preferable because of the reported good, and because shaving thickens the hair and increases unpleasant odor, unlike plucking. The pubic area is the hair above and around the penis and around the female genitals. Removing the hair of the anus is recommended out of fear that something of the exiting impurity may cling to it, making it impossible to remove via istijmar. In al-Khaniyah: It is proper to bury his nail parings and shaved hair; if he throws them away, there is no harm, but it is disliked to throw them into a toilet or bathhouse because of that. It is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded burying hair and nails, saying: 'Lest the sorcerers of the children of Adam overcome you with it.' End. Also because they are parts of a human, so they are respected. Al-Tirmidhi narrated from 'Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded burying seven things from a human: hair, nail, menstrual rag, tooth, foreskin, and the piece of cloth used for wiping. End. Al-haydah (with broken ha) is the menstrual rag, plural mahayid, as in al-Sihah. Perhaps al-mashah is the cloth with which one wipes what comes out of a human like blood. I seek forgiveness from Allah the Great, and Allah (Exalted is He) knows best.
Source pages p. 526

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi compiles various grooming rulings drawn from the Hanafi school. The author begins with a hadith about a boy with partially shaved hair, establishing the principle of uniformity in hair removal. He then discusses the mustache, noting that the recommended practice (sunnah) is ihfa' (close trimming), not full shaving, which some scholars disliked. For the beard, the Hanafi position (from Imam Muhammad in al-Athar) is to cut what exceeds a fistful in length, and also to trim excessive width for moderation. Mujahidin are excepted to leave beard and nails for martial purposes. Plucking the fanikayn (sides of the goatee) is deemed an innovation (bid'ah). Cleaning inside the nose and trimming nose hair is recommended. Plucking gray hair is not disliked if little, but if much it is disliked due to the hadith. Shaving the head and back is against proper adab. Plucking eyebrows is cursed (for women). For pubic hair, the sunnah is shaving with a razor for men, plucking for women; for armpits plucking is better. Finally, nail parings and hair should be buried or disposed respectfully, avoiding toilets or bathhouses, as these are human parts. The passage thus provides a comprehensive overview of Hanafi grooming etiquettes.

Key Terms
الفنيكين (al-fanikayn): The two sides of the goatee (the beard on the chin) at the meeting of the jaws.
النمامصة (al-namisah): A woman who plucks eyebrows (or facial hair) for others; al-mutanammisah is one who has it done.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on plucking the sides of the goatee (fanikayn) according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is sunnah.
B) It is permissible.
C) It is bid'ah (innovation).
D) It is wajib.

Key Takeaway
Plucking the fanikayn is bid'ah, plucking gray hair in excess is disliked, and plucking eyebrows for beautification is haram.

Sunan al-Fitrah: Grooming and Disposal of Clippings
Expansion on sunan al-fitrah rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on removing pubic and armpit hair and explain the recommendation to bury nail clippings and shaved hair, citing the relevant hadith.

Core Idea
The sunnah of removing pubic hair is fulfilled by any means; burying clippings honors human parts and protects from sorcery.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi expands on the sunan al-fitrah – the innate practices recommended by the Prophet ﷺ. It clarifies the preferred methods for removing pubic and armpit hair, notes gender-based differences, and addresses the proper disposal of nail clippings and hair. The text relies on hadith evidence to establish the rulings, emphasizing respect for human body parts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
Note that shaving pubic hair is sunnah, and removing armpit hair is also sunnah. The text also recommends removing anal hair as a precaution.
The sunnah level is muakkadah for both acts.
2
Compare methods of removal
For pubic hair, any remover suffices but a razor is preferred. For armpit hair, plucking is more virtuous than shaving due to narrations and to avoid thickening hair and odor.
Women are advised to pluck pubic hair according to al-Nawawi, but the general Hanafi view allows shaving.
3
Understand the ruling on anal hair
Removing anal hair is recommended (mustahabb) to prevent impurity from clinging, which could invalidate istijmar.
This is a practical hygiene recommendation.
4
Apply the ruling on burying clippings
Burying nail clippings and shaved hair is sunnah. It is disliked (makruh tanzih) to throw them into latrines or bathhouses based on a Prophetic order to bury seven things from a human.
The hadith teaches respect for human parts and protection from sorcery.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (hashiya) discussing sunan al-fitrah (innate practices). The author explains that shaving pubic hair is sunnah and can be done by any means, though using a razor is preferable. For women, plucking is better. Armpit hair should be plucked to avoid thickening and odor. Removing anal hair is recommended to prevent impurity.
