Eclipse Prayer: Definition, Wisdom, and Proof
Defines kusuf/khusuf and explains the hadith on eclipses as signs of Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of kusuf and khusuf, explain the prophetic hadith on eclipses as signs, and identify the ruling of eclipse prayer as sunnah muakkadah with its proof.

Core Idea
Eclipses are natural signs of Allah, not omens; the Prophet commanded prayer like the most recent fard.

Eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf) is a sunnah muakkadah performed in congregation without adhan or iqamah. This lesson explores its linguistic definition, the wisdom behind it, and the primary hadith evidence that refutes pre-Islamic superstitions and establishes the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Understand the linguistic definitions
Examine how the text defines kusuf and khusuf, noting the synonymity and the optional distinction between partial and total.
The text quotes Ibn Faris, al-Azhari, al-Jawhari, and al-Qamus.
2
Locate the ruling and its classification
The passage states that eclipse prayer is sunnah according to the majority (جمهور), though some said wajib. Focus on the mufta bihi: sunnah muakkadah.
The ruling is placed between Eid (wajib) and rain prayer (sunnah disputed).
3
Analyze the hadith (dalil)
Identify the key phrases: the Prophet refutes causation by death, declares them signs of Allah, and commands prayer like the most recent obligatory prayer (subh).
The command 'فصلوا' is used to derive sunnah, not wujub, because it is compared to a fard but not declared fard itself.
4
Extract the fiqh and wisdom
Notice that the hadith teaches that eclipses are natural (earth's shadow) but divinely appointed signs to turn to Allah. The text generalizes this to other fearful signs like earthquakes.
Quran 17:59 is cited: 'We do not send signs except as a warning.'
5
Identify the school's position on related issues
Observe that the Hanafi school holds eclipse prayer as sunnah with one ruku per rak'ah, unlike Shafi'i's two ruku. The passage does not detail the form, but the ruling is clear.
The ikhtilaf on wajib vs sunnah is mentioned; the relied-upon is sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة الكسوف
ذكر هذا الباب بعد صلاة العيد وقبل الاستسقاء لأن كلاً منهما صلاة نهارية بجماعة أذان ولا إقامة إلا أنّ صلاة العيد واجبة وقيل فرض كفاية، وصلاة الكسوف سنة عند الجمهور وقيل واجبة وصلاة الاستسقاء مختلف في سنيتها، فناسب ترتيب الأبواب كذا في الفتح. يقال: كسف الله الشمس كسفاً من باب ضرب، فهو معتد، وكسفت الشمس كسوفاً من باب جلس فهو لازم، وما قيل في الكسوف يقال في الخسوف، وهما بمعنى واحد وهو ذهاب الضوء من كل منهما قاله ابن فارس والأزهري، والجوهري وزاد في القاموس الخسوف ذهاب بعضهما والكسوف ذهاب كلهما. والإضافة في صلاة الكسوف للتعريف وهي من إضافة الشيء إلى سببه لأن سببها الكسوف. روى الكمال أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: إن أناساً يزعمون أن الشمس والقمر لا ينكسفان إلا لموت عظيم من العظماء، وليس كذلك إن الشمس والقمر لا ينكسفان لموت أحد ولا لحياته، ولكنهما آيتان من آيات الله إن الله إذا بدا لشيء من خلفه خشع له فإذا رأيتم ذلك فصلوا كأحدث صلاة صليتموها من المكتوبة. والمراد بالأحدث الأقرب، وكانت الصبح فإن الكسوف كان عند ارتفاعها قدر رمحين. والفقه في الحديث أن أهل الجاهلية كانوا يزعمون أن ذلك يوجب حدوث تغير في العالم كما يعتقده أهل النجوم من أن هذه الأجسام السفلية مرتبطة بالنجوم، وأن لها تأثيراً في ذلك، وأن العالم كزي الشكل، والكسوف حيلولة الأرض بين الشمس وبين الأبصار، فهو أمر عادي لا يتقدم ولا يتأخر فأخبرهم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أن اعتقادهم هذا باطل، وأن الشمس والقمر آيتان من آيات الله تعالى يريهما عباده ليعلموا أنهما مسخران بأمره ليس لهما سلطان في غيرهما، ولا قوة دفع عن أنفسهما، فلا يستحقان أن يعبدا وأن هذا من أثر الإرادة القديمة وفعل الفاعل المختار فيخلق النور والظلمة في هذين الجرمين متى شاء بلا سبب، وفي الفزع إلى الصلاة والسجود لله تعالى والتضرع إليه عند ذلك تحقيق إضافة الحوادث كلها إليه تعالى ونفي لها عما سواه. وفي هذا دليل أيضاً على أن الصلاة مستحبة عند حدوث كل آية من الآيات كالزلزلة والريح الشديدة والظلمة ونحوها كما في غاية البيان. وقال تعالى: (وما نرسل بالآيات إلا تخويفا) [الإسراء: 59]. والتخويف بهما لما فيهما من تبديل نعمة النور بظلمة لا سيما الكسوف فتفزع القلوب لذلك طبعاً، فكانا من الآيات المخوفة، والله تعالى يخوف عباده ليتركوا المعاصي ويرجعوا إليه بالطاعة والاستغفار.
Chapter on Eclipse Prayer. This chapter is placed after the Eid prayer and before the prayer for rain because each is a daytime prayer with congregation, without adhan or iqamah, except that Eid prayer is obligatory (wajib), and it is said a communal obligation, and eclipse prayer is sunnah according to the majority, and it is said to be obligatory, and the prayer for rain is differed upon regarding its sunnah status, so the arrangement of chapters is appropriate. It is said: kasafa (he caused eclipse) from the verb form of ضرب, transitive, and kusuf (eclipse) from the verb form of جلس, intransitive. What is said about kusuf is said about khusuf, and they are synonymous meaning the removal of light from both, according to Ibn Faris, al-Azhari, and al-Jawhari. Al-Qamus adds: khusuf is the removal of part, and kusuf is the removal of all. The idafah in 'salat al-kusuf' is for definition, and it is the attribution of a thing to its cause because its cause is the eclipse. Al-Kamal narrated that the Prophet (ﷺ) said: Some people claim that the sun and moon do not eclipse except for the death of a great person, but it is not so; they do not eclipse for anyone's death or life, but they are two signs from the signs of Allah. When Allah manifests to something of His creation, it humbles itself before Him. So when you see that, pray like the most recent obligatory prayer you performed. The intended meaning of 'most recent' is the closest, and it was the dawn prayer because the eclipse occurred when it had risen two spear-lengths. The fiqh in the hadith is that the people of ignorance used to claim that this causes change in the world, as astrologers believe that these lower bodies are linked to the stars and have an effect on them, and that the world is like a form. The eclipse is the earth's interposition between the sun and sight, so it is a normal event that does not precede or lag. So the Prophet informed them that this belief is false, and that the sun and moon are two signs from Allah by which He shows His servants to teach them that they are subjugated by His command, have no authority over others, and have no power to defend themselves, so they do not deserve to be worshipped. And that this is from the effect of the eternal will and the act of the free Agent, who creates light and darkness in these two bodies whenever He wills without cause. And running to prayer, prostration to Allah, and supplication to Him at that time is a confirmation of attributing all events to Him and denying them from others. This also indicates that prayer is recommended at every sign, such as earthquake, severe wind, darkness, and the like, as in Ghayat al-Bayan. And Allah said: 'And We do not send signs except as a warning' [al-Isra: 59]. And the warning by them is due to the exchange of the blessing of light with darkness, especially the eclipse, so hearts become alarmed naturally. Thus they are among the fearful signs, and Allah warns His servants to abandon sins and return to Him in obedience and seeking forgiveness.
Source pages p. 543

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the chapter of eclipse prayer. It begins by explaining the placement of the chapter between Eid and rain prayer, noting that all three are daytime prayers with congregation and no adhan. It then defines the terms kusuf and khusuf, clarifying that they refer to the removal of light, with some lexicographers distinguishing between partial (khusuf) and total (kusuf). The key proof is the hadith narrated by al-Kamal, where the Prophet refutes the pre-Islamic belief that eclipses are caused by the death of great people, instead affirming they are signs of Allah's power. The commentary highlights the wisdom: the natural cause (earth's shadow) is ordinary, but the spiritual lesson is to turn to Allah in prayer. It also generalizes the ruling to any fearful natural event, citing the Quranic verse that signs are sent for warning.

Key Terms
الكسوف (al-kusuf): The obscuration of the sun's light, either partial or total, as a sign from Allah.
الخسوف (al-khusuf): The obscuration of the moon's light; used interchangeably with kusuf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A specific eclipse prayer with two ruku' per rak'ah
B) The most recent obligatory prayer performed
C) Two rak'ahs like nafl without additional ruku'
D) Four rak'ahs with two ruku' each

Key Takeaway
Eclipses are natural signs of Allah, not omens of death; the sunnah is to pray two rak'ahs in congregation like the subh prayer.

Eclipse Prayer: One Ruku per Rak'ah (Hanafi View)
States the Hanafi position on the number of rak'ahs and ruku' in eclipse prayer, with inter-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the number of ruku in eclipse prayer and evaluate the opposing school's evidence.

Core Idea
Eclipse prayer: one ruku per rak'ah, like all prayers; two ruku is a misunderstanding.

The form of eclipse prayer is a well-known point of disagreement between the Hanafi school and the other three major schools. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling that the prayer consists of two rak'ahs with only one ruku each, akin to the nafl prayer. We then explore the evidence cited by the opposing schools and the Hanafi response, which relies on stronger hadiths and consistency with the general principles of salah.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Clearly articulate what the Hanafi school holds regarding the number of rak'ahs and ruku in eclipse prayer. Use the source text to identify the ruling.
The source states: 'so he does not perform two ruku in each rak'ah'.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Name the schools that disagree and state their position on the number of ruku. The source mentions Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad.
They hold two ruku per rak'ah.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the hadith cited by the opponents: the report of Ibn Abbas and Aisha that the Prophet performed two ruku. Understand why this evidence is considered strong by them.
It is narrated in Bukhari and Muslim (muttafaq alayh).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal: more hadiths support one ruku, the report of two ruku is interpreted as a misunderstanding due to prolonged ruku, and qiyas with all other prayers demands one ruku.
Al-Kamal ibn al-Hammam and Imam Muhammad provide the detailed response.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference in how the prayer is performed. This shows the real-world impact of the legal disagreement.
Hanafis perform one ruku per rak'ah; others perform two.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (من غير زيادة) مرتبط بقوله كهيئة النفل أي من غير زيادة ركوع ثان. قوله: (فلا يركع ركوعين في كل ركعة). وقال مالك والشافعي وأحمد في المختار عنده في كل ركعة ركوعان لخبر ابن عباس وعائشة أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ركع ركوعين في كل ركعة متفق عليه، ولنا أدلة كثيرة. قال الكمال بعد ذكرها فهذه الأحاديث منها الصحيح، ومنها الحسن قد دارت على ثلاثة أمور منها ما فيه أنه صلى ركعتين ومنها الأمر بأن يجعلوها كأحدث ما صلوا من المكتوبة وهي الصبح، ومنها ما فصل فأفاد تفصيله أنها بركوع واحد وما ذهبنا إليه رواه كبار الصحابة، فالأخذ به أولى لكثرة رواته، وصحة أحاديثه، وموافقته الأصول المعهودة لانا لم نجد في شيء من الصلوات إلا ركوعاً واحداً فيجب أن تكون صلاة الكسوف كذلك. قال الإمام محمد وتأويل ما روى من الركوعين أنه لما أطال الركوع رفع بعض أنه رفع رأسه من الركوع فرفع من خلفهم، فلما رأوا رسول الله في الصفوف رفعوا رؤوسهم ظناً منه أنهم ركعوا ركوعين.
His statement: (without increase) is connected to his statement 'like nafl', meaning without an increase of a second ruku. His statement: (so he does not perform two ruku in each rak'ah). And Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad in the preferred view according to them held that in each rak'ah there are two ruku, based on the report of Ibn Abbas and Aisha that the Prophet (ﷺ) performed two ruku in each rak'ah, which is agreed upon. And we have many evidences. Al-Kamal said after mentioning them: these hadiths, including sound and good ones, revolve around three matters: one has that he prayed two rak'ahs; another is the command to make it like the most recent obligatory prayer which is the dawn prayer; and another details that it is with one ruku. What we hold is narrated by major companions, so adopting it is more appropriate due to the number of its narrators, the authenticity of its hadiths, and its conformity with established principles, for we have not found in any prayer except one ruku, so the eclipse prayer must be the same. Imam Muhammad said, and the interpretation of what was narrated about two ruku is that when he prolonged the ruku, some people raised their heads from ruku, and those behind them raised their heads, and when they saw the Messenger of Allah in the rows, they raised their heads, thinking that they had performed two ruku.
Source pages p. 544

Commentary
This passage is a classic inter-madhhab dispute over the form of eclipse prayer. The Hanafi school holds that the prayer consists of two rak'ahs like the nafl prayer, with only one ruku in each rak'ah. The opponents (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) say there are two ruku per rak'ah, citing a hadith from Ibn Abbas and Aisha. The Hanafi response, transmitted by al-Kamal ibn al-Hammam and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, argues that the hadiths supporting one ruku are more numerous and authentic, and that the practice of the Prophet in other prayers supports the principle of one ruku per rak'ah. The report of two ruku is interpreted as a misunderstanding by some companions who saw the Prophet prolong the ruku and mistakenly thought he performed two separate ruku. This reasoning relies on qiyas (analogy) with the standard form of prayer.

Key Terms
ركوع (ruku): Bowing in prayer; a pillar (rukn) of salah
كسوف (kusuf): Solar eclipse; the occasion for the sunnah prayer
سنّة مؤكدة (sunnah muakkadah): Emphasized sunnah; act that the Prophet consistently performed and recommended

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis reject the hadith of two ruku in each rak'ah for eclipse prayer?
A) They consider it fabricated
B) They interpret it as a misunderstanding due to prolonged ruku
C) They follow a different hadith that explicitly says one ruku
D) They rely on qiyas with the funeral prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that eclipse prayer follows the standard prayer form: two rak'ahs with one ruku each, supported by stronger hadiths and qiyas.

Prayer at Fearful Events Like Earthquakes
Expands eclipse prayer ruling to fearful natural events.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the types of fearful events that warrant the sunnah prayer and explain that the ruling is analogous to eclipse prayer.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school extends the sunnah prayer of eclipses to all terrifying natural events as signs of Allah's power.

This brief passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi expands the scope of the eclipse prayer to other fearful occurrences. The matn simply says 'or ifza'' and the commentator clarifies with examples: earthquakes, severe winds, and darkness. Understanding this extension shows how the Hanafi school applies qiyas to acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
Recall that the solar and lunar eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf) is sunnah muakkadah in the Hanafi school.
This is the foundation for the extension.
2
Define 'ifza'' (fearful events)
The term 'ifza'' refers to any event that causes widespread fear and awe, reminding of Allah's power.
It is broader than just eclipses.
3
Note the examples given
The commentator lists earthquakes, severe winds, and darkness as concrete instances.
These are signs of Allah's power that disrupt normal life.
4
Understand the qiyas (analogy)
Just as an eclipse is a cosmic sign, these events are also awe-inspiring signs; hence the same ruling applies by analogy.
Qiyas is used because no explicit text exists for each event.
5
Apply the ruling
Therefore, at the occurrence of any such fearful event, it is sunnah to perform two rak'ahs with two bowings in each, like the eclipse prayer.
The prayer is performed individually or in congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وإلا فزاع) كالزلزلة والريح الشديدة والظلمة.
His statement: (or ifza') like earthquake, severe wind, and darkness.
Source pages p. 544

Commentary
This short passage clarifies the scope of the word 'ifza'' (fearful events) in the matn. It specifies that the ruling of eclipse prayer applies analogously to other terrifying natural phenomena such as earthquakes, severe winds, and darkness. The Hanafi school includes these under the sunnah of prayer at times of fear, as they are also signs of Allah's power. The proof is drawn from the earlier hadith and Quranic verse about sending signs as warnings.

Key Terms
الإفزاع (al-ifza'): Fearful events such as earthquakes, severe winds, and darkness that cause alarm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Earthquakes, severe winds, and darkness
B) Only earthquakes
C) Only solar and lunar eclipses
D) Any natural disaster like floods

Key Takeaway
The sunnah prayer for eclipses extends to all terrifying natural events like earthquakes, severe winds, and darkness.

Talqin: Deathbed Prompting and Post-Burial Recommendation
Critical refinement on talqin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on talqin at death and after burial, explain the evidence, and address the objection regarding the dead's ability to hear.

Core Idea
Talqin is mustahabb at death and after burial; the deceased hears at the time of questioning.

This passage from Al-Tahtawi's Hashiya refines the discussion on talqin (prompting the dying and deceased). While the practice is well-known, a key objection arises from the Quranic verse that the dead cannot hear. Al-Tahtawi reconciles the evidence, explaining that hearing occurs during the questioning in the grave, making talqin after burial beneficial. The lesson will guide you through the Hanafi position, the proofs, and the response to objections.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (talqin at death and after burial) and what the hukm level is (mustahabb).
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the primary evidence: the hadith from Muslim that no Muslim says the shahada at death except Allah saves him from the Fire, and the practice of the companions after burial.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the imperative in the hadith indicates recommendation (istihbab) after assuming abrogation of obligation, and how the practice of the companions supports talqin after burial.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the opposing view: some schools object using Quran 35:22 that the dead cannot hear. State the Hanafi response: the verse refers to general hearing, not the hearing at the time of questioning.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Conclude that later Hanafi authorities like al-Tahtawi prefer talqin after burial, and the mufta bihi is mustahabb.

في السنة ويقول مغمضه باسم الله وعلى ملة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم (اللهم يسر عليه أمره وسهل عليه ما بعده وأسعده بلقائك واجعل ما خرج إليه خيراً مما خرج عنه) قاله الكمال ثم يسجى
Upon them what is in Muslim that the deceased hears the footsteps of their sandals when they depart. Its completion is in Fath al-Qadir. I said: It is possible to combine, so he is prompted at the time of agony due to the explicit statement: 'For no Muslim says it at the time of death except that Allah saves him from the Fire', and acting upon the reality of 'your dead' to confirm him for the questioning in the grave due to what Sa'id ibn Mansur, Samura ibn, and Hakam ibn 'Umayr narrated: They said: When the grave of the deceased is leveled and the people depart, they used to recommend that it be said to the deceased at his grave: 'O so-and-so, say La ilaha illa Allah three times, O so-and-so, say My Lord is Allah, my religion is Islam, and my prophet is Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. O Allah, I seek intercession through Your beloved chosen one that You have mercy on my neediness at death, my beloved, my religion upon Islam and faith, and that You intercede for us with Your prophet, upon him the best of prayers and peace.' (And it is recommended for the relatives of the dying person) and his friends and neighbors to enter upon him to fulfill his right, remind him, give him drink, and give him water because ... upon the narrator, and Allah says: 'And you cannot make hear those in the graves' meaning He did not say it. His statement: (And sometimes that the hearing of the disbelievers is a miracle specific to him and an increase of grief for the disbelievers, or that that was at the time of questioning, for they are alive and hear, and matters of the afterlife are not limited, for it has been reported that the souls of the blessed overlook their graves. They said: Most of that occurs on Friday night and its day and Saturday night until sunrise. It was said: When they are at their graves, they hear those who greet them, and if they were permitted they would return the greeting. His statement: (And sometimes it is metaphorical) meaning it likens his situation and the situation of the people of the well to the situation of the people of Paradise at the time of their settlement there, and the people of Hell when the people of Paradise call out to the people of Hell saying: 'We have found what our Lord promised us to be true, so have you found...' and in it there is that it does not match the end of the hadith. His statement: (And it is problematic for them) i.e., for those who respond with these answers. His statement: (And its completion is in Fath al-Qadir) What is obtained from it is that by the first placement in the grave it is a prelude to the questioning, combining between it and the two verses, and also hearing necessitates life, which is absent, and it only comes at the time of questioning. And its completion is in the commentary. His statement: (It is possible to combine) i.e., between the prompting at the time of death and prompting after death. His statement: (And acting upon the reality of 'your dead') the appropriate addition is 'and he is prompted after placement in the grave' etc. His statement: (O Allah, I seek intercession through You...) Al-Kamal said: The weak servant, author of these words, entrusts his matter to the Rich Generous Lord, relying on Him, asking from Him, exalted is His greatness, to have mercy on my great neediness at death upon faith and certainty. And whoever relies on Allah, He is sufficient for him. There is no might nor power except with Allah, the Most High, the Great. This is his wording, and I say as he said: And upon the Generous Allah is my reliance in every state, as in the commentary, and I also say as he said: For He is hoped for every great matter, and no great sin is forgiven except by the Great Lord. His statement: (Upon death with Islam and faith) is attached to 'have mercy'. Death upon Islam means maintaining one's external deeds until near the agony, and death upon faith means the heart is certain of the truthfulness of the Messenger of Allah in what he knows he brought at the time his soul departs. His statement: (To fulfill his right) and from the right of a Muslim upon a Muslim is to visit him when he is sick and to turn him towards the qibla if possible. His statement: (And remind him) i.e., by prompting him, and by will, and similar, and its coordination with what precedes is coordination of the specific to the general. Thirst overcomes due to the intensity of agony at that time, therefore Satan comes as reported with cool water and says: 'Say there is no god but me so I may give you drink', we seek refuge with Allah from him. And they mention the grace of Allah and His vast generosity and they improve their opinion of Allah due to the report of Muslim: 'Let not any of you die except while he has good opinion of Allah, that He will have mercy on him and forgive him.' And the report of the two Sahihs: Allah says: 'I am as My servant thinks of Me.' (And they recite Surah Ya-Sin before him) due to the command for it, and in a report: 'There is no sick person before whom Ya-Sin is recited except that he dies satisfied and enters his grave satisfied.' (And some later scholars considered praiseworthy the recitation of Surah ar-Ra'd) due to the saying of Jabir, may Allah be pleased with him: 'It eases upon him the exit of his soul.' And they differed regarding removing the menstruating woman, the postpartum woman, and the person in major impurity from his presence; the reason for removal is the prevention of the presence of angels at a place with a menstruating or postpartum woman, as reported: 'A good person attends him.' (Then when he dies, his jaw is bound) with a wide band that encompasses both, and it is tied above his head for beautification and to preserve his mouth, and his eyes are closed due to the command for it in the Sunnah. And the one closing them says: 'In the name of Allah and upon the religion of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. O Allah, make his matter easy for him, make what is after him easy, make him happy with meeting You, and make what he went out to better than what he went out from.' Al-Kamal said it. Then he is covered.
Source pages p. 562

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya) from Al-Tahtawi on the rulings and etiquettes of talqin (prompting the deceased) and the deathbed. The discussion begins by addressing the hadith that the deceased can hear footsteps; the author suggests a reconciliation between prompting at death and after burial by noting that the hadith about hearing from the grave is at the time of questioning. The talqin at death is based on the explicit promise of salvation, and after burial it is to prepare the deceased for questioning—citing narrations from Sa'id ibn Mansur and others. The text then critiques various responses to the objection that the dead cannot hear, including interpretations that hearing was a miracle for the Prophet or metaphorical. The commentary moves to the deathbed: it recommends relatives, friends, and neighbors to be present to fulfill rights such as reminding the dying, giving drink to quench thirst (as Satan may tempt with water), and prompting him. Recitation of Surah Ya-Sin is commanded, and some later scholars recommend Surah ar-Ra'd. Regarding the removal of menstruating, postpartum, or junub individuals: although some argue against removing them due to compassion or need, the recommended view is that they should leave if possible because the presence of angels who bring mercy is impeded. The passage then transitions to post-death actions: binding the jaw, closing the eyes with a specific supplication, and covering the body.

Key Terms
تلقين (talqin): Prompting the dying or deceased person with the testimony of faith and other words of remembrance.
احتضار (ihtidar): The state of death agony or the moment before death.
حسن الظن بالله (husn al-zann billah): Having a good opinion of Allah, expecting His mercy and forgiveness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Quran 35:22
B) The hadith that the deceased hears the footsteps of those leaving the grave
C) The command of the Prophet to do so
D) The consensus of all scholars

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds talqin as mustahabb at death and after burial, supported by hadith and companion practice, and the ability of the deceased to hear at the time of questioning.

Post-Death Sunnah: Binding Jaw and Closing Eyes
Details the sunnah actions immediately after death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended post-death actions (binding jaw, closing eyes, supplication, covering) and explain their legal basis in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Honoring the deceased: binding jaw and closing eyes are sunnah, not wajib.

When a Muslim passes away, certain actions are recommended to honor the body. This passage from al-Tahtawi details the sunnah acts of binding the jaw, closing the eyes with a specific supplication, and covering the body. These actions are based on the Prophet's command and are considered mustahabb, not obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actions and their ruling
List the four actions mentioned: binding jaw, closing eyes, reciting the supplication, and covering. Determine the hukm: sunnah mu'akkada (recommended).
The text uses 'فَعَلَ' (does) implying sunnah, not fard.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage states 'for the command in the Sunnah' (للأمر به في السنة). Identify the primary evidence: the hadith commanding closing the eyes and speaking good.
Dalil is a hadith (zanni al-thubut), hence the ruling is sunnah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'aghmidu' (close) in the hadith indicates recommendation (istihbab) because the context is honoring the deceased, not obligation.
Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-nadb when qarinah indicates istihbab.
4
Note the supplication specifics
The supplication quoted is attributed to al-Kamal (Ibn al-Humam). It asks for ease and a happy meeting with Allah.
This supplication is sunnah, not obligatory; any good supplication suffices.
5
Understand the wisdom
Binding jaw preserves the mouth from insects and water during washing; closing eyes follows the soul; covering preserves modesty.
These actions combine respect and practical benefit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإذا مات شد لحياه) بعصابة عريضة تعمهما، وتربط فوق رأسه تحسيناً، وحفظاً لفمه وغمض عيناه (للأمر به في السنة ويقول مغمضه باسم الله وعلى ملة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم (اللهم يسر عليه أمره وسهل عليه ما بعده وأسعده بلقائك واجعل ما خرج إليه خيراً مما خرج عنه) قاله الكمال ثم يسجى
His statement: (Then when he dies, his jaw is bound) with a wide band that encompasses both [jaws], and it is tied above his head for beautification and to preserve his mouth, and his eyes are closed (due to the command for it in the Sunnah). And the one closing them says: 'In the name of Allah and upon the religion of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. O Allah, make his matter easy for him, make what is after him easy, make him happy with meeting You, and make what he went out to better than what he went out from.' Al-Kamal said it. Then he is covered.
Source pages p. 563

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement on the immediate post-death rituals. When a person dies, it is sunnah to bind the jaw with a wide bandage that wraps around both jaws and is tied above the head. The purposes are beautification and preserving the mouth (preventing insects and water entering during washing). Then the eyes are closed, in accordance with the sunnah. The one who closes the eyes recites a supplication beginning 'Bismillah wa 'ala millati Rasulillah' and then asks Allah to ease the deceased's matter, grant him a happy meeting, and make what he departed to better. Al-Kamal (Ibn al-Humam) is quoted as saying this supplication. Finally, the body is covered with a sheet (tasjiyah). These acts are mustahabb and reflect respect for the deceased.

Key Terms
شد اللحي (shadd al-lahyi): Binding the jaw (lower jaw) with a bandage to keep it closed.
تغميض العينين (taghmid al-'aynayn): Closing the eyes of the deceased by gently pressing the eyelids.
تسجية (tasjiyah): Covering the deceased body with a sheet from head to toe after death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To prevent the soul from leaving
B) For beautification and to preserve the mouth from insects and water
C) To test if the person is truly dead
D) To keep the mouth open for talqin

Key Takeaway
The immediate post-death acts of closing the eyes, binding the jaw, and covering are sunnah mu'akkada, not wajib, and are performed for respect and protection.

Sunan Acts After Death: Covering, Iron, and Joint Loosening
Describes immediate post-death sunan acts with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four sunan acts to perform on a deceased Muslim immediately after death and identify the evidence for each.

Core Idea
Covering, placing iron, hands at sides, and loosening joints are sunnah, based on practice of the Salaf.

When a Muslim passes away, there are specific recommended actions that facilitate washing and shrouding, prevent swelling, and avoid resembling non-Muslim practices. The Hanafi school derives these from narrations of the Companions and early scholars. This lesson covers the four main sunan acts and the proofs behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended actions
Read the source text and list the four physical acts prescribed for the deceased immediately after death: covering, placing iron on stomach, placing hands at sides, and loosening joints.
2
Determine the ruling level
Recognize that these acts are sunnah muakkadah (emphatically recommended), not obligatory. The text does not use wajib/fard language.
Hanafis classify them as sunnah based on the evidence being ahad and the nature of the actions.
3
Locate the dalil (proof)
Find the mentions of al-Sha'bi and al-Bayhaqi's narration about Anas. This establishes the practice as transmitted from the Salaf.
The proof is a specific riwayah (narration); it is not a direct Quranic verse.
4
Understand the wisdom (hikmah)
The text explains that iron prevents swelling 'li daf' al-nafkh' (because of a secret in it). If no iron, use any heavy object. This shows the purpose is practical, not ritual magic.
The secret may refer to iron's weight and thermal properties, but the text does not elaborate.
5
Note the prohibition against hand placement on chest
The text explicitly forbids placing hands on the chest, labeling it a practice of Ahl al-Kitab. This illustrates that some actions are avoided due to resemblance to other faiths.
This is a common mistake; the proper position is by the sides.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بثوب ويوضع على بطنه حديدة لئلا ينتفخ وهو مروي عن الشعبي، والحديد يدفع النفخ لسر فيه وإن لم يوجد فيوضع على بطنه شيء ثقيل، وروى البيهقي أن أنساً أمر بوضع حديد على بطن مولى له مات وتوضع يداه بجنبه) إشارة لتسليمه الأمر لربه (ولا يجوز وضعهما على صدره لأنه صنيع أهل الكتاب وتلين مفاصله وأصابعه بأن يرد ساعده لعضده وساقه لفخذه وفخذه لبطنه ويردها مليئة ليسهل غسله وإدراجه في الكفن
With a cloth, and an iron is placed on his stomach so that it does not swell, and this is narrated from al-Sha'bi. Iron prevents swelling due to a secret in it. If not found, a heavy object is placed on his stomach. Al-Bayhaqi narrated that Anas ordered to place iron on the stomach of a freed slave of his who died. And his hands are placed by his sides as an indication of surrendering his affair to his Lord. It is not permissible to place them on his chest because it is the practice of the People of the Book. And his joints and fingers are loosened by returning his forearm to his upper arm, his shin to his thigh, and his thigh to his stomach, and he returns them gently to facilitate washing and wrapping him in the shroud.
Source pages p. 564

Commentary
This passage outlines the recommended physical preparations immediately after death, covered in the hashya by al-Tahtawi. First, the deceased is covered with a cloth. Then a piece of iron is placed on the stomach to prevent bloating, a practice attributed to al-Sha'bi and backed by a narration from al-Bayhaqi about Anas ibn Malik. If iron is unavailable, any heavy object suffices. The hands are placed at the sides, not on the chest, to avoid resembling the People of the Book. Finally, the joints are loosened by bending the limbs in a gentle manner to facilitate washing and shrouding. These are sunna actions, not obligatory, based on prophetic practice and the example of the Companions.

Key Terms
تسجية (tasjiyyah): Covering the deceased with a cloth after death.
تليين المفاصل (talyīn al-mafāṣil): Loosening the joints of the deceased by gentle bending to facilitate washing and shrouding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) An iron

D) A wooden plank

Key Takeaway
Immediately after death, the Hanafi school prescribes four sunan acts: covering, placing a weight on the stomach, placing hands at sides, and loosening joints, all based on transmitted practice.

Reciting Quran Near the Deceased and the Nature of Impurity
Ruling with proof on recitation and impurity status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting Quran near the deceased before washing, explain the two views on the impurity of the deceased, and evaluate the preferred view using the hadith proof.

Core Idea
The believer is not impure, alive or dead; the deceased is in a state of hadath, not khabath.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi addresses a common practical question: can one recite Quran near a deceased person before the body has been washed? The answer involves a deeper legal dispute about the nature of impurity after death. We will explore the two competing views and the evidence that leads the Hanafi school to its nuanced ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? The text states: 'وتكره قراءة القرآن عنده حتى يغسل' — reciting Quran in the presence of the deceased before washing is disliked (makruh tanzih).
Note that the ruling is makruh tanzih, not haram.
2
Understand the rationale behind the ruling
The karaha is to honor the Quran from impurity (تنزيهاً للقرآن عن نجاسة). The text mentions two types of impurity: hadath (ceremonial) and khabath (filth).
The presence of both possibilities justifies the precautionary dislike.
3
Contrast the two views on the deceased's impurity
Some hold the deceased is impure with khabath (filth) — others say hadath (ritual impurity). The text states: 'فبعضهم قال إن نجاسته نجاسة خبث، وقيل حدث'.
The preferred view is hadath, as supported by strong evidence.
4
Examine the evidence for the hadath view
Two key proofs: (1) the Prophet kissed Uthman ibn Maz'un before washing — if he were khabath, the Prophet would not have placed his mouth on him; (2) the hadith 'لا تنجسوا موتاكم فإن المؤمن لا ينجس حياً ولا ميتاً' reported by Ibn Abbas and authenticated by al-Hakim.
This hadith is classified as zanni al-thubut but qati al-dalalah (clear meaning).
5
Note the practical consequence and tarjih
The thamarah al-khilaf: if khabath, recitation would be more severely prohibited; if hadath, it remains disliked but some permit. The Hanafi tarjih maintains karaha due to the predominant presence of actual impurities on the deceased's body.
Al-Tahtawi follows al-Nihayah in preferring the hadath view but retains the karaha.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتكره قراءة القرآن عنده حتى يغسل) تنزيهاً للقرآن عن نجاسة الحدث بالموت والخبث فإنه يزول عن المسلم عينيه من الدار الأخرى، وقوله : خيراً مما خرج عنه بأن يبدله داراً خيراً من داره، وزوجاً خيراً من زوجه قوله: (ثم يسجى بثوب بالتشديد أي يغطى لما روي أن أبا بكر دخل على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، وهو مسجي ببرد حبرة فكشف عن وجهه، ثم أكب عليه فقبله، ثم بكى، وفي التمهيد لما توفي عثمان يعني ابن مظعون كشف النبي الثوب الا عن وجهه ، وبكى بكاء طويلاً، وقبل بين فلما رفع على السرير قال: طوبى لك يا عثمان لم تلبسك الدنيا، ولم تلبسها». قوله : ويوضع على بطنه (حديدة أو مرآة كما في الحموي، وتنكير الحديدة يفيد أنه يكفي فيه القليل .. قوله : (لأنه منه . صنيع أهل الكتاب أي وقد أمرنا بمخالفتهم وتعبير المصنف بلا يجوز يفيد الحرمة. قوله : ( وتكره) قراءة القرآن) ولو آية كما في شرح السيد، وقوله عنده: أي بقربه . قوله: (عن نجاسة (الحدث هذا ينافي ما في الشرح من أنه على القول بأن نجاسة الميت نجاسة حدث ينبغي أن تجوز القراءة كما لو قرأها المحدث وفي السيد ما يفيد أن في الكراهة على هذا القول خلافاً، ورجح في النهاية الكراهة والحاصل أنهم اختلفوا في نجاسة الميت فقيل: نجاسة خبث وقيل : حدث، ويشهد للثاني ما رويناه من تقبيله عثمان بن مظعون وهو ميت قبل الغسل إذ لو كان نجساً وضع فاه الشريف على جسده، ولا ينافي ذلك ما ذكروه من أنه لو حمله إنسان قبل الغسل فصلى به لا تصح صلاته وكذا كراهة القراءة عنده قبل الغسل، لجواز أن يكون ذلك لعدم خلوه عن نجاسة غالباً، والغالب كالمحقق، وروى البخاري تعليقاً عن ابن عباس : المسلم لا ينجس حياً، ولا ميتاً ووصله الحاكم في المستدرك عن ابن عباس أيضاً قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : لا تنجسوا موتاكم فإن المؤمن لا ينجس حياً ولا ميتاً، قال العيني في شرح البخاري والنووي في شرح مسلم : هذا أصل عظيم في طهارة المسلم حياً، وميتاً أما الحي فبالإجماع حتى الجنين إذا ألقته أمه وعليه رطوبة فرجها فهو ظاهر بإجماع المسلمين، وأما الميت ففيه خلاف العلماء. قال البدر العيني : فإن قلت : على هذا ينبغي أن لا يغسل الميت لأنه طاهر قلنا الموجب اتباع الوارد واختلف أصحابنا في سبب غسله، فقيل: حدث يحل به لا لنجاسته لأنّ الآدمي لا ينجس بالموت كرامة له إذ لو تنجس لما ظهر بالغسل كسائر الحيوانات، وكان الواجب الاقتصار على أعضاء الوضوء كما في حال الحياة لكن ذلك إنما كان نفياً للحرج فيما يتكرر كل يوم والحدث بسبب الموت لا يتكرر، فكان كالجنابة فبقي بالغسل تكريماً له بخلاف الكافر
And recitation of the Quran is disliked in his presence until he is washed, to honor the Quran from the impurity of hadath (ceremonial impurity) through death and khabath (filth). For the Muslim, it is removed from his eyes of the next world... And the gist is that they differed concerning the impurity of the deceased: some said it is impurity of filth (khabath), and some said it is impurity of event (hadath). The second is supported by what we narrated of the Prophet kissing Uthman ibn Maz'un while he was dead before washing, because if he were impure (najis), he would not have placed his noble mouth on his body... And Bukhari narrated with a suspended chain from Ibn Abbas: 'The Muslim is not impure, alive or dead.' Al-Hakim connected it in al-Mustadrak from Ibn Abbas also who said: The Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم said: 'Do not make your dead impure, for the believer is not impure alive or dead.' Al-Ayni in his commentary on Bukhari and al-Nawawi in his commentary on Muslim said: This is a great principle in the purity of the Muslim alive and dead... Our scholars differed on the cause of washing him: some said it is a hadath that descends upon him, not due to his impurity, because the human does not become impure by death as an honor to him...
Source pages p. 564

Commentary
This passage details the ruling on reciting Quran near the deceased before washing and the underlying dispute about the nature of the deceased's impurity. Al-Tahtawi explains that recitation is disliked (makruh) to avoid exposing the Quran to impurity. Two views exist: the deceased is impure due to khabath (filth) or hadath (ritual impurity). The preferred view (from proofs like the Prophet kissing Uthman ibn Maz'un unwashed and the hadith 'the believer is not impure') is that the Muslim is pure and only becomes hadath, not khabath. Evidence includes the Prophet's kiss, the hadith from Ibn Abbas, and the principle that humans are honored. Therefore, washing is performed not because of impurity but as a requirement of sharia. The ruling of dislike (karaha) for recitation before washing is maintained because the deceased is generally not free from impurities outwardly. This shows the depth of Hanafi legal reasoning, balancing textual proofs and customary practice.

Key Terms
نجاسة الحدث (najāsat al-ḥadath): Ritual impurity that can be removed by wudu/ghusl; the deceased is considered in this state per the preferred view.
نجاسة الخبث (najāsat al-khabath): Filth impurity that is removed by washing the specific spot; alternate view for the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited, what is the status of a believing deceased?
A) Impure like a kafir
B) Impure in khabath but not hadath
C) Pure (not impure) alive or dead
D) Pure only after washing

Key Takeaway
The Muslim deceased is pure in essence, but reciting Quran before washing is disliked due to possible contact with actual impurities, not because the body itself is impure.

Announcing Death and Hastening Preparation
Rulings on notifying and hastening.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on informing people of a death and hastening the funeral preparation, and explain the evidence from the Prophet's actions.

Core Idea
Announcing death gathers prayers, preparation must be swift.

When a person dies, the community has duties toward their funeral. The Hanafi school teaches that notifying others is recommended to increase participants in the funeral prayer, while preparation must be hastened once death is certain. This lesson explores the evidence from the Prophet's practice and the conditions that keep this act from becoming ostentatious.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts
Two acts: informing people of death (i'lam al-mawt) and hastening preparation (ta'jil al-tajhiz). Determine their hukm.
Informing is mustahabb; hastening is implied wajib from 'yu'ajjal'.
2
Locate the dalil for informing
The text cites that the Prophet announced the death of al-Najashi to his companions on the same day, and also announced the deaths of Ja'far, Zayd, and Abdullah. This establishes the sunnah.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Analyze the condition for public announcement
The text from al-Nihayah states that if the deceased is a scholar or pious person, some later scholars recommended announcing in marketplaces. The correct view allows it, but not for pride.
Key condition: no exaggeration or arrogance.
4
Note the ruling on hastening
When death is certain, preparation (washing, shrouding, burial) should be hastened. This is based on general encouragement to expedite funerals.
The phrase 'yujabbar' indicates obligation after certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بأس بإعلام الناس بموته بل يستحب لتكثير المصلين عليه لما رواه الشيخان أنه نعى لأصحابه النجاشي في اليوم الذي مات فيه وأنه نعى جعفر بن أبي طالب وزيد بن حارثة وعبد الله ابن رواحة وقال في النهاية : إن كان عالماً، أو زاهداً أو ممن يتبرك به فقد استحسن بعض المتأخرين النداء في الأسواق لجنازته، وهو الأصح انتهى وكثير من المشايخ لم يروا بأسا بأن يؤذن بالجنازة ليؤدي أقاربه وأصدقاؤه حقه لكن لا على جهة التفخيم والإفراط في المدح (و) إذا تيقن موته (يعجل بتجهيزه). ولا بأس بإرثاء الميت بشعر، أو غيره ما لم يفرط في مدحه، ولا يكره البكاء عليه بإرسال الدموع، بلا رفع صوت، ولا نياحة ولا شق ثوب، وضرب خد ونحو ذلك، وسواء في ذلك قبل الموت، وبعده على الصحيح ) النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بكى على ابنه ابراهيم فقال له عبد الرحمن بن عوف وأنت يا رسول الله تبكي فقال: يا ابن عوف إنها رحمة وقال : إن العين تدمع والقلب يحزن، ولا نقول إلا ما يرضي ربنا، وإنا بفرقاك يا إبراهيم لمحزونون» أخرجه الشيخان وفي حديث ألا تسمعون أن الله لا يعذب بدمع العين، ولا بحزن القلب، ولكن يعذب بهذا، وأشار إلى لسانه، أو يرحم رواه الشيخان أيضاً
There is no harm in informing people of his death, rather it is recommended to increase those who pray over him. Because the two Shaykhs (Bukhari and Muslim) narrated that he (the Prophet) announced the death of al-Najashi to his companions on the day he died, and he announced the death of Ja'far ibn Abi Talib, Zayd ibn Haritha, and Abdullah ibn Rawaha. And it is said in al-Nihayah: If he was a scholar, or a pious person, or one from whom blessings are sought, then some later scholars recommended announcing in the marketplaces for his funeral, and that is the correct view. And many mashayikh saw no harm in informing about the funeral so that his relatives and friends may fulfill his right, but not in a manner of exaggeration and excess in praise. And when his death is certain, his preparation is hastened. There is no harm in eulogizing the deceased with poetry or other if one does not exaggerate in his praise. Nor is weeping disliked by shedding tears without raising the voice, wailing, tearing clothes, slapping cheeks, etc. And it is the same before death and after according to the correct view. The Prophet (peace be upon him) wept for his son Ibrahim, and Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf said to him: 'O Messenger of Allah, you are weeping?' He said: 'O Ibn Awf, it is mercy.' And he said: 'The eye tears and the heart grieves, and we do not say except what pleases our Lord, and we are indeed saddened by your departure, O Ibrahim.'
Source pages p. 565

Commentary
This passage discusses social and emotional practices related to death. First, informing the community is not only allowed but recommended (mustahabb) to increase the number of participants in the funeral prayer, as the Prophet himself announced the death of al-Najashi. For virtuous individuals, some scholars even endorse public announcements in markets. However, ostentation and excessive praise are discouraged. Second, if death is confirmed, preparation (washing, shrouding, burial) should be hastened. Third, eulogizing the deceased with poetry or prose is permissible as long as it does not involve exaggeration or false praise. Fourth, weeping is allowed, even before death, as long as it is silent (tears without wailing, beating, or tearing clothes). The Prophet's own tears for his son Ibrahim are the proof. Hence, loud wailing (niyahah) and physical harm are forbidden, but natural grief expressed through tears is not. This balances respect for the deceased with religious prohibitions on excessive lamentation.

Key Terms
إعلام (i'lām): Informing others of a person's death.
تجهيز (tajhīz): Preparing the deceased for burial: washing, shrouding, praying, and burying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is the Hanafi ruling on informing people of a death?
A) It is obligatory (wajib).
B) It is recommended (mustahabb) to increase participants in the funeral prayer.
C) It is disliked (makruh) because it may cause pride.
D) It is prohibited (haram) because it resembles the pre-Islamic custom.

Key Takeaway
Informing others of a death is a recommended sunnah that increases prayers for the deceased, provided it is free from ostentation.

Weeping and Eulogizing the Deceased
Rulings on weeping, wailing, and eulogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish permissible weeping from prohibited wailing and apply the Hanafi ruling on eulogizing the deceased.

Core Idea
Tears are mercy, wailing is torment; eulogize without excess.

Grief is natural; Islam does not forbid sadness. The Prophet himself wept for his son. However, loud wailing, tearing clothes, and slapping are prohibited because they express discontent with divine decree. Eulogy in poetry or prose is allowed if it does not exaggerate. This lesson examines the proofs and boundaries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts
Three acts: weeping (buka'), wailing (niyahah), and eulogizing (ritha'). Determine hukm for each.
Weeping is mubah; wailing is haram; eulogy is mubah with condition.
2
Locate the dalil for weeping
The Prophet wept for Ibrahim and said 'It is mercy'. Another hadith: 'Allah does not punish for tears but for what the tongue says.'
Hadith from Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Analyze the prohibition of wailing
Wailing, tearing clothes, slapping are explicitly forbidden. The hadith indicates punishment for what the tongue speaks (i.e., lamentation).
These actions show displeasure with Qadr.
4
Examine eulogy
Eulogizing (ritha') is allowed if without exaggeration. The text says 'لا بأس' (no harm).
Excess praise may become falsehood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بأس بإعلام الناس بموته بل يستحب لتكثير المصلين عليه لما رواه الشيخان أنه نعى لأصحابه النجاشي في اليوم الذي مات فيه وأنه نعى جعفر بن أبي طالب وزيد بن حارثة وعبد الله ابن رواحة وقال في النهاية : إن كان عالماً، أو زاهداً أو ممن يتبرك به فقد استحسن بعض المتأخرين النداء في الأسواق لجنازته، وهو الأصح انتهى وكثير من المشايخ لم يروا بأسا بأن يؤذن بالجنازة ليؤدي أقاربه وأصدقاؤه حقه لكن لا على جهة التفخيم والإفراط في المدح (و) إذا تيقن موته (يعجل بتجهيزه). ولا بأس بإرثاء الميت بشعر، أو غيره ما لم يفرط في مدحه، ولا يكره البكاء عليه بإرسال الدموع، بلا رفع صوت، ولا نياحة ولا شق ثوب، وضرب خد ونحو ذلك، وسواء في ذلك قبل الموت، وبعده على الصحيح ) النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بكى على ابنه ابراهيم فقال له عبد الرحمن بن عوف وأنت يا رسول الله تبكي فقال: يا ابن عوف إنها رحمة وقال : إن العين تدمع والقلب يحزن، ولا نقول إلا ما يرضي ربنا، وإنا بفرقاك يا إبراهيم لمحزونون» أخرجه الشيخان وفي حديث ألا تسمعون أن الله لا يعذب بدمع العين، ولا بحزن القلب، ولكن يعذب بهذا، وأشار إلى لسانه، أو يرحم رواه الشيخان أيضاً
There is no harm in informing people of his death, rather it is recommended to increase those who pray over him. Because the two Shaykhs (Bukhari and Muslim) narrated that he (the Prophet) announced the death of al-Najashi to his companions on the day he died, and he announced the death of Ja'far ibn Abi Talib, Zayd ibn Haritha, and Abdullah ibn Rawaha. And it is said in al-Nihayah: If he was a scholar, or a pious person, or one from whom blessings are sought, then some later scholars recommended announcing in the marketplaces for his funeral, and that is the correct view. And many mashayikh saw no harm in informing about the funeral so that his relatives and friends may fulfill his right, but not in a manner of exaggeration and excess in praise. And when his death is certain, his preparation is hastened. There is no harm in eulogizing the deceased with poetry or other if one does not exaggerate in his praise. Nor is weeping disliked by shedding tears without raising the voice, wailing, tearing clothes, slapping cheeks, etc. And it is the same before death and after according to the correct view. The Prophet (peace be upon him) wept for his son Ibrahim, and Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf said to him: 'O Messenger of Allah, you are weeping?' He said: 'O Ibn Awf, it is mercy.' And he said: 'The eye tears and the heart grieves, and we do not say except what pleases our Lord, and we are indeed saddened by your departure, O Ibrahim.'
Source pages p. 565

Commentary
This passage discusses social and emotional practices related to death. First, informing the community is not only allowed but recommended (mustahabb) to increase the number of participants in the funeral prayer, as the Prophet himself announced the death of al-Najashi. For virtuous individuals, some scholars even endorse public announcements in markets. However, ostentation and excessive praise are discouraged. Second, if death is confirmed, preparation (washing, shrouding, burial) should be hastened. Third, eulogizing the deceased with poetry or prose is permissible as long as it does not involve exaggeration or false praise. Fourth, weeping is allowed, even before death, as long as it is silent (tears without wailing, beating, or tearing clothes). The Prophet's own tears for his son Ibrahim are the proof. Hence, loud wailing (niyahah) and physical harm are forbidden, but natural grief expressed through tears is not. This balances respect for the deceased with religious prohibitions on excessive lamentation.

Key Terms
نياحة (niyāḥah): Loud wailing and lamentation over the deceased; forbidden.
رثاء (rithā'): Eulogizing the deceased with poetry or prose; permissible if without exaggeration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following acts is explicitly permitted in the passage?
A) Wailing with a loud voice.
B) Tearing clothes in grief.
C) Shedding tears silently.
D) Slapping the face.

Key Takeaway
Weeping silently is permissible and even shown by the Prophet; only wailing, tearing, and slapping are prohibited.

Placing the Deceased and Covering Awrah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on placement and awrah coverage of the deceased

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two disputed issues in preparing the deceased (placement and awrah covering) and explain the tarjih (preferred view) within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
For the deceased, covering the thick 'awrah suffices — the Hidayah view prevails for ease and apparent riwayah.

The preparation of a deceased person involves practical decisions such as how to lay them on the bier and what parts to cover. Within the Hanafi school, there are differing opinions on both matters. This lesson examines the views recorded in key Hanafi texts and identifies the relied-upon position, highlighting the school's method of tarjih (preference) based on ease and authority of transmission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
The passage discusses two separate issues: (1) the orientation of the deceased on the bier, and (2) the extent of covering the 'awrah. Recognize that these are independent rulings with their own ikhtilaf.
Placement: how is the body placed? Awrah: what must be covered?
2
List the differing opinions on placement
Three views are mentioned: (a) as agreed upon (the most correct per Shams al-Sarakhsi), (b) widthwise (like in the grave), (c) towards the qiblah (like one praying by gesture). Note that the passage indicates the first view is preferred.
Mufta bihi: placement however agreed (or sunnah towards qiblah?) — source says 'as agreed upon' is the most correct.
3
List the differing opinions on awrah covering
Two views: al-Zayla'i and al-Nihayah require from navel to knee; al-Hidayah says covering the thick 'awrah (private parts) suffices. Identify the basis for each.
Keys: 'thick 'awrah' means genitals and anus.
4
Understand the proofs and tarjih
The wider view relies on a hadith prohibiting looking at the thigh. The narrower view argues the purpose is to nullify desire (which is minimal for the deceased) and that the hadith applies to the living. Tarjih favors ease (taysir) and the apparent riwayah (zahir al-riwayah).
Tarjih mechanism: ease + strength of riwayah.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The preferred view in the Hanafi school is that covering only the thick 'awrah suffices. This is the mufta bihi as stated by al-Tahtawi.
The commentator sides with al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويوضع الميت (كيف اتفق على الأصح) قاله شمس السرخسي وقيل : عرضاً وقيل : إلى القبلة ويستر عورته ما بين سرته إلى ركبته قاله الزيلعي، والنهاية هو الصحيح، وفي الهداية يكتفي بستر العورة الغليظة هو الصحيح تيسراً وهو ظاهر الرواية ولبطلان الشهوة
And the deceased is placed (however it is agreed upon, which is the most correct) - said Shams al-Sarakhsi. And it is said: widthwise. And it is said: towards the qiblah. And his 'awrah is covered from his navel to his knee - said al-Zayla'i, and in al-Nihayah this is the correct view. And in al-Hidayah, covering the thick 'awrah suffices - this is the correct view for ease, and it is the apparent riwayah, and due to the nullification of desire.
Source pages p. 567

Commentary
This passage is an intra-madhhab dispute on two issues: the placement of the deceased on the bier and the extent of covering the 'awrah. On placement, there are three views: (1) as agreed upon (the most correct according to Shams al-Sarakhsi), (2) widthwise (like in the grave), (3) towards the qiblah with feet pointing to qiblah (like a sick person praying by gesture, considered sunnah in al-Muhit). On covering 'awrah, al-Zayla'i and al-Nihayah say it must be from navel to knee, but al-Hidayah says covering only the thick 'awrah (private parts) suffices for ease. The latter is preferred as it is the apparent riwayah and because the purpose is nullifying desire, which is already minimal. The author of the hashya sides with the Hidayah view.

Key Terms
العورة الغليظة (al-'awrah al-ghalizah): The private parts (front and back) that must be covered; for men, the area between navel and knee is considered 'awrah but the thick part is the genitals and anus.
تيسر (taysīr): Ease, facility; a principle in Hanafi fiqh to choose the easier ruling when evidence permits.
ظاهر الرواية (zāhir al-riwāyah): The apparent or well-known transmission; refers to rulings in the six core works of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (Zahir al-Riwayah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in al-Hidayah, what part of the deceased's body must be covered?
A) The entire body
B) From navel to knee
C) The thick 'awrah (private parts only)
D) Nothing; the deceased is not required to be covered

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, covering the thick 'awrah of the deceased suffices, and the body may be placed in any agreed orientation.

Stripping and Wudu for the Deceased: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Istinja
Ruling on stripping and wudu, with exception for minors and dispute on istinja

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules for stripping and wudu of the deceased, and explain the dispute on istinja between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
The deceased is given a simplified wudu without rinsing mouth or nose; istinja is not performed in the mufta bihi view.

This lesson examines the procedures for washing the deceased. After covering the 'awrah, the body is stripped (if not a khuntha), then given wudu. The correct view is to wash the face and wipe the head, without rinsing mouth or nose. For a minor who does not understand prayer, no wudu is given. Inside the Hanafi school, there is a dispute about whether istinja should be performed during this wudu. We will explore both positions and the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rulings on stripping and covering
Strip the deceased unless they are a khuntha. The 'awrah must be covered and washed indirectly with a rag.
Khuntha: ambiguous gender – washed in clothes to avoid uncovering 'awrah.
2
State the wudu procedure
Wudu is given: wash face, wipe head. No rinsing of mouth or nose; those are wiped with a rag.
This is the correct view (al-sahih).
3
Note the exception for minors
A minor who does not understand prayer is not given wudu. If aged seven or more and understands prayer, wudu is given.
Based on the link between wudu and prayer.
4
Analyse the intra-Hanafi dispute on istinja
Muhammad and Abu Yusuf (in one transmission) say istinja should be done; Abu Yusuf (alone) says it is not needed because the need has ceased and it may cause impurity.
The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is not to perform istinja.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if istinja is performed, extra care is taken; if omitted, the process is simpler and avoids potential additional impurity.
The mufta bihi follows Abu Yusuf's second view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم بعد ستر عورته بإدخال الساتر من تحت الثياب (جرد عن ثيابه) إن لم يكن خنثى، وتغسل عورته بخرقة ملفوفة تحت الساتر أو من فوقه إن لم يوجد خرقة (و) بعده (وضىء) يبدأ بوجهه ويمسح رأسه (في الصحيح) إلا أن يكون صغيراً لا يعقل الصلاة فلا يوضاً بلا مضمضة واستنشاق للتعسر ويمسح فمه وأنفه بخرقة
Then after covering his 'awrah by inserting the cover under the clothes, (he is stripped of his clothes) if he is not a khuntha. And his 'awrah is washed with a rag wrapped under the cover or over it if no rag is found. And after that, (he is given wudu) beginning with his face and wiping his head (according to the correct view) unless he is a minor who does not understand prayer, then he is not given wudu, without rinsing mouth and nose due to difficulty, and his mouth and nose are wiped with a rag.
Source pages p. 567

Commentary
This passage covers two procedures: stripping the deceased and performing wudu. Stripping is done unless the deceased is a khuntha (ambiguous gender), in which case he/she is washed in clothes to avoid looking at awrah. The awrah is washed with a rag wrapped around the hand to avoid direct touch, which is haram. For wudu, the correct view is to start with the face and wipe the head (like living wudu but without washing arms and feet twice? Actually the text only mentions face and head). The mouth and nose are not rinsed with water; instead they are wiped with a rag because of difficulty. A minor who does not understand prayer is not given wudu at all, but if he is seven years old or more, he is given wudu because he is commanded to pray. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute on istinja: according to Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, istinja is performed; according to Abu Yusuf alone (in one transmission), it is not done because the need has ceased. The author notes that the common practice is not to do istinja unless the deceased was in a state of janabah, etc.

Key Terms
الخنثى (al-khuntha): A person with ambiguous gender, neither clearly male nor female.
الاستنجاء (al-istinja): Washing the front and back private parts to remove impurities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a small child who does not understand prayer not given wudu?
A) Because he is not mukallaf
B) Because it is too difficult
C) Because his body is pure
D) Because wudu is only for adults

Key Takeaway
The deceased's wudu is simplified (face and head only, no mouth/nose rinsing) and istinja is not performed according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

The Sunnah of Using Sidr or Hurud in Ghusl al-Mayyit
Ruling with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on using sidr or hurud in washing the deceased and identify the proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Using sidr or hurud is a sunnah; plain water suffices for the obligatory ghusl.

In this passage, we learn the recommended method for washing the deceased: using boiled water mixed with sidr (lotus leaves) or hurud (a cleansing agent). This is based on the Prophet's command. If these are unavailable, plain heated water is sufficient. Understanding the sunnah versus obligation helps avoid unnecessary rigidity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is washing the deceased with sidr or hurud. The Hanafi ruling is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah).
2
Locate the dalil
The dalil is the hadith where the Prophet commanded washing his daughter and a muhrim who died in ihram with water and sidr.
The hadith is cited as evidence for the recommendation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's command indicates recommendation (not obligation) because plain water is also acceptable and the context (muhrim) shows flexibility.
In Hanafi usul, a command can indicate obligation or recommendation; here the existence of an alternative lowers it to sunnah.
4
Note the alternative
If sidr or hurud are not available, plain pure water (al-qarah) suffices, and it is heated.
This confirms the obligation is simply washing with water; the additives are sunnah.
5
Understand the sunnah level
This is sunnah muakkadah because of the direct prophetic command and the emphasis on cleaning.
Sunnah muakkadah is highly recommended; omitting it without excuse is disliked but the ghusl remains valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعد الوضوء صب عليه ماء مغلي قد مزج بسدر أو حرض) أشنان غير مطحون مبالغة في التنظيف وقد أمر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أن تغسل بنته ، والمحرم الذي وقصته دابته بماء وسدر ( وإلا ) أي وإن لم يوجدا (فا) الغسل با القراح وهو الماء الخالص) كاف ويسخن
And after wudu, pour upon him boiled water that has been mixed with sidr or hurud (crushed soapwort, not ground) as an emphasis on cleaning. Indeed the Prophet, peace be upon him, commanded that his daughter be washed, and the muhrim who was killed by his animal, with water and sidr. And if not (i.e., if they are not found), then washing with plain water (which is pure water) suffices, and it is heated.
Source pages p. 568

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Sunnah. After the wudu, the deceased is washed with water that has been boiled and mixed with sidr (lotus leaves) or hurud (a cleansing agent like soapwort). This is to ensure thorough cleaning. The Prophet ﷺ ordered that his daughter (Zaynab or Fatimah according to different reports) be washed with water and sidr. Similarly, the muhrim (one in ihram) who was killed by his mount was washed with water and sidr. If these ingredients are not available, plain pure water suffices, and it is recommended to be warm. The word 'mugliy' means boiled, indicating heated water is preferred.

Key Terms
السدر (al-sidr): Lotus tree leaves, used as a cleansing agent in washing the deceased.
الحرض (al-hurud): A plant (soapwort) used as a detergent, crushed but not ground.
القراح (al-qarah): Pure, plain water without any additive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on using sidr or hurud when washing the deceased?
A) Obligatory (fard)
B) Recommended (sunnah)
C) Permissible (mubah)
D) Disliked (makruh)

Key Takeaway
Sidr or hurud is a sunnah additive; plain water fulfills the obligation of ghusl.

Rinsing Mouth and Nose for Deceased with Janaba
Intra-Hanafi dispute on madmadah/istinshaq for junub deceased

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on madmadah/istinshaq for a junub deceased and identify the dalil (Hadith of Hanzala) used to support the majority view.

Core Idea
A deceased in janaba does not require mouth/nose rinsing; the angels omitted it for Hanzala.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute: when a deceased person was in a state of janaba (major impurity), must the washer rinse their mouth and nose? The base text of Maraqi al-Falah suggests it is required, but al-Tahtawi's commentary refutes this, citing the hadith of Hanzala. The ruling has practical implications for funeral washing (ghusl al-mayyit).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the relied-upon view: madmadah and istinshaq are not required for the deceased, even if they were in janaba.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the minority view and its proof
Al-Khalikhali argues that the deceased must have mouth and nose rinsed, analogizing to a living person in janaba who must do so.
This is based on qiyas.
3
Examine the Hanafi response and dalil
The majority rejects the analogy because the Hadith of Hanzala (angels washing him without madmadah/istinshaq) provides a specific exception (takhsis) that overrides the analogy.
The hadith is ahad but its absence of mention is considered indicative.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if one follows the minority view, they add the rinsing steps; the majority omits them, relying on the explicit sunna.
The majority view is preferred for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عليه عمل الناس إلا أن يكون جنباً أو حائضاً، أو نفساء فيكلف غسل فمه وأنفه تتميماً لطهارته. قال في الفتح وغيره: استحب بعض العلماء أن يلف الغاسل على إصبعه خرقة، ويمسح بها أسنانه، ولهائه وشفتيه، ومنخريه وسرته، كما عليه عمل الناس اليوم. هذا ما ذكره الخلخالي، وهو غريب مخالف لعامة الكتب كما في الشلبي على الكنز، والذي في التبيين أن الجنب كغيره، وما في شرح السيد من أن ما ذكره الخلخالي مخالفاً لغيره مخرج على خلاف آخر في الشهيد إذا كان جنباً فإنه يغسل عند الإمام، وما ذكره غير مخرج على قول الصاحبين، وهو الذي في عامة الكتب فيه نظر لأن الكلام هنا في المضمضمة والاستنشاق لا في الغسل، والفرق أنه لا خرج فيه بخلافهما، وقد عرفنا غسل الشهيد الجنب بالنص، وهو تغسيل الملائكة حنظلة بن الراهب حين استشهد وهو جنب، فقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: رأيت الملائكة تغسل حنظلة بن أبي عامر بين السماء والأرض بماء المزن في صحائف الفضة، ولم يذكر فيه المضمضة والاستنشاق فانصرف إلى المعهود في غسل الميت، وهو الغسل بدونهما فتأمل أفاده بعض الأفاضل.
The practice of the people is upon it unless the deceased is in a state of major impurity (janaba) or menstruation or postpartum bleeding, then he is tasked with washing his mouth and nose to complete his purification. Al-Fath and others said: Some scholars recommended that the washer wrap a cloth on his finger and wipe the teeth, palate, lips, nostrils, and navel of the deceased, as is the practice of people today. This is what al-Khalikhali mentioned, which is strange and contrary to the majority of books as in al-Shibli on al-Kanz. In al-Tabyin it is said that the one in janaba is like others. What is in Sharh al-Sayyid, that what al-Khalikhali mentioned contrary to others is derived from another difference regarding the martyr if he is in janaba: according to Abu Hanifa he is washed, and what he mentioned is derived from the saying of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), which is in most books. There is consideration in this because the discussion here is about rinsing the mouth and nose, not about the washing itself. The difference is that there is no difficulty in it unlike the two. We know the washing of the martyred Hanzala ibn al-Rahib when he was martyred in janaba by the text: The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: I saw the angels washing Hanzala ibn Abi 'Amir between the sky and the earth with rainwater in silver trays, and he did not mention rinsing the mouth and nose. So he turned to the customary practice in washing the deceased, which is washing without them. So ponder. This was communicated by one of the distinguishers.
Source pages p. 568

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a deceased person who was in a state of janaba (major impurity) requires additional rinsing of the mouth and nose (madmadah and istinshaq) during the ritual washing (ghusl al-mayyit). The base ruling (from Maraqi al-Falah) states that the deceased is washed like a living person except if they were junub, ha'id, or nufasa'; in those cases, the washer must clean the mouth and nose to complete purification. Al-Tahtawi then critiques this: he notes that al-Khalikhali's view is unusual and contrary to most Hanafi works. He cites al-Tabyin which says the junub is like any other deceased. He then clarifies that the real dispute concerns the martyr (shahid): Abu Hanifa holds that a martyred junub is washed (contrary to the usual rule that martyrs are not washed), while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that he is not washed. However, the present context is about madmadah/istinshaq, not full washing. The proof is the hadith of Hanzala: the angels washed him with rainwater but did not rinse his mouth or nose. This indicates that madmadah/istinshaq are not required for the deceased, even if junub. Thus, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that one does not rinse the mouth and nose of the deceased, contrary to what the base text suggests. The passage guards against the misunderstanding that the requirement for a living person in janaba to rinse mouth/nose necessarily applies to the deceased.

Key Terms
مضمضة (madmadah): Rinsing the mouth with water during wudu or ghusl.
استنشاق (istinshaq): Inhaling water into the nose and expelling it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling on rinsing the mouth and nose (madmadah/istinshaq) when washing a deceased person who was in janaba?
A) It is wajib because the deceased is like a living person.
B) It is not required; the hadith of Hanzala shows it was omitted.
C) It is mustahab but not mandatory.
D) It is makruh to do so.

Key Takeaway
Madmadah and istinshaq are not required for washing a deceased in janaba; the angels' washing of Hanzala without them is the evidence.
