6 min
Procedure of Washing the Deceased
Detailed fiqh procedure with prophetic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for washing the deceased, identify the prophetic proof for using sidr, and apply the ruling that excrement during washing does not invalidate the ghusl.

Core Idea
Wash the deceased with water and sidr, starting with the right; incidental impurities do not break the ghusl.

This lesson details the step-by-step Hanafi procedure for washing a deceased Muslim (ghusl al-mayyit). The source passage from Al-Tahtawi’s hashia combines practical instructions with the prophetic proof for using sidr. You will learn the order of washing, the use of cleaning agents, and the legal rulings for incidental impurities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the legal classification: washing the deceased is fard kifayah (communal obligation). The detailed steps are sunan and mustahabbat.
The obligation falls on the community; if some perform it, others are absolved.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the hadith where the Prophet commanded washing his daughter and a muhrim with water and sidr.
This hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), but sufficient for establishing the sunnah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the proof yields the ruling: the command (amr) implies that using sidr is prescribed and the act of washing itself is established.
In Hanafi usul, al-amr yufidu al-nadb (recommendation) when not accompanied by qarinah indicating wujub.
4
Understand the conditions and sunan
Identify the sequence: after wudu of the washer, use heated water with sidr or ushnan, wash head/beard with khitmi, then wash body starting with right side, then left, massage belly, dry the body.
If sidr/ushnan unavailable, pure water suffices. The belly massage may expel remains.
5
Note the special case of excrement
If excrement emerges, wash only the soiled area; do not repeat the entire ghusl or wudu of the deceased, as it does not break his state.
This rule is based on istihsan: the deceased is not subject to the same purity rules as the living.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و بعد الوضوء صب عليه ماء مغلي قد مزج بسدر أو حرض أشنان غير مطحون مبالغة في التنظيف وقد أمر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أن تغسل بنته والمحرم الذي وقصته دابته بماء وسدر وإلا فا الغسل با القراح وهو الماء الخالص كاف ويسخن إن تيسر لأنه أبلغ في التنظيف ويغسل رأسه وشعر لحيته بالخطمي نبت بالعراق طيب الرائحة يعمل عمل الصابون في التنظيف وإن لم يكن فالصابون وإن لم يكن به شعر لا يتكلف لهذا ثم بعد تنظيف الشعر والبشرة يضجع الميت على يساره فيغسل شقه الأيمن ابتداء لأن البداءة بالميامن سنة حتى يصل الماء إلى ما يلي التخت منه ثم على يمينه فيغسل كذلك حتى يصل الماء إلى سائر جسده ثم أجلس الميت مسنداً إليه لئلا يسقط ومسح بطنه مسحاً رفيقاً ليخرج فضلاته وما خرج منه غسله فقط تنظيفاً ولم يعد غسله ولا وضؤه لأنه ليس بناقض في حقه ثم ينشف بثوب كيلا تبتل أكفانه، والنية في تغسيله لإسقاط الفرض عنا حتى إنه إذا وجد غريقاً يحرك في الماء بنية غسله لهذا لا لصحة الصلاة لفقد الماء ثم وجد بعد الصلاة عليه بالتيمم غسل وصلي عليه ثانياً.
And after wudu, pour boiling water mixed with sidr (lotus leaves) or ushnan (a cleaning herb) not ground, for thorough cleaning. The Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded that his daughter and the muhrim whose mount broke his neck be washed with water and sidr. Otherwise (if not found), washing with pure water (al-qarrah) suffices, and it should be heated if possible, as it is more effective. Wash his head and the hair of his beard with khitmi (a fragrant Iraqi plant acting like soap). If not available, then soap. If there is no hair (on the body), do not bother for this. Then, after cleaning the hair and skin, lay the deceased on his left side and wash his right side, starting with the right because beginning with the right is sunnah, until water reaches what is next to the bier (the side). Then lay him on his right side and wash likewise until water reaches all his body. Then sit the deceased propped against something so he does not fall, and gently massage his belly to expel excrement. Whatever comes out, wash it clean only, and do not repeat the washing (ghusl) or wudu of the deceased because it does not invalidate his state. Then dry him with a cloth so that his shroud does not become wet. The intention in washing him is to discharge our duty; thus if a drowned person is found, he is moved in the water with the intention of washing him for this purpose, not for the validity of prayer because water is absent. Then if water is found after prayer with tayammum, they are washed and prayed over again.
Source pages p. 568

Commentary
This passage presents the detailed procedure for washing the deceased (ghusl al-mayyit) according to the Hanafi school. It begins with the water preparation: after wudu (performed by the washer), hot water boiled and mixed with sidr (lotus leaves) or ushnan (a type of soap herb) is poured over the body for cleansing. This is based on the Prophet's command for his daughter and the muhrim who died from his mount. If these are unavailable, pure water suffices, and heating it is recommended for better cleaning. Then the head and beard are washed with khitmi (a fragrant plant) or soap; if the deceased has no hair, this is not done. The body is then washed in order: first laid on the left side to wash the right side, then on the right side to wash the left, ensuring water reaches all parts. Beginning with the right is sunnah. After washing, the deceased is propped up and the belly is gently massaged to expel remains; any excrement is washed off without repeating the entire ghusl or wudu, as that does not break the deceased's state. Finally, the body is dried with a cloth to keep the shroud dry. The intention (niyyah) for washing is to fulfill the communal obligation (fard kifayah); therefore, if a drowned person is found, moving him in water with the intention of washing suffices even though water is already present. If tayammum was performed (due to lack of water) and later water is found, the deceased must be washed and the funeral prayer repeated. This passage emphasizes the practical steps and the legal reasoning (istihsan, qiyas) behind them.

Key Terms
سدر (sidr): Leaves of the lotus tree (Ziziphus spina-christi) used as a cleansing agent in ghusl al-mayyit.
خطمي (khitmi): A fragrant plant from Iraq used like soap for washing the hair and beard of the deceased.
قراح (qarrah): Pure water free from any mixture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi procedure for washing the deceased, what is the ruling if excrement emerges during the belly massage?
A) The entire ghusl must be repeated.
B) Only wash the soiled area and continue without repeating.
C) Abandon the washing and perform tayammum.
D) The deceased's wudu is broken and must be renewed.

Key Takeaway
The correct procedure for washing the deceased includes using sidr, starting with the right, and not repeating ghusl if excrement appears.

Procedure of Washing the Deceased
Sequential steps of ghusl al-mayyit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the sequential steps of ghusl al-mayyit according to the Hanafi school and identify the ruling for each act.

Core Idea
Washing the deceased is a fard kifayah; the sunnah procedure prioritizes the right side and uses a cleansing agent.

This lesson walks you through the practical steps of washing a deceased Muslim as prescribed in the Hanafi school. The procedure is both thorough and respectful, ensuring purification without unnecessary repetition. Understanding these steps is essential for fulfilling this collective obligation correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall ruling
Recognize that ghusl al-mayyit is fard kifayah (collective obligation) and that the described method is the sunnah (recommended).
The obligation is met by washing the entire body once; the sunnah adds extra acts.
2
Note the preparatory step
Observe that washing begins with the head and beard using a cleansing agent like khitmi (or soap if unavailable). If there is no hair, no special effort is made.
This ensures thorough cleaning of hair and skin.
3
Understand the washing order
The deceased is first laid on the left side to wash the right side, because beginning with the right is sunnah. Then laid on the right side to wash the left side, ensuring water reaches the entire body.
This order is based on the general sunnah of favoring the right.
4
Recognize post-wash handling
After washing, the deceased is seated supported, and the stomach is gently wiped to expel waste. Any discharge is washed off, but the ghusl is not repeated because impurities do not break the purity state of the deceased.
This avoids unnecessary repetition.
5
Final drying
The body is dried with a cloth to prevent the shroud from getting wet.
Practical consideration for burial preparations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن تيسر لأنه أبلغ في التنظيف ( ويغسل رأسه) أي شعر رأسه (و) شعر (لحيته بالخطمي) نبت بالعراق طيب الرائحة يعمل عمل الصابون في التنظيف وإن لم يكن فالصابون وإن لم یکن به شعر لا يتكلف لهذا (ثم) بعد تنظيف الشعر والبشرة (يضجع) الميت (على يساره فيغسل شقه الأيمن ابتداء لأن البداءة بالميامن سنة حتى يصل الماء إلى ما أي الجنب الذي (يلي) التخت بالخاء المعجمة (منه) أي الميت ( ثم) يضجع (على يمينه) فيغسل (كذلك) حتى يصل الماء إلى سائر جسده ثم أجلس الميت (مسنداً إليه) لئلا يسقط (ومسح بطنه) مسحاً رفيقاً ليخرج فضلاته (وما خرج منه غسله) فقط تنظيفاً (ولم يعد غسله) ولا وضؤه لأنه ليس بناقض في حقه ثم ينشف بثوب) كيلا تبتل أكفانه
If it is available because it is more thorough in cleaning. And he washes his head, meaning the hair of his head, and the hair of his beard with khitmi, a plant from Iraq with a pleasant fragrance that acts like soap in cleaning. If not available, then soap. If he has no hair, one does not go to trouble for this. Then after cleaning the hair and skin, the deceased is laid on his left side, and his right side is washed first because beginning with the right is sunnah, until water reaches what, meaning the side that is on the cot, from him, i.e., the deceased. Then he is laid on his right side and washed likewise until water reaches all parts of his body. Then the deceased is seated, supported to prevent falling, and his stomach is wiped gently to expel waste. Whatever comes out is washed only for cleaning, and he does not repeat the ghusl nor wudu because it is not a breaker in his case. Then he is dried with a cloth so that his shroud does not become wet.
Source pages p. 569

Commentary
This passage details the procedure for washing the deceased according to the Hanafi school. It begins with washing the head and beard using a cleansing agent like khitmi or soap. The body is washed on both sides starting with the right, following the sunnah of preferring the right side. After washing, the deceased is seated and the stomach is gently pressed to expel any remaining impurities. Any discharge is washed off, but the complete ghusl or wudu is not repeated as these discharges do not break the state of ritual purity for the deceased. The body is then dried to prevent the shrouds from getting wet. The ruling emphasizes that the washing is a collective obligation (fard kifayah) and the procedure is designed to be thorough yet gentle.

Key Terms
الخطمي (al-khitmi): A plant from Iraq used as a cleansing agent, like soap, for washing the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Start with the right side
B) Start with the left side
C) Wash both sides simultaneously
D) It does not matter

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi procedure for ghusl al-mayyit emphasizes thoroughness, respect, and following sunnah by beginning with the right side, using a cleansing agent, and not repeating ghusl for discharge.

The Intention and Rules for Washing a Drowned Person
Intra-Hanafi dispute on washing a drowned person and repetition of funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) on washing a drowned person and apply the ruling on repeating the funeral prayer after finding water.

Core Idea
Intention for washing the deceased fulfills the obligation; moving a drowned person in water counts as washing.

This lesson addresses two related issues: the necessity of intention when washing the deceased, and the specific rules for a drowned person. It presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding the number of times a drowned body should be moved or washed, and whether the funeral prayer must be repeated if water is found after tayammum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal purpose of intention
Recognize that the intention (niyyah) for washing the deceased is made to discharge the collective obligation (fard kifayah), not for the prayer of the deceased (since they do not pray).
2
Distinguish the positions on washing a drowned person
Compare Abu Yusuf's view (move three times in water) with Muhammad's view (if intention at removal, two washes suffice according to sunnah). Understand that the obligation is fulfilled by intention and movement.
The movement in water with intention constitutes actual washing in this context.
3
Analyze the repetition of prayer after finding water
Examine the disagreement: according to Abu Yusuf, the body must be washed and the prayer repeated; another narration from him says no repetition, analogous to a living person's tayammum. Muhammad's view aligns with no repetition.
The analogy to a junub (ritually impure person) performing tayammum and later finding water is used.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والنية في تغسيله لإسقاط الفرض عنا حتى إنه إذا وجد غريقاً يحرك في الماء بنية غسله لهذا لا لصحة الصلاة لفقد الماء ثم وجد بعد الصلاة عليه بالتيمم غسل وصلي عليه ثانياً، والمنتفخ عليه وإذا. يمم

قوله : ( يحرك في الماء) ثلاثاً في قول أبي يوسف كما في الفتح، وعن محمد: إن نوى الغسل عند الإخراج من الماء يغسل مرتين يعني على وجه السنة، والفرض قد سقط بالنية عند الإخراج قوله : (ثم وجد أي الماء. قوله : (وصلى عليه ثانياً) في قول أبي يوسف وعنه يغسل ولا تعاد الصلاة عليه كجنب تيمم ،وصلى ثم وجد الماء كما في البرهان.
The intention in washing him is to remove the obligation from us, such that if a drowned person is found, he is moved in the water with the intention of washing him for this reason, not for the validity of prayer due to the lack of water. Then if he finds (water) after praying over him with tayammum, he is washed and prayed over again. The bloated one... and if. He performs tayammum. He said: 'He moves in the water' three times according to Abu Yusuf, as in al-Fath. From Muhammad: if he intends ghusl at the time of removal from water, he washes twice, meaning according to the sunnah; the obligation has already been fulfilled by the intention at removal. He said: 'then he found' meaning water. He said: 'and prayed over again' according to Abu Yusuf, and from him: he is washed and the prayer is not repeated, like a junub who performed tayammum and prayed then found water, as in al-Burhan.
Source pages p. 569

Commentary
This passage discusses the intention (niyyah) required when washing the deceased. The intention is made to fulfill the communal obligation, not for the validity of the prayer (since the deceased is not praying). For a drowned person, moving the body in water with the intention of washing suffices for ghusl. There is a dispute between Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding how many times the person should be moved or washed. Abu Yusuf says three times, while Muhammad says if the intention is made at the moment of removal from water, two washes suffice. Additionally, if a body was prayed over with tayammum (due to no water), and then water is found later, the body must be washed and the prayer repeated according to Abu Yusuf. However, another narration from Abu Yusuf says the prayer is not repeated, similar to the case of a living person who performed tayammum and later found water. This reflects the Hanafi internal difference on the requirement of repetition.

Key Terms
النية (al-niyyah): The intention made by the washer to fulfill the collective obligation of washing the deceased.
الغريق (al-ghariq): A drowned person who is found dead.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Once
B) Twice
C) Three times
D) Until clean

Key Takeaway
The intention for ghusl of the deceased fulfills the obligation, and for a drowned person, moving in water with intention counts as washing, with a Hanafi internal difference on the number of moves and whether to repeat prayer after finding water.

Concealing Defects and Speaking About the Deceased
Ruling on concealing defects with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on concealing defects of the deceased and apply the hadith to determine when it is permissible to mention negative traits.

Core Idea
Concealing defects of the deceased is wajib; mentioning them is haram unless done to deter public sin.

After washing the deceased, the washer may observe certain features. This lesson clarifies the legal obligations regarding what to say or conceal about the deceased, supported by a prophetic hadith and scholarly commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Recognize that the ruling concerns speech about the deceased after washing.
2
Extract the general ruling
Determine that it is wajib to conceal defects and haram to mention bad qualities, except when the deceased was a public sinner.
3
Locate the dalil
The hadith 'اذكروا محاسن موتاكم وكفوا عن مساويهم' is the primary evidence.
The command 'كفوا' indicates prohibition.
4
Analyze the exception
If the deceased was an innovator or flagrant sinner, mentioning his faults is allowed as a deterrent.
This is based on the principle of blocking harm.
5
Understand the severity
Backbiting the deceased is more severe than backbiting the living because the deceased cannot seek forgiveness.
Quoted from Hujjat al-Islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستر ما لا ينبغي إظهاره) في الأزهار قال العلماء : فإذا رأي الغاسل من الميت ما يعجبه كاستنارة وجهه وطيب ريحه، رعة انقلابه على المغتسل استحب أن يتحدث به وإن رأى ما يكره كنتنه وسواد وجهه وبدنه ، أو انقلاب صورته حرم أن يتحدث به كذا في شرح المشكاة قيل : إلا أن يكون مبتدعاً يظهر البدعة أو مجاهراً بالفسق والظلم فيذكر ذلك زجراً لأمثاله كذا في ابن أمير حاج، وعن ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : واذكروا محاسن موتاكم وكفوا عن مساويهم أخرجه أبو داود والترمذي وصححه ابن حبان قال حجة الإسلام: غيبة الميت أشد من الحي لأن عفو الحي واستحلاله ممكن ومتوقع في الدنيا بخلاف الميت، وروى البيهقي في المعرفة والحاكم في المستدرك، وقال: على شرط مسلم من غسل ميتاً فكتم عليه غفر له أربعون كبيرة، ومن كفنه كساه الله من السندس والإستبرق ومن حفر له قبراً حتى يجنه فكأنما أسكنه حتى يبعث، وفي الجنائز لابن شاهين : يا علي غسل الموتى فإنه من غسل ميتاً غفر له سبعون مغفرة لو قسمت مغفرة منها على جميع الخلائق لوسعتهم قلت: ما يقول من يغسل قال : يقول : غفرانك يا رحمن حتى يفرغ من الغسل. قوله : ( ويكره أن يكون جنباً) وتغسيل الكافر أشد كراهة إلا إذا لم يوجد غيره ذاكراً في حق المسلم أو أنثى في حق المسلمة كما في ابن أمير حاج قوله : ( ويجعل الحنوط) بفتح الحاء المهملة ويقال له : الحناط بكسر الحاء. قوله: (مركب من أشياء طيبة ويدخل فيه المسك في قول الأكثر خلافاً لعطاء. قوله : (للرجال) فيكرهان لهم دون النساء اعتباراً بحال الحياة فجعلهما في كفن الرجال جهل كما في مسكناً
He conceals what should not be revealed. In al-Azhar, the scholars said: If the washer sees something pleasing from the deceased, like the brightness of his face or pleasant smell, or a change of appearance on the wash, it is recommended to talk about it. But if he sees something disliked, like stench or blackness of face or body, or change of form, it is prohibited to talk about it. Unless the deceased was an innovator who displays innovation or a flagrant sinner and oppressor, then mention it as a deterrent for others like him. Ibn Umar reported that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Mention the good qualities of your dead and refrain from mentioning their bad qualities.' It was reported by Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi and authenticated by Ibn Hibban. Hujjat al-Islam said: backbiting the deceased is more severe than the living because the living can forgive and seek forgiveness in this world, unlike the deceased. Al-Bayhaqi and al-Hakim reported that whoever washes a dead person and conceals (his defects) will have forty major sins forgiven. Whoever shrouds him, Allah will clothe him with silk. Whoever digs a grave for him until he hides him, it is as if he housed him until resurrection. In al-Jana'iz of Ibn Shahin: 'O Ali, wash the dead, for whoever washes a dead person will have seventy forgivenesses, one of which would suffice all creation.' I asked: What should the washer say? He said: Say 'Ghufranaka ya Rahman' until he finishes washing. He said: 'It is disliked that he be junub.' Washing a disbeliever is more disliked unless no one else is available, like a Muslim male or a Muslim female. He said: 'And he places the hanut' with a fatha on the ha, and it is also called hanat with a kasr. He said: 'A compound of pleasant things, and musk is included according to the majority, contrary to Ata. He said: 'For men,' so saffron and wars are disliked for men but not for women, considering the state of life. Placing them in the shroud of men is ignorance.
Source pages p. 570

Commentary
This passage covers important etiquettes and rulings after washing the deceased. It is obligatory to conceal any defects or unpleasant features of the deceased. If good features are seen, they may be mentioned, but bad features should be kept secret unless the person was a public sinner. A hadith encourages mentioning only the good qualities. There is a strong warning against backbiting the dead. The washer should recite 'Ghufranaka ya Rahman' (Your forgiveness, O Merciful) throughout. It is disliked for a person in a state of janabah to wash the deceased, and even more disliked to wash a disbeliever (unless necessary). After washing, the deceased is shrouded. The hanut (perfume) is applied to the head and beard. It should be a mixture of aromatic substances, including musk according to the majority. Saffron and wars (a type of plant dye) are disliked for men but not for women, based on the rule of applying perfume during life.

Key Terms
الحنوط (al-hanut): A mixture of aromatic substances applied to the head and beard of the deceased.
الجنب (al-junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on mentioning the bad qualities of a deceased person who was not a public sinner?
A) Mustahabb
B) Mubah
C) Haram
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
Concealing defects of the deceased is wajib; mentioning bad traits is generally haram, with an exception for public sinners as a deterrent.

Rulings on Washing the Deceased and the Washer's Dua
Rulings on the washer's state and dua

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on a junub washing the deceased, washing a disbeliever, and the recommended dua during washing.

Core Idea
A junub should not wash the deceased (makruh), and washing a disbeliever is more disliked; the washer should recite 'Ghufranaka ya Rahman'.

Washing the deceased is a communal obligation. Certain states of the washer affect the ruling. This lesson covers the dislike of a junub washing, the extreme dislike of washing a disbeliever unless necessary, and the recommended supplication during the ghusl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on junub
It is makruh for a person in a state of janabah to wash the deceased.
The washing is still valid if done.
2
Understand the ruling on washing a disbeliever
It is more disliked (ashad karaahah) for a Muslim to wash a disbeliever, unless no one else is available.
The permissibility is limited to necessity.
3
Learn the recommended dua
The washer should continuously say 'Ghufranaka ya Rahman' (Your forgiveness, O Merciful) until he finishes.
This is reported from the practice of the Companions.

Source Text

ويستر ما لا ينبغي إظهاره) في الأزهار قال العلماء : فإذا رأي الغاسل من الميت ما يعجبه كاستنارة وجهه وطيب ريحه، رعة انقلابه على المغتسل استحب أن يتحدث به وإن رأى ما يكره كنتنه وسواد وجهه وبدنه ، أو انقلاب صورته حرم أن يتحدث به كذا في شرح المشكاة قيل : إلا أن يكون مبتدعاً يظهر البدعة أو مجاهراً بالفسق والظلم فيذكر ذلك زجراً لأمثاله كذا في ابن أمير حاج، وعن ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : واذكروا محاسن موتاكم وكفوا عن مساويهم أخرجه أبو داود والترمذي وصححه ابن حبان قال حجة الإسلام: غيبة الميت أشد من الحي لأن عفو الحي واستحلاله ممكن ومتوقع في الدنيا بخلاف الميت، وروى البيهقي في المعرفة والحاكم في المستدرك، وقال: على شرط مسلم من غسل ميتاً فكتم عليه غفر له أربعون كبيرة، ومن كفنه كساه الله من السندس والإستبرق ومن حفر له قبراً حتى يجنه فكأنما أسكنه حتى يبعث، وفي الجنائز لابن شاهين : يا علي غسل الموتى فإنه من غسل ميتاً غفر له سبعون مغفرة لو قسمت مغفرة منها على جميع الخلائق لوسعتهم قلت: ما يقول من يغسل قال : يقول : غفرانك يا رحمن حتى يفرغ من الغسل. قوله : ( ويكره أن يكون جنباً) وتغسيل الكافر أشد كراهة إلا إذا لم يوجد غيره ذاكراً في حق المسلم أو أنثى في حق المسلمة كما في ابن أمير حاج قوله : ( ويجعل الحنوط) بفتح الحاء المهملة ويقال له : الحناط بكسر الحاء. قوله: (مركب من أشياء طيبة ويدخل فيه المسك في قول الأكثر خلافاً لعطاء. قوله : (للرجال) فيكرهان لهم دون النساء اعتباراً بحال الحياة فجعلهما في كفن الرجال جهل كما في مسكناً
He conceals what should not be revealed. In al-Azhar, the scholars said: If the washer sees something pleasing from the deceased, like the brightness of his face or pleasant smell, or a change of appearance on the wash, it is recommended to talk about it. But if he sees something disliked, like stench or blackness of face or body, or change of form, it is prohibited to talk about it. Unless the deceased was an innovator who displays innovation or a flagrant sinner and oppressor, then mention it as a deterrent for others like him. Ibn Umar reported that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Mention the good qualities of your dead and refrain from mentioning their bad qualities.' It was reported by Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi and authenticated by Ibn Hibban. Hujjat al-Islam said: backbiting the deceased is more severe than the living because the living can forgive and seek forgiveness in this world, unlike the deceased. Al-Bayhaqi and al-Hakim reported that whoever washes a dead person and conceals (his defects) will have forty major sins forgiven. Whoever shrouds him, Allah will clothe him with silk. Whoever digs a grave for him until he hides him, it is as if he housed him until resurrection. In al-Jana'iz of Ibn Shahin: 'O Ali, wash the dead, for whoever washes a dead person will have seventy forgivenesses, one of which would suffice all creation.' I asked: What should the washer say? He said: Say 'Ghufranaka ya Rahman' until he finishes washing. He said: 'It is disliked that he be junub.' Washing a disbeliever is more disliked unless no one else is available, like a Muslim male or a Muslim female. He said: 'And he places the hanut' with a fatha on the ha, and it is also called hanat with a kasr. He said: 'A compound of pleasant things, and musk is included according to the majority, contrary to Ata. He said: 'For men,' so saffron and wars are disliked for men but not for women, considering the state of life. Placing them in the shroud of men is ignorance.
Source pages p. 570

Commentary
This passage covers important etiquettes and rulings after washing the deceased. It is obligatory to conceal any defects or unpleasant features of the deceased. If good features are seen, they may be mentioned, but bad features should be kept secret unless the person was a public sinner. A hadith encourages mentioning only the good qualities. There is a strong warning against backbiting the dead. The washer should recite 'Ghufranaka ya Rahman' (Your forgiveness, O Merciful) throughout. It is disliked for a person in a state of janabah to wash the deceased, and even more disliked to wash a disbeliever (unless necessary). After washing, the deceased is shrouded. The hanut (perfume) is applied to the head and beard. It should be a mixture of aromatic substances, including musk according to the majority. Saffron and wars (a type of plant dye) are disliked for men but not for women, based on the rule of applying perfume during life.

Key Terms
الحنوط (al-hanut): A mixture of aromatic substances applied to the head and beard of the deceased.
الجنب (al-junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should the washer recite during the ghusl of the deceased?
A) Surah al-Fatiha
B) Ghufranaka ya Rahman
C) La ilaha illallah
D) Subhanallah

Key Takeaway
A junub washing the deceased is makruh but valid; washing a disbeliever is more disliked unless necessary; the washer repeatedly says 'Ghufranaka ya Rahman'.

The Hanut (Perfume) for the Deceased: Composition and Application
Ruling on hanut composition and application

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of hanut, the recommended ingredients, and the ruling regarding saffron and wars for men and women.

Core Idea
Hanut is a mixture of aromatic substances including musk; saffron and wars are disliked for men but allowed for women.

After washing and shrouding, the deceased is perfumed with hanut. This lesson defines hanut, specifies its composition (musk included according to the majority), and clarifies that saffron and wars are disliked for men but permissible for women, based on the rule of applying perfume during life.

Guided Path
1
Define hanut
Hanut is a compound of pleasant-smelling substances applied to the head and beard of the deceased.
It is called hanat as well.
2
Identify the agreed ingredient
Musk is included in the hanut according to the majority, unlike the opinion of Ata.
The minority view excludes musk.
3
Apply the rule for men vs women
Saffron and wars are disliked for men but not for women, considering the practice during life.
Placing them in the shroud of men is considered ignorance.

Placing Camphor on the Deceased's Prostration Points
Ruling on applying camphor to the deceased's sujood body parts with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on applying camphor to the deceased's prostration points and explain the evidence and the exception for a muhrim.

Core Idea
Camphor on the prostration points honors the deceased and repels worms; even a muhrim receives it because ihram ends at death.

In the Hanafi school, funeral rites include specific practices to honor the deceased. One such practice is the application of camphor to the seven points of prostration. This lesson examines the ruling, its evidence from the Companions' practice, and a key dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding a person who died in ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being done? The act is placing camphor on the deceased's prostration points. The ruling is sunnah (recommended), not obligatory.
The text states 'يجعل الكافور على مساجده' – it is a practice derived from the Companions.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? Narrations from Ali, Anas, Ibn Umar, and Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with them) show that they practiced this. This is the transmitted practice (athar) of the Salaf.
The proof is ahad (solitary) and considered zanni in transmission and meaning.
3
Trace the wisdom behind the ruling
Why is camphor specifically applied to these limbs? The text says 'to repel worms' and 'extra honor' because these limbs are used in prostration. This wisdom (hikma) explains the recommendation.
The rationale is preservation from decay and honoring the parts that humble themselves before Allah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf with Imam al-Shafi'i
Does the ruling apply to someone who died in ihram? The Hanafi school says yes, because ihram ends at death. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that a muhrim should not be perfumed after death, so camphor would be prohibited.
The practical difference (thamarah) is whether to apply camphor to a pilgrim who dies during Hajj/Umrah.
5
Examine the commentary expansion
Later Hanafi scholars like al-Shumni, al-Siraj, and al-Qahstani expand on the method: after shrouding, camphor is placed on the prostration points, and also on the head, beard, and body. They also discuss herbs like wars and turmeric.
This shows the depth of the school's practical jurisprudence (fiqh al-‘amal).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
روي ذلك عن علي، وأنس وابن عمر رضي الله تعالى عنهم (و) يجعل (الكافور على مساجده) سواء فيه المحرم، وغيره فيطيب ويغطى رأسه ليطرد الدود عنها، وهي الجبهة، وأنفه ويداه وركبتاه وقدماه روي ذلك عن ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه فتخص بزيادة إكرام الشمني والسراج وغيرهما، والورس الكركم قوله على رأسه ولحيته) وسائر جسده كما في الجوهرة بعد أن يوضع على الإزار كما في القهستاني قوله : ( ويجعل الكافور) هو شجر عظيم بالهند، والصين قهستاني قوله : (سواء فيه المحرم وغيره لأن الإحرام ينقطع بالموت عندنا خلافاً للشافعي . قوله : (ليطرد الدود عنها هذه حكمة تخصيص الكافور وهو علة لقوله : ويجعل الكافور على مساجده قوله: فتخص بزيادة إكرام أي لما كانت هذه الأعضاء يسجد بها خصت بزيادة إكرام صيانة لها عن سرعة الفساد
It is narrated from Ali, Anas, and Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them) that camphor is placed on his prostration points, whether he is in ihram or not, and he is perfumed and his head is covered to repel worms; they are the forehead, nose, hands, knees, and feet. This is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him), so they are specified with extra respect. [Commentary from al-Shumni, al-Siraj, etc.: the word 'on his head and beard' and the rest of his body as in al-Jawhara after placing on the shroud as in al-Qahstani. He said: 'and he places camphor'—it is a great tree in India and China. Al-Qahstani said: 'whether he is in ihram or not' because ihram ends at death according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i. He said: 'to repel worms'—this is the wisdom of specifying camphor, and it is the rationale for placing camphor on his prostration points. He said: 'so they are specified with extra respect'—because these limbs are used for prostration, they are singled out for extra honor to preserve them from rapid decay.
Source pages p. 571

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that camphor is applied to the deceased's prostration points (forehead, nose, hands, knees, feet). It is based on narrations from several Companions. The ruling applies equally to one who died in ihram and one who did not, because ihram ends at death (Hanafi view, contrary to Shafi'i). The wisdom is to repel worms and honor these parts. The commentary expands on the herbs used (wars, turmeric) and the method of placement after shrouding. It emphasizes the special respect for the prostration limbs.

Key Terms
مساجده (masajidihi): The seven points of the body that touch the ground during prostration: the forehead, nose, hands, knees, and feet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many prostration points are specified for placing camphor on the deceased?
A) 4
B) 7
C) 10
D) 6

Key Takeaway
Applying camphor to the seven prostration points is a sunnah practice for the deceased, supported by Companion narrations, and applies equally to those who die in ihram.

Cutting the Deceased's Nails and Hair: Prohibition and Exception
Ruling that the deceased's nails and hair should not be cut, with exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cutting the deceased's nails and hair, explain the exception for a broken nail, and compare the Hanafi position with the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Do not beautify the dead: the deceased's nails and hair are left uncut unless broken.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on grooming the deceased. While preparing the body, one might wonder about cutting nails or trimming hair. The source clarifies that such acts are prohibitively disliked except for a broken nail. It also contrasts the Hanafi view with that of Imam al-Shafi'i, who permits trimming for cleanliness.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the act (cutting nails, hair, combing) and the ruling (makruh tahrimi). Note that the source states 'لا يقص' and 'لا يسرح'.
The prohibition is based on the principle that these acts are for adornment and the deceased no longer needs adornment.
2
Identify the exception
Find the exception: if the nail is broken (مكسور), it may be removed and discarded. This is narrated from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
The exception is specific to a broken nail; other situations follow the general prohibition.
3
Follow the opponent's view
Imam al-Shafi'i permits cutting the mustache, nails, and removing excess hair for cleanliness. Understand his reasoning: cleanliness (nadhafah) is praiseworthy for both living and dead.
This contrasts with the Hanafi focus on beautification.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school counters that cleanliness is achieved through washing, not cutting. Cutting is a form of beautification, which is inappropriate after death.
Therefore, the Hanafi ruling is more restrictive.
5
Determine the practical difference
Summarize the thamarah al-khilaf: in the Hanafi school, cutting nails/hair is makruh tahrimi and clippings go in the shroud; in the Shafi'i school, it is permissible or recommended.
This affects how funeral directors and families handle the deceased in real practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يقص ظفره) أي الميت (و) لا (شعره ولا يسرح شعره أي شعر رأسه ولحيته) لأنه للزينة وقد استغنى عنها قوله: (ولا يقص ظفره) إلا أن يكون مكسوراً فلا بأس بأخذه، ورميه روي ذلك عن الإمام والثاني كما في البحر وغيره وفي القهستاني عن العتابية، فلو قطع شعره أو ظفره أدرج معه في الكفن، وقال الإمام الشافعي رضي الله عنه : يقص شاربه وظفره ويزال من شعره ما حفه لإزالة كذا في مسكين قوله : (ولا يسرح (شعره ظاهر القنية أنها تحريمية حيث قال: إما لتزيين بعد موتها والامتشاط وقطع الشعر فلا يجوز نهر قوله : ( ولحيته) إنما ذكرها بعد الشعر لعدم تبادر الذهن عند إطلاق الشعر إليها لكونها مخصوصة باسم أو من عطف الخاص على العام
And he does not cut his nail—meaning the deceased—and no, his hair, and he does not comb his hair, i.e., the hair of his head and beard, because it is for adornment and he has no need for it. He said: (and he does not cut his nail) unless it is broken, then there is no harm in removing and discarding it. That is narrated from the Imam and the second (Abu Yusuf) as in al-Bahr and elsewhere, and in al-Qahstani from al-Atabiyya. If he cuts his hair or nail, it is placed with him in the shroud. Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah be pleased with him) said: he trims his mustache, cuts his nail, and removes excess hair for cleanliness, as in Miskin. He said: (and he does not comb his hair) – the apparent from al-Qunyah is that it is prohibitively disliked, as he said: either for beautification after her death, and combing and cutting hair is not permissible, as stated in Nahr. He said: (and his beard) – it is mentioned after hair because the mind does not immediately jump to it when 'hair' is mentioned, as it has a specific name, or it is a case of mentioning the specific after the general.
Source pages p. 571

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling that the deceased's nails, hair (head and beard) are not to be cut or combed, as these acts are for adornment and the deceased has no need. An exception is made for a broken nail, which may be removed. If cutting does occur, the clippings are placed in the shroud. The commentary notes that according to al-Qunyah, it is makruh tahrimi. Imam al-Shafi'i differs, permitting trimming for cleanliness. The Hanafi school bases its position on the principle that the deceased should not be beautified.

Key Terms
تحريمية (tahrimiyyah): A term used in al-Qunyah indicating that an act is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on cutting the deceased's nails?
A) Permitted unconditionally
B) Makruh tahrimi, except if the nail is broken
C) Sunnah to cut them
D) Not mentioned

Key Takeaway
The deceased's nails and hair are not to be cut except for a broken nail, as these acts are beautification, and the Hanafi school prohibits beautification of the dead.

Woman Washing Her Deceased Husband
Ruling with proof on a wife washing her deceased husband, with conditions and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a wife washing her deceased husband and identify the conditions that affect this permissibility.

Core Idea
A wife may wash her deceased husband even during iddah from a revocable divorce, as the marriage bond persists until the iddah ends.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi clarifies the Hanafi position on a delicate matter: who may perform the ritual washing of a deceased husband. While the general rule is that a spouse may wash the other, certain marital statuses affect the permissibility. The text provides the ruling, details exceptions, and supports it with prophetic practice and Companion precedent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Is it obligatory or recommended? The wife washing her deceased husband is a sunnah act, not fard.
The text says 'the woman washes her husband', indicating permissibility.
2
List the conditions for permissibility
Which marital states allow the wife to wash? The text mentions she can do so even if in iddah from raj'i or dhihar, and until she becomes ba'in or the iddah ends.
Specifically, a ba'in woman cannot wash him.
3
Examine the exceptions and disputes
What about a wife who is mazhar (li'an)? The text notes two narrations; the more apparent view according to the commentary is that she cannot wash him.
Also, if she gives birth and iddah ends, the permission ceases.
4
Analyze the dalil
What evidence supports the ruling? The hadith of Aisha that only the Prophet's wives washed him, and the practice of Abu Bakr and Abu Ayyub.
The marriage bond continues after death until the iddah expires.
5
Understand the legal rationale (ta'lil)
Why does the marriage continue post-death? Because the permission for washing is derived from the marriage contract, which persists in effect until iddah ends.
This explains why a ba'in woman cannot wash him.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والمرأة تغسل زوجها ولو معتدة من رجعي أو ظهار منها في الأظهر أو إلى ما لا يحل مسه، والنظر إليه ببقاء العدة فلو ولدت عقب موته وانقضت عدتها من رجعي أو كانت مبانة، أو قوله: (ولو معتمدة من رجعي) أي ولو كانت المرأة معتدة من رجعي فإن معتدته زوجة يحل قربانها ومحترزة صرح به الشرح .بعد قوله أو ظهار منها في الأظهر) الأولى أن يقول، ولو مظاهراً منها في الأظهر وهذا ينافي ما قاله في الشرح، وفي المظاهر منها روايتان الأظهر أن لا يحل لها تغسيله، فجعل الأظهر عدم الحل قوله : (أو) إلى ما لا يحل مسه، والنظر إليه ببقاء العدة) لعل في العبارة تحريفاً من الناسخ وصوابها وإيلاء لحل مسه، والنظر إليه ببقاء العدة. قال في الشرح والإيلاء لا يحرم وطئها فتغسله ا هـ فهذا يقتضي التعليل لقوله تغسله فتأمل . قوله : (فلو (ولدت أي امرأته التي توفي عنها هو محترز قوله : معتدة قوله : (أو كانت مبانة محترز قوله : ولو معتدة من رجعي. قوله : (أو رضاع) بأن أرضعت ضرتها الصغيرة. قوله : (أو صهرية) كان مست ،ابنه، أو أباه بشهوة، والأصل في تغسيل الزوجة زوجها ما روي عن عائشة رضي الله عنها أنها قالت: واستقبلنا من أمرنا ما استدبرنا ما غسل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلا نساؤه، ومعنى ذلك أنها لم تكن عالمة وقت وفاة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلمل بإباحة غسل و المرأة زوجها، ثم عملت بعد ذلك، وروي أن أبا بكر الصديق الله تعالى عنه أوصى إلى امرأته أسماء بنت عميس أنها تغسله بعد وفاته، وهكذا فعل أبو الأشعري رضي الله عنه، ولأن إباحة الغسل مستفادة بالنكاح فتبقى ما بقي النكاح والنكاح باقي بعد الموت إلى انقضاء العدة
And the woman washes her husband even if she is in iddah from a raj'i (revocable) divorce or from dhihar (in the most apparent view) or until such time as touching her is not permissible and looking at her due to the remaining iddah. If she gives birth immediately after his death and her iddah from raj'i ends, or if she is ba'in (irrevocably divorced) ... Commentary: (even if she is in iddah from raj'i) meaning even if the woman is in iddah from a raj'i divorce, for a woman in iddah from raj'i is still a wife whose intimacy is permissible and she is a mahram, stated by the sharh. After the statement 'or dhihar from her in the most apparent' – it would be better to say 'or if he had made dhihar from her in the most apparent', and this contradicts what was said in the sharh. Regarding the mazhar (li'an), there are two narrations; the most apparent is that she cannot wash him, so the 'most apparent' is not permissibility. In the text 'or until what does not permit touching and looking due to remaining iddah' – perhaps there is corruption from the copyist; the correct is 'or ila (oath of abstention) does not forbid her touching and looking due to remaining iddah.' The sharh said: ila does not forbid intercourse, so she washes him. This implies the rationale for the ruling. The original basis for a wife washing her husband is narrated from Aisha (ra) that she said: ‘We encountered in our matter what we did not expect; no one washed the Messenger of Allah (saw) except his wives.’ The meaning is that she was not aware at the time of the Prophet's death that it was permissible for a woman to wash her husband, but later she acted upon it. It is also narrated that Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (ra) advised his wife Asma bint Umays to wash him after his death, and Abu Ayyub (ra) did the same. And because the permission for washing is derived from marriage, it remains as long as the marriage remains, and marriage remains after death until the end of the iddah period.
Source pages p. 571

Commentary
This passage establishes the Hanafi ruling that a woman may wash her deceased husband. The permissibility extends to a wife who is in iddah from a revocable divorce or from dhihar, as she is still considered a wife. It also discusses the case of a wife who gives birth after her husband's death (ending iddah) and clarifies that if she becomes ba'in (e.g., through divorce before death), she cannot wash him. The commentary corrects a textual corruption regarding 'ila' (oath of abstention). The proof is from the hadith of Aisha that only the Prophet's wives washed him, and from the practice of Abu Bakr and Abu Ayyub. The legal principle is that the marital bond continues after death until the iddah period expires.

Key Terms
معتدة من رجعي (mu'taddah min raj'i): A woman in the waiting period after a revocable divorce; she is still legally considered a wife.

Washing of Spouses: Wife Washes Husband, Husband Does Not
Inter-madhhab dispute on husband washing wife

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a husband washing his deceased wife, identify the evidence from hadith and practice, and evaluate the opposing position of the three other imams.

Core Idea
Marriage ends at death, so a husband is a non-mahram and cannot wash his wife.

One of the most emotionally charged moments in funeral rites is deciding who may wash the deceased. For spouses, the Hanafi school draws a sharp distinction: a wife may wash her husband, but a husband may not wash his wife. In this lesson, we examine the reasoning behind this rule and the inter-madhhab dispute that arises from the famous incident of Ali washing Fatima.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling: the wife may wash her husband (mubah), but the husband may not wash his wife (haram). Note the exceptions for fosterage and affinity.
The wife's permissibility is based on the marriage tie continuing after death until the end of iddah.
2
Identify the opponent and their proof
The three other imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) hold that the husband may wash his wife. They rely on the report that Ali (ra) washed Fatima (ra).
This is a well-known ikhtilaf based on a single hadith.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the opposing proof
The Hanafi response argues that the report is not authentic (Umm Ayman washed Fatima), or if authentic, it is specific to Fatima due to her unique status as the daughter of the Prophet and his statement about her being Ali's wife in the Hereafter.
The hadith 'every cause and lineage is cut off except mine' supports the general rule but allows exception for the Prophet's family.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
The practical consequence: in a Hanafi setting, a widower cannot wash his wife; if no woman is available, tayammum is performed. In other madhhabs, the widower may wash her if no other mahram woman is present.
This affects funeral arrangements and who should be called.
5
Apply the rule to related cases
The same logic extends to slave women (umm walad, mudabbara, qinn) who cannot wash their master. Also, if a woman dies among non-mahram men, tayammum is performed wrapped in cloth.
The principle of avoiding direct contact between non-mahrams is consistently applied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حرمت بردة أو رضاع، أو صهرية لا تغسله (بخلافه) أي الرجل فإنه لا يغسل زوجته لانقطاع النكاح وإذا لم توجد امرأة لتغسيلها ييممها، وليس عليه غض بصره عن ذراعيها بخلاف الأجنبي وهو (كأم الولد والمدبرة والقنة (لا تغسل سيدها) وتيممه بخرقة (ولو ماتت امرأة مع الرجال المحارم وغيرهم (يمموها (كعكسه) وهو موت رجل بين وكن محارمه ييممنه (بخرقة) تلف على يد الميمم الأجنبي حتى يمس الجسد، ويغض يقتضي التعليل لقوله تغسله فتأمل . قوله : (فلو (ولدت أي امرأته التي توفي عنها هو محترز قوله : معتدة قوله : (أو كانت مبانة محترز قوله : ولو معتدة من رجعي. قوله : (أو رضاع) بأن أرضعت ضرتها الصغيرة. قوله : (أو صهرية) كان مست ،ابنه، أو أباه بشهوة، والأصل في تغسيل الزوجة زوجها ما روي عن عائشة رضي الله عنها أنها قالت: واستقبلنا من أمرنا ما استدبرنا ما غسل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلا نساؤه، ومعنى ذلك أنها لم تكن عالمة وقت وفاة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بإباحة غسل المرأة زوجها، ثم عملت بعد ذلك، وروي أن أبا بكر الصديق الله تعالى عنه أوصى إلى امرأته أسماء بنت عميس أنها تغسله بعد وفاته، وهكذا فعل أبو موسى الأشعري رضي الله عنه، ولأن إباحة الغسل مستفادة بالنكاح فتبقى ما بقي النكاح والنكاح باقي بعد الموت إلى انقضاء العدة قوله : (فإنه لا يغسل زوجته) وكذا لا يمسها ولا يمنع من النظر إليها في الأصح تنوير قوله : (لانقطاع النكاح) بانعدام محله فصار الزوج أجنبياً واعتبر بملك اليمين حيث لا ينتفي عن المحل بموت المالك، ويبطل بموت المحل فكذا هذا، وقالت الأئمة الثلاثة يجوز لأن علياً غسل فاطمة رضي الله عنها قلنا : وروى أنها غسلتها أم أيمن ولو ثبت أن علياً غسلها فهو محمول على بقاء الزوجية لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «كل سبب، ونسب ينقطع بالموت إلا سببي ونسبي مع أن ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه أنكر عليه، فقال له : أما علمت أن رسول الله قال : إنّ فاطمة زوجتك في الدنيا والآخرة فدعواه الخصوصية دليل على أنه كان معروفاً بينهم أنّ الرجل لا يغسل زوجته .
A woman forbidden due to fosterage or affinity does not wash him. (Contrary to him) i.e., the man, for he does not wash his wife because the marriage tie is severed. And if no woman is found to wash her, she is given tayammum. And he is not required to lower his gaze from her forearms unlike a non-mahram. And it (i.e., the ruling) is like the umm al-walad, mudabbara, and qinn: they do not wash their master, and they perform tayammum for him with a cloth. If a woman dies among men who are mahrams and others, they perform tayammum for her, and the reverse: if a man dies among his mahram women, they perform tayammum for him with a cloth wrapped on the hand of the non-mahram performer so that it touches the body. The commentary: 'This necessitates the reasoning for his saying "she washes him" so consider. His saying: 'or she gave birth' i.e., his wife who died is the exclusion of his saying 'observing iddah'. His saying: 'or she is divorced irrevocably' is the exclusion of his saying 'even if observing iddah from a revocable divorce'. His saying: 'or fosterage' such as her breastfeeding the small co-wife. His saying: 'or affinity' such as the masturbation of his son or father with desire. The basis for a wife washing her husband is what was narrated from Aisha that she said: 'We came upon what we had not known before; the Messenger of God was washed only by his wives.' The meaning is that she was not aware at the time of the Prophet's death of the permissibility of a woman washing her husband, then she acted upon that later. And it was narrated that Abu Bakr al-Siddiq advised his wife Asma bint Umays to wash him after his death, and similarly Abu Musa al-Ash'ari did. And because the permissibility of washing is derived from the marriage, so it remains as long as the marriage remains, and the marriage remains after death until the end of the iddah. His saying: 'for he does not wash his wife' and similarly he does not touch her nor is he prevented from looking at her according to the soundest view. His saying: 'because the marriage tie is severed' due to the absence of its subject, so the husband becomes a non-mahram, and it is analogized to ownership of the right hand: it does not cease from the subject due to the death of the owner, but becomes void due to the death of the subject; likewise this. The three imams said it is permissible because Ali washed Fatima. We say: it was narrated that Umm Ayman washed her, and if it is established that Ali washed her, it is interpreted as due to the continuation of marriage because of the Prophet's saying: 'Every cause and lineage is cut off by death except my cause and my lineage.' And Ibn Mas'ud objected to him, saying: 'Do you not know that the Messenger of God said: Fatima is your wife in this world and the Hereafter?' Thus his claim of specificity is evidence that it was known among them that a man does not wash his wife.
Source pages p. 572

Commentary
This passage from al-Tahtawi's hashya comments on the ruling of spouses washing each other after death. It begins with the matn stating that a woman who is forbidden to her husband due to fosterage or affinity cannot wash him. It then contrasts with the husband: a man does not wash his wife because the marriage tie is severed. The commentary expands: the wife can wash her husband because the marriage contract persists after death until the end of the iddah, citing the practice of the Prophet being washed by his wives and the examples of Abu Bakr and Abu Musa. For the husband not washing his wife, the reasoning is that death eliminates the subject of the marriage, making the husband a non-mahram. The three imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) argue that the husband can wash his wife based on Ali washing Fatima. The Hanafi response is that the report is not authenticated, or it is specific to Fatima due to her unique status. The hadith 'every cause and lineage is cut off except mine' and Ibn Mas'ud's objection confirm the general rule that a husband does not wash his wife.

Key Terms
محرم (mahram): A person who is permanently forbidden in marriage due to blood, fosterage, or affinity. Here, a husband becomes non-mahram after death.
تغسيل (taghsīl): The ritual washing of the deceased body prior to burial.
عدة (iddah): The waiting period for a widow after her husband's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the marriage ends at death
B) Because it is not sunnah
C) Because it is makruh tanzihi
D) Because the wife's body is sacred

Key Takeaway
A wife may wash her deceased husband because marriage ties persist after death until iddah ends, but a husband may not wash his wife because the marriage tie is severed at death.

Tayammum for the Deceased: Non-Mahram and Mahram Rulings
Details conditions for tayammum on a deceased woman among men and the role of mahram vs. non-mahram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on tayammum for a deceased woman, distinguishing between mahram and non-mahram, and identify exceptions for slave women, children, and the hermaphrodite.

Core Idea
A non-mahram must use a cloth barrier for tayammum; a mahram may do without — but both must avoid desire.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah clarifies the conditions for performing tayammum on a deceased woman when only non-mahram men are present. It distinguishes the roles of mahram and non-mahram, and addresses special cases like slave women, children, hermaphrodites, and eunuchs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
What is the default rule for tayammum on a deceased woman among non-mahram men? The non-mahram must wrap his hand in a cloth to avoid direct contact.
This is based on the principle of avoiding touching the awrah of a non-mahram.
2
Distinguish mahram from non-mahram
How does the ruling change if a mahram relative is present? A mahram may perform tayammum without a cloth, as it is permissible to touch the limbs used in tayammum without desire.
Mahram includes those whom one cannot marry permanently, such as father, son, brother.
3
Examine exceptions
What exceptions exist for slave women, children, the hermaphrodite, and the eunuch? Slave women (umm al-walad, mudabbara, qinn) do not require a barrier for the non-mahram. Children who have not reached desire can be washed directly. The hermaphrodite (khuntha mushkil) is given tayammum. The eunuch (majbub) is treated as a normal man.
These exceptions arise from the absence of awrah ruling or the absence of mahram relationship.
4
Note the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf disliked that a non-mahram wash a child who has not reached desire, but the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is permissibility because the child's body parts are not awrah.
This is a legitimate difference within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ييممها) أي زوجها. قوله: (بخلاف الأجنبي) أي فإنه يلف يده بخرقة وييممها كف بصره عن ذراعيها إلا أن تكون أمة مع فلا تحتاج إلى حائل قوله : (وهو) كأم الولد لا تغسله ولا يغسلها، وكذا المكاتبة لزوال الأمة، والمكاتبة إلى الورثة وبطلانه في أم الولد والمدبرة لعتقهما بالموت، فإن قيل أم الولد تعتد منه فينبغي أن تلحق بالزوجة قلنا : عدتها لم تجب قضاء لحقه، بل للتعرف عن براءة الرحم فإن قيل هلا اكتفى بحيضة كما في استبراء الأمة قلنا عدة أم الولد وجبت بزوال الفراش فأشبهت عدة النكاح قوله : (المحارم) الأولى حذفه للتصريح به في قوله: بعد وأن وجد ذو رحم محرم قوله : (يمموها) فعل ماض وفي نسخة بالمضارع، والمناسب عليها إثبات النون. قوله: (وكن (محارمه الأولى غير محارمه قوله : (بخرقة) راجع إلى الصورتين إلا أن تكون المرأة أمة فلا تحتاج إلى حائل. بصره عن ذراعي المرأة ولو عجوزاً وإن وجد ذو رحم محرم يمم) الميت ذكراً كان أو أنثى (بلا خرقة) لجواز مس أعضاء التيمم للمحرم ، بلا شهوة كالنظر إليها منها له (وكذا الخنثى المشكل ييمم في ظاهر الرواية وقيل : يجعل في قميص لا يمنع وصول الماء إليه (ويجوز للرجل والمرأة تغسيل صبي وصبية لم يشتهيا لأنه ليس لأعضائهما حكم العورة وعن أبي يوسف أنه قال : أكره أن يغسلهما الأجنبي، والمجبوب كالفحل قوله : (والمجبوب كالفحل) فليس له تغسيل امرأة أجنبية إلا أن تكون من محارمه فييممها بخرقة قاله السيد أي، ولا يعطي حكم بسبب الجب، وكذا إذا مات النساء بين أما بخرقة أو دونها على التفصيل، وكذا له أن يغسل الصبي والصبية اللذين لم يشتهيا، فالحاصل أنه في حكم الرجال من كل وجه .
His saying: 'they perform tayammum for her' i.e., her husband. His saying: 'contrary to the non-mahram' i.e., he wraps his hand in a cloth and performs tayammum for her, restraining his gaze from her forearms, except if she is a slave woman then no barrier is needed. His saying: 'and it (the ruling) is like umm al-walad' does not wash him nor he wash her, and likewise the mukatabah due to the removal of slavery, and the mukataabah to the heirs and its invalidity in umm al-walad and mudabbara due to their emancipation upon death. If it is said: umm al-walad observes iddah from him, so she should be like a wife, we say: her iddah is not obligatory to fulfill his right, but to ascertain the emptiness of the womb. If it is said: why not suffice with one menstrual period like the istibra' of a slave woman, we say: the iddah of umm al-walad becomes obligatory due to the removal of the bed, so it resembles the iddah of marriage. His saying: 'the mahrams' – it would be better to omit it due to the explicit mention in his saying after: 'and if a mahram relative is found'. His saying: 'they performed tayammum' is past tense, and in a copy in the present tense, and the appropriate is to add the nun. His saying: 'and they were his mahrams' – the first is not his mahrams. His saying: 'with a cloth' refers to both cases except if the woman is a slave then no barrier is needed. He restrains his gaze from the woman's forearms even if she is old. And if a mahram relative is found, he performs tayammum for the deceased, male or female, without a cloth, because it is permissible for the mahram to touch the parts of tayammum without desire, like looking at them. Similarly, the hermaphrodite is given tayammum in the apparent narration, and it is said: he is placed in a shirt that does not prevent water from reaching him. It is permissible for a man and woman to wash a boy and girl who have not reached the age of desire, because their body parts do not have the ruling of awrah. Abu Yusuf said: I dislike that a non-mahram wash them. The eunuch is like a normal man. His saying: 'the eunuch is like a normal man' – so he may not wash a non-mahram woman except if she is from his mahrams, then he performs tayammum for her with a cloth, as the master said. He is not given a ruling due to castration. Similarly, if women die among men, either with a cloth or without according to the detail. Likewise, he may wash a boy and girl who have not reached desire. So the result is that he is under the ruling of men in every respect.
Source pages p. 572

Commentary
This passage from al-Tahtawi's hashya explains the rules of tayammum for the deceased when a female is among non-mahram men. The matn states that if no woman is available, she is given tayammum. The commentary elaborates: the non-mahram must wrap his hand in a cloth and avoid looking at her forearms, unless she is a slave woman. For a mahram relative, tayammum can be performed without a cloth, as it is permissible for them to touch the body parts of tayammum without desire. The passage also discusses slave women (umm al-walad, mudabbara, qinn) who do not wash their master and vice versa, with reasoning about the iddah of umm al-walad. Then it addresses the hermaphrodite (khuntha mushkil) who should be given tayammum in the apparent narration. Regarding children, it is permissible for an adult to wash a boy or girl who has not reached the age of desire, as their body parts are not considered awrah; however, Abu Yusuf dislikes it for non-mahrams. The eunuch (majbub) is treated as a normal man in these rulings.

Key Terms
أم الولد (umm al-walad): A slave woman who has borne a child to her master, who becomes free upon his death.
مدبرة (mudabbara): A slave woman whose master has declared she will be free after his death.
خنثى مشكل (khuntha mushkil): A hermaphrodite whose gender is unclear; in this context, they are treated as needing tayammum to avoid direct contact.
مجبوب (majbub): A man who has been castrated, but retains the rulings of a normal man regarding washing others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) With a barrier cloth
B) Without a barrier
C) Only if no woman is available
D) Not at all

Key Takeaway
Tayammum for a deceased woman requires a cloth barrier for non-mahram and is done without barrier by a mahram, with exceptions for slave women and children.

Kissing the Deceased and the Husband's Obligation to Shroud His Wife
Rulings on kissing the deceased and husband's duty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kissing the deceased and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether a husband must shroud his wealthy wife.

Core Idea
Kissing the deceased is allowed for love and blessing, but the husband's duty to shroud his wife sparks an intra-Hanafi debate.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi addresses two distinct funeral-related rulings: the permissibility of kissing the deceased and the scope of a husband's obligation to prepare his wife's body. The first is settled by explicit sunna; the second reveals a nuanced ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school, with Abu Yusuf offering two views. Understanding the conditions and the preferred view (mufta bihi) is essential for proper practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Read the passage and note that it begins with kissing the deceased (taqbil al-mayyit) and then shifts to the husband's duty (tajhiz al-zawj li-zawjatihi).
Both are part of janaza (funeral) fiqh.
2
Analyze the ruling on kissing
Extract the condition: permissible (la ba's) if done for love (mahabbah) and seeking blessings (tabarruk) as a farewell, free from any prohibited intent. If done for lust (shahwah), it becomes haram.
The hadith of Abu Bakr kissing the Prophet and the Prophet kissing Uthman ibn Maz'un serve as evidence.
3
Examine the dispute on husband's obligation
The passage presents two views attributed to Abu Yusuf: (1) obligation only if the wife is poor (mu`sirah), and (2) obligation absolutely (mutlaqan), even if the husband is poor.
The second view is chosen by later authorities (al-Mughni, al-Muhit, al-Zahiriya) and is the mufta bihi.
4
Understand the arguments
The first view analogizes shrouding to maintenance (nafaqa) which is due only to a poor wife. The second view emphasizes the marriage bond as a general responsibility not conditional on poverty.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf based on different weightings of analogy vs. general principle.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
Conclude that in fatwa, the husband must shroud and bury his wife regardless of her wealth, and kissing the deceased is permissible only with the correct intention.
The condition (free from lust) applies even to spouses because marriage ends at death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بأس بتقبيل الميت للمحبة والتبرك توديعاً خالصة عن محظور وعلى الرجل تجهيز (مرأته أي تكفينها ودفنها عند أبي يوسف لو كانت معسرة، وهذا التخصيص مختار صاحب المغني والمحيط والظهيرية انتهى ويلزمه أبو يوسف بالتجهيز مطلقاً أي (ولو) كان الزوج (معسراً) وهي قوله : لما روي البخاري عن عائشة رضي الله عنها قالت: أقبل أبو بكر على فرسه من مسكنه بالسنح حتى نزل، فدخل المسجد، فلم يكلم الناس حتى دخل على عائشة، فتيمم النبي ، وهو مسجى ببرد حبرة فكشف عن وجهه، ثم أكب عليه فقيله، ثم بكى، ولم يفعل ذلك إلا قدوة به لما روى أبو داود والترمذي وابن ماجه، والحاكم مصححاً رضي الله عنها أن رسول الله دخل على عثمان بن مظعون، وهو ميت فأكب عليه، وقبله، ثم بكى حتى رأيت الدموع تسيل على وجنتيه وفي التمهيد لما توفي عثمان كشف النبي الثوب عن وجهه وبكى بكاء طويلاً، وقبل بين عينيه فلما رفع على السرير قال: طوبى لك يا عثمان لم تلبسك الدنيا ولم تلبسها» ا هـ . قوله: (والتبرك) الواو بمعنى فإن تقبيله عثمان للمحبة، وتقبيل أبي بكر الرسول الأكرم ل لهما معاً. قوله: (خالصة عن محظور) هذا قيد في الجواز أما إذا كانت لشهوة فحرام ولو زوجة فيما يظهر لقولهم أن النكاح انقطع بموتها لذهاب محله قوله : ( ودفنها) أي مؤنته أن لم يتبرع به قوله : (لو كانت معسرة) هذا أحد وجهين لأبي يوسف والأولى تأخيره عن قوله، ولو معسراً، ويجعله مقابلاً له. قوله : (وهذا التخصيص) أي تخصيص وجوب التجهيز على الزوج بما إذا كانت معسرة. قوله : (ويلزمه أبو يوسف) في نسخة بأو، وهي لحكاية الخلاف عن أبي يوسف، وهي الصواب قال
There is no harm in kissing the deceased for love and seeking blessings as a farewell, free from prohibition. And upon the husband is the preparation of his wife, i.e., shrouding and burying her, according to Abu Yusuf if she is poor. And this specification is the choice of the author of al-Mughni, al-Muhit, and al-Zahiriya. And Abu Yusuf obligates preparation absolutely, i.e., even if the husband is poor. His saying: as narrated by Bukhari from Aisha: 'Abu Bakr arrived on his horse from his residence at al-Sanh, dismounted, entered the mosque, and did not speak to anyone until he entered upon Aisha. He approached the Prophet, who was covered with a striped cloak, uncovered his face, leaned over him, kissed him, and wept. He did that only following the example of the Prophet, as narrated by Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, and al-Hakim authenticating that the Messenger of God entered upon Uthman ibn Maz'un while he was dead, leaned over him, kissed him, then wept until I saw tears flowing on his cheeks.' And in al-Tamhid: 'When Uthman died, the Prophet uncovered the cloth from his face, wept long, and kissed between his eyes. When he was lifted onto the bier, he said: Blessed are you, O Uthman, the world did not clothe you nor did it clothe itself.' His saying: 'and seeking blessings' – the waw means because his kissing of Uthman was for love, and Abu Bakr's kissing of the noble Prophet was for both. His saying: 'free from prohibition' is a condition for permissibility; if it is for lust, it is forbidden even for a wife apparently, because they say the marriage tie is severed by her death due to the removal of its subject. His saying: 'and burying her' i.e., its expense if she does not donate. His saying: 'if she was poor' – this is one of two views of Abu Yusuf; it is better to delay it after his saying 'even if the husband is poor' and make it an opposite. His saying: 'and this specification' i.e., specifying the obligation of preparation on the husband to the case when she is poor. His saying: 'and Abu Yusuf obligates' – in a copy with 'aw' (or), which is a narration of the disagreement from Abu Yusuf, and that is correct, he said.
Source pages p. 573

Commentary
This passage covers two distinct rulings. First, it states that kissing the deceased is permissible if done for love and seeking blessings, following the example of Abu Bakr kissing the Prophet and the Prophet kissing Uthman ibn Maz'un. The condition is that it must be free from lust; if done with desire, it is forbidden even for a spouse, as the marriage tie ends at death. Second, the passage addresses the husband's obligation to shroud and bury his wife. According to Abu Yusuf, this obligation is conditional: if the wife is poor, the husband must prepare her; otherwise, it is not obligatory. The preferred view (selected by the authors of al-Mughni, al-Muhit, and al-Zahiriya) is that the obligation is absolute, even if the husband is poor. The commentary notes a variant narration that Abu Yusuf obligates preparation absolutely. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the extent of the husband's duty.

Key Terms
تقبيل الميت (taqbīl al-mayyit): Kissing the deceased; permissible if for love/blessing, forbidden if for lust.
تجهيز (tajhīz): Preparation of the deceased for burial, including shrouding and burial.
معسرة (mu`sirah): A woman who is poor, i.e., has no assets to cover her own shrouding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position regarding the husband's obligation to shroud his wife?
A) The husband is obligated only if the wife is poor.
B) The husband is obligated absolutely, regardless of the wife's wealth.
C) The husband is obligated only if he is wealthy.
D) The husband is not obligated at all if the wife has family.

Key Takeaway
Kissing the deceased is permissible with the right intention, and the husband's duty to shroud his wife is absolute according to the soundest view.

The Sunnah Shroud for Men: Components and Rulings
Detailed explanation of the obligatory nature and sunnah components of a man's shroud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah garments for a man's shroud, explain the proof from the Prophet's practice, and apply the rule on when increase is permissible.

Core Idea
The sunnah shroud for a man is three garments: shirt, waist-wrapper, wrap — proven by the Prophet's ﷺ own burial.

Shrouding the deceased is a communal obligation (fard kifayah) upon the Muslim community. While the minimum is one garment, the sunnah specifies three pieces for a man as transmitted from the Prophet ﷺ. This lesson from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah details the components, the evidence, and the scope of permissible variation, ensuring you understand both the recommended practice and the limits of modification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal status of shrouding
The text states 'التكفين فرض' — shrouding is an obligation (fard kifayah). Understand that this means if some Muslims perform it, the community is absolved.
Fard kifayah differs from fard ayn; it does not fall on every individual.
2
Distinguish the three categories of shroud adequacy
The author divides shrouds into sunnah (three garments), kifayah (sufficiency), and darurah (necessity). Focus on the sunnah category.
The second and third categories are mentioned briefly; the passage mainly elaborates on the sunnah.
3
List and describe the three sunnah garments
The three garments are: a shirt (qamis) from collar to feet without sleeves, a waist-wrapper (izar) from crown to foot, and an outer wrap (lifafah) that extends beyond head and feet for folding.
Some authorities define the izar from shoulder to foot; the famous view is from crown to foot.
4
Understand the dalil: Prophetic practice and command to beautify
The text cites the hadith that the Prophet ﷺ was shrouded in three garments (kuffina fi thalathati athwabin) and the command 'حسنوا أكفان موتاكم' (make good the shrouds of your dead). This establishes the sunnah nature.
The command is for quality, not obligation of three.
5
Evaluate the difference of opinion on increasing beyond three
The text notes that increase is generally disliked unless the deceased bequeaths more. Some authorities (al-Dhakhira) allow up to five without dislike. The relied-upon view is that the sunnah is three, but increase is not forbidden.
Sticking to three is better to follow the sunnah, but not required.
