Book of Prayer: Something is spent for its owner. If unknown, another is shrouded with it; otherwise it is given in charity. It is not obligatory upon one who only has one garment to shroud a deceased who has no other. If a wild animal eats the deceased, the shroud belongs to the one who donated it, not the heir. If more than half the body or half with the head is found, it is washed and prayed upon; otherwise no. Shrouding is an obligation. As for the number of garments, there are three categories: sunnah, sufficiency, and necessity. The first is the sunnah for a man: three garments: a shirt from the collar to the feet without sleeves or cuffs, a waist-wrapper from the crown to the foot, and the third a wrap that exceeds above the crown and foot to wrap the deceased and be tied. Assistance upon the probing. His saying: 'It is not obligatory upon one who only has one garment etc.' meaning if there is only one man with the deceased and he has only one garment and the deceased has nothing, then the owner is more entitled to it, and the deceased is not shrouded with it. I say: the apparent is that if there are many men with the deceased and each has only one garment, the ruling is the same. And it indicates that if he has two garments, he shroud him in one of them. His saying: 'or half with the head' is a condition, because if half is found without a head, it is not washed or prayed upon; rather it is buried. This is derived from his saying 'otherwise no'. The body (badan) refers to what is beyond the limbs. His saying: 'Shrouding is an obligation' meaning a communal obligation (fard kifayah) with regard to the general Muslims, not for one who is specifically obligated, as in the author's hashiah on al-Durar. His saying: 'As for the number of garments' first are its types. His saying: 'It is the shroud of a man' meaning the adult and similarly the adolescent. For one who has not reached adolescence, it is best similarly. If he is shrouded in one garment, it is permissible. A stillborn and a newborn who dies are wrapped in a piece of cloth without observing the manner of the shroud, like a limb of the deceased, because they do not have complete sanctity, as the legal texts only mention shrouding the deceased, and the term 'deceased' does not apply to them just as it does not apply to a part of the deceased, as in al-Khaba'iyyah etc. His saying: 'Three garments' because it is reported that the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم was shrouded in three garments, and because that is the utmost beauty a man can have in his life, so similarly after his death. Increase is disliked as in al-Mujtaba, unless he bequeaths more, then it is not disliked. Unlike if he bequeaths to be shrouded in two garments, then he is shrouded in three and his condition is not followed because it contradicts the sunnah. In Ghayat al-Bayan, there is no harm in increasing beyond three for a man's shroud, and Ibn Amir Haj mentioned from al-Dhakhira that increase up to five is not disliked. Then sticking to three is to negate that the lesser is sunnah, as in al-Hamawi. His saying: 'A shirt (qamis) and a shift (dir') are the same in al-Hawi, but expressing it as qamis is clearer because dir' is ambiguous between that and an iron coat of armor. His saying: 'without sleeves or cuffs' repeats what comes in the text. His saying: 'A waist-wrapper (izar): it, the mantle (rida'), and the wrap (lifafah) have the same meaning: a long wide garment covering the body from the crown to the foot, as in Ibn Amir Haj from al-Hawi al-Qudsi. There is discussion on this interpretation by Mawlana al-Kamal. His saying: 'from the crown to the foot' is the famous view, as in al-Qahistani. In some copies of al-Mukhtar: from the shoulder to the foot. His saying: 'the third: a wrap (lifafah)' with a kasrah: that with which one is wrapped. It is also called rida' in al-Qahistani, and it is what is spread on the ground first. No problem in its top and bottom. The shroud is taken from what the man used to wear in his life on Friday and the two Eid, and it should be made good due to the hadith: 'Make good the shrouds of your dead, for they visit each other and boast about the beauty of their shrouds.' And one should not be extravagant due to his saying: 'Do not be extravagant in the shroud, for it is quickly stripped.' He was shrouded in three white Sahuliyyah garments (with fathah on the seen; with dammah, a village in Yemen). And the second: the shroud of sufficiency (kifayah) ... (translation continues to end of OCR, but truncated)
Source pages p. 575

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi explains the rulings of the shroud (kafan) for a deceased Muslim man. The author begins by establishing that shrouding (takfin) is a communal obligation (fard kifayah) upon the Muslim community. He then divides the number of garments into three categories: sunnah (recommended), kifayah (sufficient), and darurah (necessity). The focus here is on the sunnah category: three garments — a shirt (qamis) without sleeves or cuffs, a waist-wrapper (izar) covering from crown to foot, and a wrap (lifafah) that extends above the head and feet. The proof for three garments is that the Prophet ﷺ was shrouded in three, and it represents a man's customary adornment in life. Increase beyond three is generally disliked unless the deceased expressly bequeathed it; in that case, it is not disliked. However, some authorities like al-Dhakhira allow up to five without dislike. The shroud should be taken from the deceased's own clothing that he wore in life, especially on Fridays and Eids, and it should be of good quality — white, cotton, not extravagant. The hadith 'Make good the shrouds of your dead' encourages quality, but not extravagance. The passage also addresses edge cases: if only half a body with head is found, it is washed and prayed over; if without head, it is buried without prayer. Shrouding a stillborn or newborn is simple wrapping regardless of the sunnah three-piece set. The shroud belongs to the donor if the deceased was eaten by a beast. The second category (kifayah) is briefly mentioned but the text cuts off.

Key Terms
كفن (kafan): The shroud or burial garment for a deceased person.
قميص (qamis): A shirt-shaped garment from collar to feet without sleeves or cuffs.
إزار (izar): A waist-wrapper covering from crown to foot (or shoulder to foot in some views).
لفافة (lifafah): The outer wrap that is spread beneath and folded over the deceased.
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): A communal obligation; if fulfilled by some, others are absolved.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the sunnah number of garments for a man's shroud?
A) One garment
B) Two garments
C) Three garments
D) Five garments

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi sunnah for a man's shroud is three specific garments, increasing is allowed if bequeathed, and the shroud must not be extravagant.

Rules of the Shroud (Kafan) – Material, Number, and Prohibitions
Commentary on rulings of shroud material, number, and prohibitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the shroud (kafan): the recommended material, the sufficient minimum, and the prohibitions regarding sleeves, pockets, and turban.

Core Idea
The shroud should be of white cotton, moderate, and consist of three garments; the minimum is a waist-wrapper and wrapper.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi rulings on shrouding the deceased. Al-Tahtawi's commentary refines the rules based on hadith evidence, emphasizing moderation and the practice of the Prophet ﷺ. You will learn the sunnah shroud, the sufficient minimum, and the acts disliked due to their association with the living.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is shrouding the deceased. The Hanafi ruling: the sunnah is three white cotton garments; the minimum sufficient is a waist-wrapper and wrapper. Extravagance is prohibited, and using a turban is disliked.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith 'Hassinu akfan mawtakum' (Ibn Adi) and 'Idha kaffana ahadukum akhahu falyuhsin kaffanahu' (Muslim) indicate recommendation. 'La taghalu fi al-kafan' prohibits extravagance. The Prophet's action of three white garments sets the sunnah.
These hadith are ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'hassinu' implies recommendation (nadb) in Hanafi usul. The prohibition 'la taghalu' indicates haram of extravagance. The actual practice of the Prophet indicates sunnah muakkadah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools may permit silk or luxurious shrouds under certain conditions. The Hanafi school restricts the shroud to what was permissible for the deceased to wear in life.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the three white cotton garments. If not possible, the waist-wrapper and wrapper suffice. Extravagance is avoided, and the turban is makruh.
Al-Tahtawi cites al-Hidayah and al-Bahr.

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya) on the rulings of the shroud (kafan) for the deceased. It begins by stating that the shroud should be taken from what the deceased used to wear on Fridays and Eids, and it is recommended to beautify it based on the hadith commanding good shrouds. Extravagance is prohibited based on another hadith. The Prophet was shrouded in three white cotton garments. The minimum sufficient shroud for a man is a waist-wrapper and a wrapper, especially when wealth is little and heirs many. The best is to use white cotton, and both old washed and new garments are equal. The waist-wrapper and wrapper should cover from head to foot. A shirt (qamees) should not have sleeves, a pocket, or a slit on the chest, as these are for the needs of the living. If shrouded in a living person's shirt, its pocket, sleeves, and slit must be cut. The ends are not hemmed as there is no need. The turban is disliked according to the correct view because it was not part of the Prophet's shroud and would make the number even, whereas the sunnah is odd.

Key Terms
كفن (kafan): The shroud or burial garment for the deceased.
اللفافة (al-lifafa): The outer wrapper that covers the entire body from head to foot.
الإزار (al-izar): The waist-wrapper, a lower garment covering from waist to foot.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is disliked (makruh) in the correct view
C) It is obligatory (wajib)
D) It is permissible without dislike

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi shroud should be moderate, white cotton, and odd in number; avoid features designed for the living and unnecessary items like the turban.

Funeral Prayer: Ruling, Pillars, and Conditions
Establishes ruling, pillars, conditions, and refines first takbir status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling (fard kifayah), identify the pillars and conditions of funeral prayer, and explain why the first takbir is both a condition and a pillar according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Funeral prayer is fard kifayah; its pillars are takbirs and standing; the first takbir uniquely serves as both the opening condition and a pillar substitution.

Funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) is one of the most important collective duties in Islam. This passage from a Hanafi hashiah affirms its ruling as fard kifayah, clarifies its essential pillars and conditions, and delves into a nuanced scholarly debate: is the first takbir a condition, a pillar, or both? The author resolves this by combining the two views, a hallmark of Hanafi legal refinement. By working through this lesson, you will understand not only the basic requirements but also the legal reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the statement that funeral prayer is fard kifayah. Understand that this means it must be performed by some, not all, unless only one person is available.
The text explicitly says 'فرض كفاية' (fard kifayah) and adds 'مع عدم الإنفراد بالخطاب بها' – meaning if alone, it becomes individual.
2
Distinguish pillars from conditions
The text lists the pillars (arkan) as the takbirs and standing. Then it mentions conditions (shurut). Focus on the first takbir: why does the author say it is both a condition (shart) and a pillar (rukn)?
The first takbir is the opening takbir (shart) and also substitutes for a rak'ah (rukn). This dual categorization resolves a disagreement between Abu Yusuf and the combined view.
3
List the six conditions of funeral prayer
From the passage, identify the six conditions: Islam of the deceased, purity of his body, purity of the place, the deceased in front, prayer must stand, and the deceased present (or grave if necessary).
Condition 1: Islam – because prayer is intercession. Condition 2: Purity – from hadath and najasah. Condition 3: Purity of place. Condition 4: Deceased in front. Condition 5: Standing (qiyam). Condition 6: Presence of deceased (exception for grave prayer when washing impossible).
4
Examine the Quranic proof
The text cites Quran 9:84 and 9:103 as evidence. Note how the imperative 'salli' in 9:103 indicates obligation, while the prohibition in 9:84 shows the condition of Islam.
The dalil is both for the obligation and for the condition of Islam. The prohibition of praying over hypocrites proves that Islam is a shart.
5
Understand the practical consequence of the first takbir's dual nature
Because the first takbir is both shart and rukn, if it is missed, the entire prayer is invalid and must be restarted. This is unlike a mere sunnah whose omission would not invalidate.
This distinction matters in practice: if someone joins after the first takbir, they must make it up as a missed unit? Actually, funeral prayer does not have qada in the usual sense due to its nature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل الصلاة عليه
ككفنه ودفنه وتجهيزه فرض كفاية مع عدم الإنفراد بالخطاب بها ولو امرأة وأركانها التكبيرات والقيام لكن التكبيرة الأولى شرط باعتبار الشروع بها ركن باعتبار قيامها مقام ركعة كباقي التكبيرات كما في المحيط وشرائطها سنة أولها إسلام الميت لأنها شفاعة وليست لكافر والثاني طهارته وطهارة مكانه لأنه كالإمام والثالث تقدّمه أمام القوم والجماعة فيها ليست بشرط والصلاة على الكبير أفضل منها على الصغير قهستاني ويصح النذر بها لأنها قربة مقصودة بخلاف التكفين وتشييع الجنازة بحر قيل هي من خصائص هذه الأمة كالوصية بالثلث ورد بما أخرجه الحاكم وصححه عنه أنه قال: «كان آدم رجلاً أشقر طوالاً كأنه نخلة سحوق فلما حضره الموت نزلت الملائكة بحنوطه وكفنه من الجنة فلما مات عليه الصلاة والسلام غسلوه بالماء والسدر ثلاثاً وجعلوا في الثالثة كافوراً وكفنوه في وتر من الثياب وحفروا له لحداً وصلوا عليه وقالوا لولده هذه سنة لمن بعده» فإن الخصوصية تعين حمله على أنه بالنسبة لمجرد التكبير والكيفية قال الواقدي : لم تكن شرعت يوم موت خديجة وموتها رضي الله عنها بعد النبوة بعشر سنين على الأصح وقوله وحفروا له لحداً أي بمكة عند حواء عليهما السلام كما ذكره ابن العماد وهو أحد أقوال وكان جبريل هو الإمام بالملائكة كذا في النهاية وجزم ابن العماد بأنه شيث ويمكن الجمع كما ذكره بعض الأفاضل بأن شيئاً كان إمام البشر جبريل إمام الملائكة أو أن جبريل كان مبلغاً والملائكة مقتدون به وقد يؤيد كلام ابن العماد بأن شيئاً كان لا يعلم الكيفية فالظاهر أن الإمام جبريل ليعلم الكيفية شيث منه كا وقع للنبي في أول صلاة فرض بعد افتراض الخمس . قوله: (مع عدم الانفراد بالخطاب) فلو انفرد واحد بأن لم يحضره إلا هو تعين عليه تكفينه ودفنه كما في الضياء والشمني والبرهان قوله: (والقيام) فلا تصح قاعداً أو راكباً من غير عذر كذا في الدر لأنها صلاة من وجه لوجود التحريمة وكذا يشترط للصلاة ولو تعذر النزول عن الدابة لطين ونحوه جاز أن يصلي عليها راكباً استحساناً قوله: (لكن التكبيرة الأولى الخ) اعلم أن الكمال قال : إنّ التكبيرة الأولى شرط لأنها تكبيرة إحرام ولذا اختصت برفع اليدين وتعقبه في البحر والنهر بما في المحيط من أنه لا يجوز بناء صلاة جنازة على تحريمة أخرى ولو كانت شرطاً لجاز وذكر في الغاية أن الأربع تكبيرات قائمة مقام الأربع ركعات وهذا يقتضي أنها ركن فجمع المصنف بينهما بهذا الجمع ويؤيد هذا الجمع ما في الكافي حيث قال : إلا أن أبا يوسف يقول في التكبيرة الأولى معنيان معنى الافتتاح والقيام مقام ركعة ومعنى الافتتاح يترجح فيها ولهذا اختصت برفع اليدين ا هـ ثم في تعقب الشيخين للكمال تأمل لأنه لا يجوز بناء الفرض على تحريمه النفل أو فرض آخر مع أنها شرط لا ركن وفي السيد نقلاً عن حاشية المؤلف أفضل صفوفها آخرها وفي غيرها أولها إظهاراً للتواضع لتكون شفاعته أدعى إلى القبول ا هـ ومثله في القنية ونقله ابن ملك في شرح الوقاية عن الكرماني ا هـ قلت وينظر فيه بإطلاق ما صح في مسلم وغيره عنه خير صفوف الرجال أولها وشرها آخرها وإظهار التواضع لا يتوقف على التأخر لأن كونها أقرب إلى الإجابة إنما هو بالتحقق بالتواضع والخضوع وذلك بالمنحة الربانية لا بالتأخر قطعاً فيعمل بالإطلاق ما لم يوجد له مخصص صحيح كذا بحثه بعض الأذكياء وقد علمت ما نصه أهل المذهب على أنه قد يقال : إنّ الظاهر عنوان الباطن. قوله: (أولها إسلام الميت) إما بنفسه أو بإسلام أحد أبويه أو بتبعية الدار وإذا استوصف البالغ الإسلام ولم يصفه ومات لا يصلي كذا في شرح السيد. قوله: (لأنها شفاعة الخ) ولقوله تعالى: ﴿ولا تصل على منهم مات أبدا) [التوبة: ٩] كذا في الشرح قوله: (والثاني طهارته) عن نجاسة حكمية وحقيقية في البدن فلا تصح على من لم يغسل ولا على من عليه نجاسة وهذا الشرط عند الإمكان فلو دفن بلا غسل ولم يمكن إخراجه إلا بالنبش سقط الغسل وصلي على قبره بلا غسل للضرورة بخلاف ما إذا لم يهل عليه التراب بعد فإنه يخرج ويغسل ولو صلي عليه حموي أحد
Chapter on Prayer over the Dead. Like its shroud, burial, and preparation, it is a collective obligation (fard kifayah) provided there is no exclusive address to any individual, even if she is a woman. Its pillars are the takbirs and standing, but the first takbir is a condition by virtue of commencing with it, and a pillar by virtue of taking the place of a rak'ah like the other takbirs, as in al-Muhit. Its conditions are six: first, that the deceased be Muslim because it is intercession and not for a disbeliever; second, his purity and purity of place because it is like the imam; third, that he be placed in front of the congregation. Congregation is not a condition for it, and praying over an adult is better than over a child, as in Qahistani. Vowing to perform it is valid because it is an intended act of worship, unlike shrouding and escorting the funeral. It is said it is a characteristic of this ummah like the bequest of one-third, but this is rejected by what al-Hakim narrated and authenticated from him (the Prophet) who said: 'Adam was a tall, fair-skinned man like a tall palm tree. When death came to him, the angels descended with his embalming materials and shroud from Paradise. When he (Adam) died, they washed him with water and lotus leaves three times, placing camphor in the third, shrouded him in an odd number of garments, dug a grave for him with a niche, prayed over him, and said to his children: This is the sunnah for those after you.' So the specificity (to this ummah) is understood to be regarding mere takbir and manner. Al-Waqidi said: It was not legislated on the day of Khadija's death—and her death (may Allah be pleased with her) was ten years after prophethood according to the correct view—and the statement 'they dug a grave for him with a niche' means in Mecca at Hawwa's (Eve) grave as mentioned by Ibn al-Imad, which is one of the opinions. Jubril was the imam leading the angels, as in al-Nihaya, but Ibn al-Imad asserted that it was Seth, and it can be reconciled as some scholars mentioned: Seth was the imam of mankind, Jubril the imam of angels, or Jubril was the conveyor and the angels followed him. This may support Ibn al-Imad's statement because Seth did not know the manner, so the apparent is that Jubril was the imam to teach Seth the manner, as occurred with the Prophet (SAW) in the first obligatory prayer after the obligation of the five prayers. His statement: 'provided there is no exclusive address' — so if a person is alone, i.e., no one else is present, then shrouding and burying become specifically obligatory on him, as in al-Diya, al-Shamni, and al-Burhan. His statement: 'and standing' — so it is not valid sitting or riding without excuse, as in al-Durr, because it is a prayer in some respect due to the presence of the opening takbir (tahrimah). Similarly, it is required for prayer; if it is impossible to dismount from the animal due to mud or the like, it is permissible to pray on it riding, by istihsan. His statement: 'but the first takbir' — know that al-Kamal said: The first takbir is a condition because it is the takbir of ihram, and therefore it is distinguished by raising the hands. This was criticized in al-Bahr and al-Nahr by what is in al-Muhit that it is not permissible to build a funeral prayer on another tahrimah, and if it were a condition, it would be permissible. And in al-Ghayah it is mentioned that the four takbirs take the place of the four rak'ahs, and this requires that they be pillars. So the author (Maraqi al-Falah) combined between them with this combination. This combination is supported by what is in al-Kafi where it says: Abu Yusuf says concerning the first takbir that it has two meanings: the meaning of opening and taking the place of a rak'ah, and the meaning of opening is preponderant in it, and therefore it is distinguished by raising the hands. Then there is reflection in the criticism of the two shaykhs (al-Bahr and al-Nahr) of al-Kamal, because it is not permissible to build an obligatory act on its tahrimah as a supererogatory or another obligatory act, even if it is a condition not a pillar. And in al-Sayyid, quoting from the author's gloss: 'The best of its rows is the last one, and in others the first one, to show humility so that his intercession is more likely to be accepted.' A similar statement is in al-Quniyah, and Ibn Malik narrated it in Sharh al-Wiqayah from al-Kirmani. I say: This needs to be considered because of the absolute statement in Muslim and others that 'the best rows of men are the first and the worst are the last.' Showing humility does not depend on being behind, because being closer to acceptance is actually through actual humility and submission, and that is by divine gift, not by being behind, definitely. So one should act on the absolute statement as long as no sound specification exists. This is what some intelligent ones researched, and you know what the scholars of the madhhab have stated that it may be said: the outward is the title of the inward. His statement: 'first, Islam of the deceased' — either by himself or by the Islam of one of his parents or by following the abode of Islam. If an adult is asked about Islam and does not describe it and dies, one does not pray over him, as in Sayyid's commentary. His statement: 'because it is intercession' — and because of Allah's statement: 'And do not ever pray over any of them who dies' (9:84). His statement: 'second, his purity' — from ritual impurity (hadath) and actual impurity (najasah) on the body, so it is not valid over one who has not been washed or over one who has impurity on him. This condition is when possible. So if he is buried without washing and it is not possible to take him out except by exhuming, the washing is dropped and one prays over his grave without washing due to necessity, contrary to if the soil has not been poured over him completely, then he is taken out and washed. And even if prayed over... Hamwi one.
Source pages p. 580

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiyah) on the section of funeral prayer from Maraqi al-Falah. It begins by affirming the well-known ruling: funeral prayer, like shrouding, burial, and preparation, is fard kifayah (collective obligation) by consensus, meaning that if some Muslims perform it, the obligation is discharged from all. Its pillars (arkan) are the takbirs and standing. The author notes a subtle point from al-Muhit: the first takbir is both a condition (shart) because it is the takbir of ihram and a pillar (rukn) because it stands in place of a rak'ah. This resolves an intra-Hanafi ambiguity. The conditions (shurut) are then listed: the deceased must be Muslim (the prayer is intercession, not for a disbeliever), physical purity of the deceased and his place (as if the deceased is the imam), and that the deceased is placed in front of the congregation. The passage then discusses several ancillary issues: congregation is not a condition, praying over an adult is superior to a child, and vowing to perform funeral prayer is valid (unlike shrouding or escorting, which are not independent acts of worship). A long digression reports a hadith about the funeral prayer of Adam (upon him peace) to refute the claim that funeral prayer is a distinctive characteristic of this ummah; the hadith shows that angels performed it for Adam. The commentary clarifies that the specificity (if any) relates only to manner. Further, the passage elaborates on the condition of non-exclusive address: if only one person is present, it becomes obligatory upon that individual. Standing is normally required, but riding is permitted by istihsan when dismounting is difficult. A significant portion debates the status of the first takbir: citing al-Kamal, al-Bahr, al-Nahr, and al-Kafi, the text weighs the views of Abu Yusuf and others, concluding that the first takbir has two aspects (opening and substitution for a rak'ah), with the opening aspect predominating. The best rows for funeral prayer are also discussed: some say the last row is best to show humility, but this is reconciled with the general hadith that the first rows of men are best. The commentator leans toward the absolute hadith unless a specific mukhassis (specifier) exists. Finally, the conditions of Islam and purity are detailed with practical cases: if a Muslim is born to Muslim parents or in a Muslim land, he is considered Muslim; if an adult is asked about Islam and does not affirm it, no prayer is offered. Purity from hadath and najasah is required; if the deceased is buried unwashed, the prayer can be performed over the grave after burial due to necessity, but not before the earth is fully poured.

Key Terms
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): An obligation that must be fulfilled by some members of the Muslim community; if no one performs it, all are sinful, but if a sufficient number do, the rest are absolved.
الشرط والركن (al-shart wa al-rukn): In this context, the first takbir is considered both a condition (shart) because it is the opening takbir that initiates the prayer, and a pillar (rukn) because it substitutes for a rak'ah's takbir.
الشفاعة (al-shafa'ah): Intercession; the funeral prayer is described as intercession for the deceased, seeking Allah's forgiveness for him.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is the first takbir of funeral prayer considered both a condition (shart) and a pillar (rukn)?
A) Because it is the opening takbir and also represents one of the four takbirs replacing rak'ahs
B) Because it is obligatory by Quran and must be raised with the hands
C) Because Abu Hanifa ruled it as both to avoid ikhtilaf
D) Because it is the only takbir that requires standing

Key Takeaway
Funeral prayer is a collective duty; its key feature is that the first takbir uniquely serves as both the opening condition and a pillar, and knowing this distinction is essential for correct practice.

Conditions of Imam and Dead in Janazah Prayer
Conditions and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on position of imam and dead

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for the imam's position and the deceased's placement in janazah prayer, identify the ruling when conditions are violated, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding following a sitting imam.

Core Idea
Imam on ground, dead on ground: prayer invalid without excuse.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi details two key conditions of the janazah prayer: the imam's stance and the deceased's placement. It also clarifies exceptions for legitimate excuses and addresses a known intra-Hanafi disagreement on the validity of standing followers behind a sitting imam. Understanding these conditions ensures the prayer is performed correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition on the imam's position
The text states the imam must be on the ground (على الأرض). If he is on a riding animal while the congregation is on foot, the prayer is invalid without an excuse.
The relied-upon view (al-mukhtar) is that the prayer is invalid unless there is an excuse.
2
Recognize the exception for excuses
Excuses like illness or muddy ground make the prayer valid even if the condition is not met. For example, a sick imam may pray sitting and the prayer is valid.
The exception applies for any legitimate excuse (عذر).
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute on following a sitting imam
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that a standing person cannot validly follow a sitting imam, even with excuse. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold it is valid if the imam has an excuse.
The text mentions 'عندهما لا عند محمد' which likely refers to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) vs. Abu Hanifa, though it is phrased confusingly.
4
Identify the sixth condition: deceased on ground
The deceased must be placed on the ground. This condition applies to those who catch all takbirs with the imam; for a masbuq (latecomer), there is disagreement.
If the deceased is lifted before the masbuq completes his takbirs, he may continue if not too far removed, according to one view.
5
Note additional conditions from commentary
The commentary adds that the imam must be mature (baligh), should stand opposite a part of the deceased (preferably chest), and covering the deceased's private parts suffices for the prayer (full shroud is for honor).
For multiple deceased, they can be lined up in a row and the imam stands by the best of them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(على الأرض) لكونه الإمام من وجه فإن كان على دابة أو أبدى الناس لم تجز الصلاة على المختار إلا إن كان من عذر) كما في التبيين (بلا عذر أما بالعذر فتصبح كما إذا كان مريضاً، ولو إماماً فصلى قاعداً، والناس خلفه قياماً أجزأه عندهما لا عند محمد بناءً على الخلاف في صحة اقتداء القائم بالقاعد، وعدمها، ولا فرق في المصلي قاعداً بعذر بين كونه ولياً، أو لا لأن كون الولي له حق التقدم لا يمنع سقوط الفرض بغيره، ولو بدون إذنه وإنما الولي له حق الإعادة، وحينئذ فلا فرق في سقوط الفرض بصلاة غير الولي بين أن يكون قائماً، أو قاعداً لعذر أفاده بعض الحذاق راداً على السيد فيما ذكره قوله : ( والسادس) كون الميت موضوعاً على الأرض) الظاهر أن اشتراط وضعه بالنسبة للمدرك الذي لم يفته شيء من التكبير خلف الإمام أما المسبوق ففي كون الوضع شرطاً له أيضاً خلاف ولهذا قالوا إذا رفعت قبل أن يقضي ما عليه من التكبير فإنه يأتي به ما لم يتباعد على قول ذكره السيد وعلى المشهور أنه يأتي به تتراً بلا دعاء إن خشي رفع الميت على الأعناق كما يأتي للمصنف . قوله : (إلا) من (عذر كأن كان بالأرض وحل لا يتأتى وضع الميت عليها . تنبيه : قال في الدور بقي من الشروط بلوغ الإمام ا هـ، وبقي منها أن يحاذي الإمام جزأ من الميت كما في القهستاني والسراج قلت : الظاهر أن هذا فيما إذا لم تكثر الموتى إذ عند كثرتها يجوز أن يجعلها صفاً واحداً ويقوم عند أفضلهم، وبقي من الشروط ستر عورته فقط، وإن كان الفرض في الكفن ستر جميع البدن لأن هذا من حيث الصلاة عليه، وذاك من حيث تكريمه وأداء حقه كذا قاله بعض الأفاضل
(On the ground) because he is the imam in one respect. If he is on a riding animal or the people are on foot, the prayer is not valid according to the chosen position unless there is an excuse, as in al-Tabyeen. (Without excuse) but with excuse it is valid, as when he is sick. If an imam prays sitting and the people behind him are standing, it is valid according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), not according to Muhammad, based on the disagreement about the validity of a standing person following a sitting one. There is no difference in the one praying sitting due to excuse between being a guardian or not, because the guardian's right to precedence does not prevent the obligation falling by another, even without his permission; the guardian only has the right to repeat. Thus there is no difference in the falling of the obligation by the prayer of a non-guardian whether he is standing or sitting due to excuse, as some refined scholars stated, refuting al-Sayyid. His statement: (And the sixth) is that the deceased is placed on the ground. Apparently, the condition of his placement is for the one who did not miss any takbir behind the imam. As for the one who is preceded (masbuq), there is disagreement about whether the condition is also for him. Hence they said: if it (the deceased) is lifted before he completes the takbirs he owes, he performs them as long as he has not moved far, according to a view mentioned by al-Sayyid. According to the well-known view, he performs them successively without supplication if he fears the deceased being raised on shoulders, as will come from the author. His statement: (except) due to (an excuse, such as the ground being muddy and it is not possible to place the deceased on it). A note: In al-Durr, it is said: Among the conditions remaining is the puberty of the imam, etc. Also remaining is that the imam should be opposite a part of the deceased, as in al-Qahistani and al-Siraj. I say: Apparently this is when there are not many deceased, for when they are many, it is permissible to line them up in one row and stand at the best of them. Also remaining among the conditions is covering only his private parts, although the obligation in the shroud is to cover the whole body, because this is with respect to praying over him, and that is with respect to honoring him and fulfilling his right, as some virtuous scholars have said.
Source pages p. 583

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi deals with two key conditions of the Janazah prayer: the imam's position and the placement of the deceased. The first condition states that the imam should be on the ground; if he prays on a riding animal while the congregation is on foot, the prayer is invalid according to the relied-upon view, unless there is an excuse (e.g., illness). The commentary then discusses the intra-Hanafi dispute on following a sitting imam: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that if the imam sits due to excuse, the prayer of standing followers is valid, while Muhammad (actually Imam Muhammad is part of the Sahibayn, but here it seems a distinction is made; likely a reference to a different Muhammad, perhaps Muhammad al-Shaybani himself is one of the two, so the text says 'عندهما لا عند محمد' meaning the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) agree with Abu Hanifa? Actually in the Hanafi school, the view of Abu Hanifa is that a standing person cannot follow a sitting one, while the two disciples allow it. The text says 'عندهما' at the first mention, then 'لا عند محمد' which is confusing. Possibly a typo; it should be 'لا عند أبي حنيفة'. However, the commentator continues to say that if the imam has an excuse, there is no difference between a guardian (wali) and others in the validity of the prayer. The second condition is the sixth condition: the deceased must be placed on the ground. The commentator explains that this condition applies to the person who catches all the takbirs with the imam; for the masbuq (latecomer), there is disagreement. If the deceased is lifted before the masbuq completes his takbirs, he may continue if he has not moved far, according to one view, or he should complete them quickly without dua if necessary. Exceptions are allowed for excuses like muddy ground. Additional conditions mentioned: the imam must be mature (baligh) and should stand opposite a part of the deceased (preferably the chest, as per the sunan). For multiple dead bodies, they can be lined up in a row and the imam stands by the best of them. Also, the covering of the deceased's private parts is sufficient for the prayer, though the full shroud is for respect.

Key Terms
عذر (ʿudhr): A legitimate excuse (e.g., illness, muddy ground) that permits deviation from the normal condition.
مسبوق (masbūq): A person who joins the prayer late, after the imam has already commenced.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the imam leads janazah prayer while riding a donkey without any excuse, the prayer is:
A) Valid, because the imam's position does not matter.
B) Invalid according to the relied-upon view.
C) Valid only if the congregation is also riding.
D) Valid but makruh.

Key Takeaway
The imam must be on the ground and the deceased on the ground; without excuse, the prayer is invalid; with excuse, it is valid.

Order of Priority for Leading the Funeral Prayer
Determining the rightful imam for janaza prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of priority for who leads the janaza prayer and identify when a person with right may delegate.

Core Idea
The funeral prayer leadership follows a fixed order: wali, father, blood relative, husband, neighbors.

This lesson clarifies the hierarchy of individuals entitled to lead the funeral prayer based on their relationship to the deceased. Understanding this priority is essential to ensure that the prayer is led by the most deserving person, honoring both the deceased and the living. The text cites a hadith about the virtue of a father's supplication and details the roles of master, blood relative, emancipator, husband, and neighbors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
Recognize that the purpose of the janaza prayer is supplication for the deceased, and the one whose supplication is most likely to be answered is preferred.
The hadith about three answered supplications supports preferring the father.
2
Trace the specific order
List the categories in order: master (if the deceased was a slave), blood relative (asabah), emancipator, then husband, then neighbors.
The text states 'السيد أولى من قريب عبده' (the master is more entitled than the relative of his slave).
3
Understand the right to authorize
The one with the right of precedence may authorize another person to lead, because he can forfeit his right.
Permission can be given explicitly or implicitly by praying behind another.
4
Apply to cases with equal ranks
When two persons share equal right (e.g., two sons), the second may prevent the first's authorization. The appointment by the older is preferred over that by the younger.
The text says 'فالذي قدمه الأكبر أولى' (the one appointed by the older is more entitled).

دفنه من يوم
Book of Prayer. Most High: For preferring the father there is a good aspect: that the purpose is supplication for the deceased and his supplication is answered. Abu Hurairah narrated from the Prophet (ﷺ): 'Three supplications are answered: the supplication of the oppressed, the supplication of the traveler, and the supplication of a parent for his child.' Recorded by al-Tayalisi. The master (owner) is more entitled than the relative of his slave according to the correct view. The relative (by blood) is given precedence over the emancipator. If there is no guardian (wali), then the husband, then the neighbors. And the one who has the right of precedence may authorize another, because he can forfeit his right. If there are multiple, the second may prevent. And the one appointed by the older is more entitled than the one appointed by the younger...
Source pages p. 590

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement on the commentary of Maraqi al-Falah, dealing with the order of priority in leading the funeral prayer (salat al-janaza) and the rules for repeating it. The text begins by affirming that the father should be preferred due to the virtue of his supplication, citing a hadith about three answered supplications. The commentator explains that the master (sayyid) of a slave is more entitled than the slave's blood relative, since the master owns him, while a blood relative is preferred over the emancipator because the latter has no remaining right. If there is no wali (guardian), the husband takes precedence due to marital bonds, then neighbors as defined by custom. The one who has the right may authorize another to lead or to leave after the prayer, and doing so without permission is disliked (makruh). If two persons share equal right, the second may prevent the first's authorization. The text then discusses repetition: if someone without right prays without permission and does not follow the rightful person, the rightful one may repeat the prayer (istihbab, not wujub), because his right was not extinguished. However, if he prayed behind the rightful one or gave permission, repetition is not allowed. The one with right of precedence is more entitled than a person appointed by the deceased's will, as such a will is invalid in the mainstream view. Finally, if the deceased was buried without prayer for a valid reason, prayer may be performed at the grave, even if the body was not washed, and exhumation is not required. The commentary draws on multiple sources including al-Hidayah, al-Bahr, al-Jawharah, al-Nahr, al-Durr, al-Muhit, and al-Fath, and addresses various intra-Hanafi and inter-school nuances.

Key Terms
ولي (wali): The guardian or person entitled to lead the funeral prayer, usually the closest male relative (father, son, etc.).
إعادة (i'adah): Repeating the funeral prayer by the rightful person after someone else has prayed without his permission.
وصية (wasiyyah): A will or bequest by the deceased regarding who should lead his funeral prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who has the right to lead the janaza prayer if the deceased was a free man with no close male relatives?
A) His master (if he was a slave).
B) His husband.
C) His neighbours.
D) Any Muslim present.

Key Takeaway
The wali (closest male relative) has the primary right to lead the janaza prayer; he may delegate but his right takes precedence.

Repetition of the Funeral Prayer and the Deceased's Will
Rules for repeating janaza and validity of will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain when a funeral prayer may be repeated and why a will designating an imam is invalid in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A rightful person may repeat the janaza if not prayed by or with authorization; a will for imam is invalid.

This lesson addresses two important issues: the permissibility of repeating the funeral prayer when the rightful person did not lead, and the legal status of a deceased's will regarding who should lead. These rulings protect the established rights of the wali and prevent vain repetition. The text also covers prayer at the grave if burial occurred without prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions for repetition
The rightful person may repeat the janaza if someone else led without his permission and he did not pray behind that person. Repetition is optional, not obligatory.
The text uses 'إن شاء' (if he wishes) indicating istihbab.
2
Understand the nullity of will
A deceased's will designating a specific person to lead the prayer is invalid on the mufta bihi view; the wali's right cannot be overridden.
Al-Tahtawi reports from al-Sadr al-Shahid: 'الوصية باطلة على المفتي به'.
3
Consider the exception of burial without prayer
If the deceased was buried without prayer for a valid reason, the prayer can be performed at the grave, even if the body was not washed.
Exhumation is not required; prayer at the grave suffices.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference about the will
Ibn Rustam narrates that the will is valid, but the majority (mufta bihi) says it is invalid.
The difference is recorded in Nawadir Ibn Rustam.

Source pages p. 590

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement on the commentary of Maraqi al-Falah, dealing with the order of priority in leading the funeral prayer (salat al-janaza) and the rules for repeating it. The text begins by affirming that the father should be preferred due to the virtue of his supplication, citing a hadith about three answered supplications. The commentator explains that the master (sayyid) of a slave is more entitled than the slave's blood relative, since the master owns him, while a blood relative is preferred over the emancipator because the latter has no remaining right. If there is no wali (guardian), the husband takes precedence due to marital bonds, then neighbors as defined by custom. The one who has the right may authorize another to lead or to leave after the prayer, and doing so without permission is disliked (makruh). If two persons share equal right, the second may prevent the first's authorization. The text then discusses repetition: if someone without right prays without permission and does not follow the rightful person, the rightful one may repeat the prayer (istihbab, not wujub), because his right was not extinguished. However, if he prayed behind the rightful one or gave permission, repetition is not allowed. The one with right of precedence is more entitled than a person appointed by the deceased's will, as such a will is invalid in the mainstream view. Finally, if the deceased was buried without prayer for a valid reason, prayer may be performed at the grave, even if the body was not washed, and exhumation is not required. The commentary draws on multiple sources including al-Hidayah, al-Bahr, al-Jawharah, al-Nahr, al-Durr, al-Muhit, and al-Fath, and addresses various intra-Hanafi and inter-school nuances.

Key Terms
ولي (wali): The guardian or person entitled to lead the funeral prayer, usually the closest male relative (father, son, etc.).
إعادة (i'adah): Repeating the funeral prayer by the rightful person after someone else has prayed without his permission.
وصية (wasiyyah): A will or bequest by the deceased regarding who should lead his funeral prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the deceased's will designating a specific person to lead the janaza prayer according to the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school?
A) The will is valid and must be followed.
B) The will is invalid, and the rightful guardian takes precedence.
C) The will is valid only if the guardian agrees.
D) The will is invalid only if the designated person is not a relative.

Key Takeaway
Repetition of the janaza is optional for the rightful person if not prayed with permission; the deceased's will cannot override the guardian's right.

Taharah — Purification

Exhuming a Body Buried Without Ghusl
States ruling on exhuming and repeating prayer before decomposition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exhuming a body buried without ghusl and apply the criterion of decomposition (tafassukh) to determine obligation.

Core Idea
Exhumation for ghusl is wajib before decomposition; if earth thrown, assess by judicial estimate.

In Hanafi fiqh, washing the deceased (ghusl) is a condition for the validity of the janazah prayer. If a body is buried without ghusl, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated. But how does burial affect this? The hashīya of al-Tahtawi refines the rule: exhumation is required unless the body has begun to decompose. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of the prayer after burial.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognise that the act under discussion is the janazah prayer performed on a body that was not washed (ghusl) before burial. Determine the hukm: the prayer is invalid (fasid), and exhumation for washing is wajib.
The hukm level is wajib for exhumation, not fard.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is based on the principle that washing is a condition for prayer; the ability to wash existed before burial, so omission invalidates the prayer. This is a dalīl naqlī derived from the general rules of ṭahārah.
No specific hadith is cited for the ruling itself; the hadith about three rows is about the virtue of rows, not directly about exhumation.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
The text mentions a second opinion: 'qīla tanaqalabu ṣaḥīḥatan' – some (perhaps Ḥasan ibn Ziyād) held the prayer becomes valid after burial due to realized inability. Understand the basis: after burial, washing is impossible, so the prayer is considered valid.
This is a weaker (nawādir) opinion; the relied-upon position (zāhir al-riwāyah) rejects it.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The majority response: inability is not realized until earth is thrown. If earth has not been thrown, exhumation is easy. Even after throwing, if the body has not decomposed, exhumation is still possible. The criterion for decomposition is the judge's informed judgment (akbar al-ra'y).
The text adds a ruling on rows (if the congregation is seven), but that is a separate issue; our focus is on the exhumation ruling.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarāt al-khilāf)
If earth not thrown: exhume, wash, and pray again. If earth thrown but no decomposition: still exhume, wash, and pray. If decomposed: exhumation is not allowed (haram) because of sanctity of the corpse, and the prayer is not repeated.
The muftā bihī position is the majority view: exhume unless decomposed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرط طهارته لحرمة نبشه وتعاد (لو) صلي عليه قبل الدفن بلا غسل لفساد الأولى بالقدرة على تغسيله قبل الدفن وقيل تنقلب صحيحة لتحقق العجز ولو لم يهل التراب يخرج فيغسل ويصلى عليه (ما لم يتفسخ والمعتبر فيه أكبر الرأي على الصحيح لاختلافه باختلاف الزمان، والإنسان، وإذا كان القوم سبعة يقدم واحد أماماً، وثلاثة بعده، وإثنان بعدهم وواحد بعدهما لأنّ في الحديث: (من صلى عليه ثلاثة صفوف غفر له وخيرها آخرها) لأنه أدعى للإجابة بالتواضع
Its purity is a condition for the sanctity of exhuming it. And it is repeated (if) prayer was performed over it before burial without washing, because the first becomes invalid due to the ability to wash it before burial. And it is said it becomes valid due to the realization of inability. And if the earth has not been thrown in, it is taken out, washed, and prayed over. (As long as it has not decomposed.) And the criterion for that is the greater opinion, correctly due to its variation with variation of time and person. And when the people are seven, one is put forward as imam, three after him, two after them, and one after them both, because in the hadith: 'Whoever prays over him in three rows will be forgiven, and the best of them is the last' – because it is more conducive to response due to humility.
Source pages p. 592

Commentary
This is a hashiya commentary that refines the ruling on exhuming a body buried without ghusl. The passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: the first opinion (zahir al-riwayah) holds that if prayer was performed before burial without washing, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated after washing, because the inability (ghusl) is removed before burial. A second opinion (likely from nawadir) considers that the prayer becomes valid after burial due to actual inability. The text confirms the relied-upon position: if earth has not been thrown, exhumation is obligatory; after throwing, it depends on decomposition. The criterion for decomposition is determined by the judge's honest judgment (akbar al-ra'y), varying by climate and physique. The hadith about three rows is cited to emphasize the virtue of rows, though the main ruling is about exhumation.

Key Terms
نبش (nabsh): Exhuming a buried body.
تفسخ (tafassukh): Decomposition of the body to the point where limbs separate.
أكبر الرأي (akbar al-ra'y): The considered judgment of the (judicial) authority based on prevailing conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what should be done if a body was buried without ghusl and the grave earth has NOT been thrown?
A) Nothing; burial completes the duty.
B) Exhume, wash, and repeat the janazah prayer.
C) Only repeat the prayer without exhumation.
D) Wait for decomposition, then decide.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires exhumation of a body buried without ghusl before decomposition, as the original prayer is invalid due to the ability to wash having existed.

Rulings on a Miscarried Fetus (Saqt)
Details the washing, naming, prayer, and resurrection of a miscarried fetus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on washing and praying over a miscarried fetus (saqt) and explain the proof from hadith regarding its resurrection and intercession.

Core Idea
A miscarried fetus is washed but not prayed over: it is a soul yet not fully a living child.

This lesson delves into the unique rulings for a miscarried fetus (saqt) according to the Hanafi school. The text from Hashiya al-Tahtawi distinguishes between washing and funeral prayer, providing a nuanced position that reconciles the fetus's status as a potential soul and a part of its mother. A hadith about the fetus interceding for its parents underpins the ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the core ruling
Identify the mufta bihi: the miscarried fetus is washed, wrapped, named, and buried, but no funeral prayer is performed.
This applies if the fetus showed signs of life (cried) or had formed limbs.
2
Identify the proof
Find the hadith evidence cited: the fetus will be resurrected and can intercede for parents, proving it is a soul.
The hadith is from Abu Ubayda and Ibn Majah; its transmission is zanni.
3
Understand the reconciliation
Note how the commentator reconciles the Zahir al-Riwayah (which prohibits all) with the chosen position: washing is due to the soul aspect, no prayer due to being part of Adam.
This is a critical refinement (ta'tiq) of the matn.
4
Note the condition of limbs
Determine that if no limbs formed, the fetus is not washed or named, as it will not be resurrected.
If some limbs appear, it is washed, named, and will be resurrected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن لم يستهل غسل وإن لم يتم خلقه في المختار لأنه نفس من وجه وأدرج في خرقة وسمي ودفن ولم يصل عليه ويحشر إن بان بعض خلقه وذكر في المبسوط قولاً آخر: لا يتم نقاه فمن محمد وروى الجرجاني عن أصحابنا أنه يشق قال الكمال وهو أولى معللاً: بأن احترامه سقط بتعديه، والاختلاف في شقه مقيد بما إذا لم يترك مالاً، وإلا لا يشق اتفاقاً قاله السيد. قوله : إلا ذلك إلا اسم بمعنى غير أي لا يسع غير ذلك أحد، ويحتمل أن فاعل يسع ضمير يرجع إلى معلوم من المقام أي لا يسع الحال غير ذلك قوله : (وإن لم يستهل) مثله ما إذا استهل فمات قبل خروج أكثره، وأما الاستهلال في البطن فغير معتبر بالأولى. قوله : (وإن لم خلقه فيغسل، وإن لم يراع فيه السنة، وبهذا يجمع بين من أثبت غسله، وبين من أثبته أراد الغسل في الجملة، ومن نفاه أراد الغسل المراعي فيه وجه السنة، والمتبادر منه أنه ظهر فيه بعض خلق، وأما إذا لم يظهر فيه خلق أصلاً، فالظاهر أنه لا يغسل، ولا يسمى لعدم حشره وحرره. قوله : (في المختار) وظاهر الرواية منع الكل، وكذا لا يرث، ولا يورث اتفاقاً لأنه كجزء الحي كما في الزيلعي والحموي، وحاصل ما في المصنف أنه بالنظر لكونه نفساً من وجه يغسل، ويصلى عليه، وبالنظر لكونه جزء آدمي لا ولا فاعملنا الشبهين، فقلنا: يغسل عملاً بالأول، ولا يصلى عليه عملاً بالثاني، ورجحنا خلاف ظاهر لرواية قوله: (لأنه نفس من وجه الأولى ما في ملتقى البحار حيث قال إكراماً لبني آدم وإنما كان نفساً لأنه يبعث، وإن لم ينفخ فيه الروح على أحد القولين. قوله : (وسمى) أي وإن لم يتم خلقه كما في الشرح عن الطحاوي قوله: (ويحشر إن بان بعض خلقه) هو الذي يقتضيه مذهب أصحابنا لأنه يثبت له حرمة بني آدم بدليل ثبوت الأحكام الشرعية له ،كاستيلاد وانقضاء عدة نهر، وقد قالوا: إن السقط يحيا في الآخرة، وترجى شفاعته واستدلوا بما روى أبو عبيدة مرفوعاً أن السقط ليقف محينطئا على باب الجنة فيقول لا أدخل حتى يدخل أبواي وقوله محبنطئا يروى بغير همز وبهمز فعلى الأول معناه المتغضب المستبطىء للشيء، وعلى الثاني معناه العظيم البطن المنتفخ يعني يغضب، وينتفخ بطنه من الغضب حتى يدخل أبواه الجنة، وروى ابن ماجه من حديث علي رضي الله عنه أن السقط ليراغم ربه إذ دخل أبواه النار فيقال أيها السقط المراغم ربه أدخل أبويك الجنة فيجرهما بسرره حتى يدخلهما الجنة ا هـ والسرر بفتحتين، ويكسر لغة في السر بالضم وهو ما تقطعه القابلة من سرة الصبي ويحشر على ما مات عليه كغيره من أهل الموقف، ثم عند دخول الجنة يصيرون طولاً واحداً ففي الحديث الصحيح يبعث كل عبد على ما مات عليه وفيه صفة أهل الجنة أنهم على صورة آدم طول كل واحد منهم ستون ذراعاً زاد أحمد وغيره في عرض سبعة أذرع ، وهم أبناء ثلاث وثلاثين.
And if it did not cry [at birth], it is washed, even if its creation was not complete, according to the chosen [position] because it is a soul in one respect. And it is wrapped in a cloth, named, buried, and no prayer is performed over it. And it will be resurrected if some of its limbs appear. And it was mentioned in al-Mabsut another saying: it is not perfected... from Muhammad. And al-Jurjani narrated from our companions that it should be split. al-Kamal said: and it is more appropriate, reasoning that its reverence fell due to its transgression. And the difference about splitting it is restricted to when it did not leave wealth; otherwise it is not split by agreement, as al-Sayyid said. His statement: except that except a noun meaning other, i.e., nothing other than that can accommodate one. It is possible that the subject of 'can accommodate' is a pronoun referring to something understood from context, i.e., the situation cannot accommodate anything else. His statement: (And if it did not cry) similarly if it did cry and died before most of it came out. As for crying in the womb, it is not considered, all the more so. His statement: (And if not created...) it is washed even if the sunnah is not observed in it. And by this reconciliation is made between those who affirm its washing and those who affirm it intended washing in general; and those who negated it intended washing with the sunnah aspect observed. The apparent understanding is that some creation appeared in it. As for when no creation appeared at all, apparently it is not washed and not named because it will not be resurrected and will be destroyed. His statement: (in the chosen) and the apparent narration prohibits all; likewise it does not inherit nor is it inherited by agreement because it is like a part of the living, as in al-Zaylai and al-Hamawi. The gist of what is in the text is that from the perspective of being a soul in one respect, it is washed and prayer is performed over it; from the perspective of being a part of Adam, it is not. So we consider both similarities: we say it is washed acting on the first, and no prayer is performed over it acting on the second, and we favored contrary to the apparent narration due to a narration. His statement: (because it is a soul in one respect) the first is what is in Multaqa al-Bihar where he said: honoring the children of Adam; and it is a soul because it will be resurrected, even if the spirit was not blown into it according to one of the two sayings. His statement: (and named) i.e., even if its creation is not complete, as in the commentary from al-Tahawi. His statement: (and it will be resurrected if some of its limbs appear) this is what the madhhab of our companions requires because it has the sanctity of the children of Adam, as evidenced by the establishment of legal rulings for it such as istilad (establishing paternity) and completion of 'idda. And they said that the miscarried fetus lives in the afterlife and its intercession is hoped for. They adduced what Abu Ubayda narrated in marfu' form: 'Indeed the miscarried fetus stands angrily at the gate of Paradise and says: I will not enter until my parents enter.' And the word 'muhbanṭi'an' is narrated with and without hamza; in the first it means angry and impatient, in the second it means big-bellied, i.e., he becomes angry and his belly swells from anger until his parents enter Paradise. And Ibn Majah narrated from 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) that the miscarried fetus quarrels with his Lord when his parents enter the Fire, and it is said: O miscarried fetus who quarrels with his Lord, cause your parents to enter Paradise, so he drags them by their umbilical cords until he brings them into Paradise. And 'al-surr' (with two fatha) and kasra as a dialect for 'al-sirr' (with damm) is what the midwife cuts from the child's navel. And he will be resurrected in the state he died upon like others of the people of the standing, then upon entering Paradise they become of one height. In the authentic hadith: 'Every servant will be raised upon what he died upon' and in it the description of the people of Paradise that they are in the form of Adam, each one sixty cubits tall, and Ahmad and others added: seven cubits in width, and they are thirty-three years of age.
Source pages p. 598

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya Al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement (hashiya) of Maraqi al-Falah, addressing the legal rulings for a miscarried fetus (saqt). The author begins by stating the core ruling from the matn: if the fetus did not cry after birth, it is washed (ghusl), wrapped in a cloth, given a name, buried, and no funeral prayer (janazah) is performed over it, according to the chosen (mukhtar) position. The reason given is that it is a soul (nafs) in one respect—because it will be resurrected on the Day of Judgment even if the spirit was not blown into it according to one opinion. The text then presents an alternative view from al-Mabsut attributed to Imam Muhammad, and another from al-Jurjani about splitting the womb to extract the fetus. The commentator, al-Tahtawi, refines these: the difference about splitting is restricted to when the fetus left no wealth; if it did leave wealth, splitting is not allowed by consensus. He then clarifies the phrase 'except that' (illa dhalika) meaning nothing else can accommodate. The ruling is then qualified: if the fetus cried at birth but died before emerging completely, it has the same ruling. Crying in the womb is not considered. The washing applies even if not done according to sunnah, reconciling different views: those who affirm washing mean any washing, those who negate mean washing with sunnah form. If no limbs are formed, it is not washed or named, as it will not be resurrected. The text notes that according to zahir al-riwayah (the apparent transmission), all these rulings (washing, naming, prayer) are prohibited, but the author chose the middle path: wash it (due to its soul aspect) but do not pray over it (due to its being part of a human). The fetus does not inherit or be inherited because it is like a part of the living body. However, if some limbs appear, it will be resurrected, as it has the sanctity of Adam's children—evidenced by legal rulings like istilad (paternity) and 'iddah. The passage then brings a hadith about the intercession of the miscarried fetus for its parents, narrated by Abu Ubayda and Ibn Majah, describing how the fetus stands at the gate of Paradise angrily until its parents enter, or drags them by their umbilical cords if they are destined for Hell. The hadith supports that the fetus lives in the afterlife and is resurrected. The commentator concludes with the general principle that everyone is resurrected in the state they died upon, and the people of Paradise will be like Adam, thirty-three years old and sixty cubits tall. This lesson combines fiqh rulings (wasl, naming, janazah, inheritance) with eschatological proof (hadith) about the fetus's resurrection and intercession.

Key Terms
سقط (saqt): A miscarried fetus that is born before full term, possibly dead or alive.
مختار (mukhtar): The chosen or preferred position within the Hanafi madhhab on a disputed issue.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent or transmitted ruling from the core works (al-usul), often representing the authoritative position unless a stronger dalil overrides.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on performing funeral prayer (janazah) over a miscarried fetus (saqt) that cried after birth?
A) It is obligatory (fard kifayah).
B) It is sunnah mu'akkadah.
C) It is not performed (according to the mukhtar).
D) It is performed only if the fetus showed signs of life after complete emergence.

Key Takeaway
A miscarried fetus that showed signs of life or limbs is washed, named, and buried, but no funeral prayer is offered, based on its dual nature and proof from intercession hadith.

Rulings on Walking and Riding Behind a Funeral
Rulings on walking and riding behind a funeral with proof from Sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on walking and riding behind a funeral and explain the basis from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Walking behind the funeral is superior; walking ahead is disliked; riding is permissible but humility is preferred.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies the proper conduct when following a funeral procession. It addresses two modes: walking and riding, and provides the ruling for each based on prophetic practice and hadith. Understanding these etiquettes ensures one fulfills the sunna with proper adab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
The passage discusses two acts: walking behind the funeral and riding behind it. Determine the hukm level for each from the text.
Walking ahead is 'yukrahu' (disliked); riding is 'la ba'sa' (no harm, i.e., permissible).
2
Locate the prophetic proof
The author cites a hadith from the Sunan where the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) instructs: 'The rider goes behind the funeral, and the walker goes in front of it, close to its right or left.' Identify the source and authenticity.
Also mentions a report from Jabir ibn Samurah showing the Prophet walked and rode.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the preferred position. The Prophet's action of walking behind his son's funeral and his statement indicate that walking is the norm and riding is an exception.
The phrase 'لا بأس' indicates permissibility, but the context shows walking is better.
4
Analyze the rationale for superiority
The commentator explains that walking is closer to humility (tawadu') and more fitting for one seeking intercession (shafi'). Consider why this matters in funeral etiquette.
Humility is a key value in Islamic funerary rites.
5
Distinguish between makruh tahrimi and mubah
The term 'yukrahu' here is understood as makruh tahrimi (close to haram) for walking ahead of the entire procession or alone. Riding is mubah but not recommended without need.
Some scholars may classify it as makruh tanzihi; Hanafi position is stronger.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مشى خلف جنازة ابنه إبراهيم حافياً ويكره أن يتقدم الكل عليها أو ينفرد متقدماً ولا بأس بالركوب خلفها من غير إمتداد لغيره وفي السنن قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: الراكب يسير خلف الجنازة والماشي أمامها قريباً عن يمينها أو عن يسارها وأشار بلا بأس إلى أن المشي أفضل لأنه أقرب إلى التواضع، وأليق بحال الشفيع، وعن جابر بن سمرة أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم تبع جنازة ابن الدحداح ماشياً، راكباً على فرسه» رواه الترمذي وقال حديث حسن قوله: (وفي السنن) أي الأربعة لأبي ورجع داود والترمذي والنسائي وابن ماجه
The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, walked barefoot behind the funeral of his son Ibrahim. It is disliked that one walk ahead of all of them or proceed alone. There is no harm in riding behind it without stretching excessively for others. In the Sunan, the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'The rider goes behind the funeral, and the walker goes in front of it, close to its right or left.' He indicated by 'no harm' that walking is better because it is closer to humility and more fitting for the state of an intercessor. From Jabir ibn Samurah: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, followed the funeral of Ibn al-Dahdah walking while returning on a horse. Tirmidhi narrated it and said it is a hasan hadith. His saying: 'In the Sunan' meaning the four: Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, and Ibn Majah.
Source pages p. 606

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the manner of following a funeral procession. The matn states that walking behind is disliked if one walks ahead of the entire procession or alone. Riding is permissible but without excessive posture. The hashya explains that walking is superior because it demonstrates humility and suits the one seeking intercession. It cites a hadith from Jabir ibn Samurah showing the Prophet walked behind the funeral but also rode back, indicating both are allowed. The commentator identifies 'Sunan' as the four books of hadith.

Key Terms
يكره (yukrahu): Legally disliked (makruh) with tahrimi level here.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is mandatory to walk behind.
B) It is disliked to walk ahead of all or alone.
C) It is permissible to walk anywhere.
D) Walking is forbidden.

Key Takeaway
Walking behind the funeral is the preferred practice due to humility; walking ahead is disliked (makruh tahrimi), and riding is permissible but not recommended.

Prohibition of Raising Voice and Observing Silence at Funerals
Ruling with proof on raising voice and silence in funerals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raising the voice in dhikr and Qur'an during funeral processions and explain the prohibition based on consensus and textual evidence.

Core Idea
Loud dhikr and recitation behind a funeral are impermissible; silent remembrance is the sunnah.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies the proper conduct for those following a funeral. While many may think that any form of dhikr or Qur'an recitation is meritorious, the Hanafi school draws a sharp distinction between silent, inward remembrance and loud, ostentatious displays. The text rules that raising the voice is makruh tahrimi (disliked to the point of prohibition) and that certain common sayings and practices are blameworthy innovations. Let us examine the evidence and reasoning behind these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Ruling
The primary act addressed is raising the voice in dhikr or Qur'an recitation while following a funeral. The ruling is that it is makruh tahrimi. Also, saying phrases like 'every living being dies' is declared a bid'ah.
Makruh tahrimi means it is forbidden and sinful, though not as severe as haram.
2
Locate the Evidence (Dalil)
The text cites multiple authorities (al-Qahistani, al-Zahiriyyah) and states that loud recitation with prolongation is unanimously forbidden (la yajuz bil ijma). Consensus (ijma) is the primary proof.
Ijma is a binding source of law in Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the Scope of Prohibition and Recommendation
What is prohibited: raising voice, loud recitation, and useless worldly speech. What is recommended: silent dhikr (in the heart, audible only to oneself), reflection on death, and supplication. The text even provides recommended phrases.
Silence (al-samt) here means refraining from worldly talk, not from all speech.
4
Recognize Blameworthy Innovations (Bid'ah)
The text identifies specific practices as bid'ah: saying 'every living dies' and carrying food/sheep to the grave (called 'kaffarah' or 'dinner of the grave'). These are innovations because they were not done by the Salaf.
Bid'ah here is blameworthy (qabiha) and stems from imitating non-Salaf practices.
5
Apply the Ruling in Practice
A mufti or knowledgeable person must not remain silent when seeing these innovations; he is obligated to forbid them. The text warns against being deceived by the multitude who commit these acts.
Enjoining good and forbidding wrong applies here, even if the majority practices it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكره رفع الصوت بالذكر والقرآن وعليهم الصمت وقولهم كل حي سيموت ونحو ذلك خلف الجنازة بدعة قيل : يكره تحريماً كما في القهستاني عن القنية، وفي الشرح عن الظهيرية فإن أراد أن يذكر الله تعالى ففي نفسه أي سراً بحيث يسمع نفسه، وفي السراج، ويستحب لمن تبع الجنازة أن يكون مشغولاً بذكر الله تعالى، والتفكر فيما يلقاه الميت، وأن هذا عاقبة أهل الدنيا وليحذر عما لا فائدة فيه من الكلام، فإن هذا وقت ذكر وموعظة فتقبح فيه الغفلة، فإن لم يذكر الله تعالى فليلزم الصمت ولا يرفع صوته بالقراءة، ولا بالذكر ولا يغتر بكثرة من يفعل ذلك، وأما ما يفعله الجهال في القراءة على الجنازة من رفع الصوت والتمطيط فيه فلا يجوز بالإجماع، ولا أحداً يقدر على إنكاره يسع أن يسكت عنه، ولا ينكر عليه ا هـ . قوله : (عليهم الصمت) مبتدأ وخبر (۱) . قوله : (ونحو ذلك) كالأذكار المتعارفة. قوله : (بدعة) أي قبيحة كالمسمى بالكفارة ذكر ابن الحاج في المدخل في الجزء الثاني إن من البدع القبيحة ما يحمل أمام الجنازة من الخبز والخرفان ويسمون ذلك عشاء القبر فإذا وصلوا إليه ذبحوا ذلك بعد الدفن، وفرقوه مع الخبز وذكر مثله المناوي في شرح الأربعين في حديث من أحدث في أمرنا هذا ما ليس منه فهو رد قال ويسمون ذلك بالكفارة فإنه بدعة مذمومة ا هـ قال ابن أمير حاج ولو تصدق بذلك في البيت سراً لكان عملاً صالحاً لو سلم من البدعة أعني أن يتخذ ذلك سنة، أو عادة لأنه لم يكن من فعل من مضى يعني السلف، والخير كله في اتباعهم، وفي السراج، ويستحب لمن مرت عليه جنازة، أو رآها أن يقول: سبحان الذي لا إله إلا هو الحي القيوم ويدعو للميت بالخير والتثبيت ا هـ وفي شرعة الإسلام إذا رآها يقول: هذا ما وعدنا الله ورسوله وصدق الله ورسوله اللهم زدنا إيماناً، وتسليماً ويكثر من التسبيح والتهليل خلف الجنازة، ولا يتكلم بشيء من كلام الدنيا، ولا ينظر يميناً، ولا شمالاً فإن ذلك يقسي القلب ، هـ، ولا ينبغي أن يرجع من يتبع الجنازة حتى يصلى بحر . لا يموت (1) قوله مبتدأ أو خبر في بعض النسخ ما نصه قوله وعليهم الصمت عليهم اسم فعل بمعنى ليلزموا والصمت منصوب على الإغراء والمراد أنهم يصمتون عما كان من الدنيا أ.هـ.
Raising the voice in remembrance and Quran is disliked, and they must observe silence. Their saying 'Every living being will die' and similar things behind the funeral is an innovation. It is said: it is disliked with tahrim, as in al-Qahistani from al-Qunyah, and in the Sharh from al-Zahiriyyah. If one wishes to remember Allah, let him do so in his heart, secretly such that he hears himself. In al-Siraj: It is recommended for the follower of a funeral to be occupied with remembrance of Allah, reflection on what the deceased meets, that this is the end of the people of the world. He should beware of useless speech, for this is a time of remembrance and admonition where heedlessness is ugly. If he does not remember Allah, let him maintain silence, not raise his voice in recitation or remembrance, and not be deceived by the multitude who do so. As for what the ignorant do in reciting over the funeral with loud voice and prolongation, it is not permissible by consensus, and no one who is able to deny it may remain silent about it. His saying: 'Alayhim al-samt' is a subject and predicate. His saying: 'Wa nahwa dhalik' like customary remembrances. His saying: 'Bid'ah' meaning ugly innovation, like what is called 'kaffarah'. Ibn al-Hajj mentioned in al-Madkhal in the second volume that among the ugly innovations is carrying bread and sheep in front of a funeral, calling it the dinner of the grave, then slaughtering them after burial and distributing with bread. Al-Manawi mentioned similarly in his commentary on the forty hadith on 'Whoever innovates in this matter of ours what is not part of it is rejected'. He said they call it 'kaffarah' and it is a blameworthy innovation. Ibn Amir Hajj said: If one were to give charity with that at home secretly, it would be a good deed if free from innovation, I mean if it is taken as a sunnah or custom because it was not the practice of those who passed (i.e., the Salaf), and all good is in following them. In al-Siraj: It is recommended for one who passes by a funeral or sees it to say: 'Subhanalladhi la ilaha illa huwa al-hayy al-qayyum' and supplicate for the deceased with good and steadfastness. In Shari'at al-Islam: When he sees it he says: 'Hadha ma wa'adana Allahu wa rasuluhu wa sadaqa Allahu wa rasuluhu Allahumma zidna imanan wa tasliman'. He should increase tasbih and tahlil behind the funeral, not speak any worldly speech, not look right or left, for that hardens the heart. It is not proper for the follower to return until after the prayer. (Footnote: In some copies: 'Qawlahu wa alayhim al-samt' – 'alayhim' is a verbal noun meaning 'lazim' and 'al-samt' is accusative for incitement, meaning they should be silent about worldly matters.)
Source pages p. 606

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling on raising voice during funeral processions. The matn states it is disliked (makruh) to raise the voice in dhikr or Quran, and silence is required. Saying phrases like 'every living being dies' is considered an innovation (bid'ah). The hashya clarifies that the dislike is tahrimi (prohibited-degree). It recommends silent dhikr and contemplation. It strongly condemns loud recitation with prolongation as unanimously forbidden. The commentary then explains the meaning of 'silence' and 'similar things', and elaborates on the innovation of carrying food and slaughtering animals, calling it a blameworthy practice. The text ends with recommended supplications when seeing a funeral, emphasizing remembrance and avoidance of worldly talk.

Key Terms
بدعة (bid'ah): Innovation in religious practice that is blameworthy and rejected.
الصمت (al-samt): Silence, specifically refraining from worldly speech during the funeral.
الإجماع (al-ijma): Consensus of the scholars, a binding source of law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling on saying 'Every living being dies' behind a funeral?
A) It is recommended.
B) It is permissible.
C) It is an innovation (bid'ah).
D) It is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
Raising the voice in remembrance or recitation during a funeral procession is prohibited by consensus, and silence with silent dhikr is the sunnah.
