Rulings on Women Attending Funerals, Weeping, and Wailing
Rulings on women's participation, permissible weeping, and prohibition of wailing and garment tearing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on women following funerals, permissible weeping, and prohibited wailing, and explain the proofs.

Core Idea
Women following funerals is makruh tahrimi; silent tears are allowed; wailing is haram by consensus.

This passage from Maraqi al-Falah with its hashya clarifies the nuanced Hanafi position on women's involvement in funerary rites. While some assume all expressions of grief are forbidden, the text distinguishes between permissible weeping (buka) and prohibited wailing (nawah), and addresses the situation when women insist on following the funeral.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act the matn is ruling upon and the initial hukm level (makruh).
Open with the phrase 'It is disliked for women to follow funerals.'
2
Clarify the degree of karahah
The hashya specifies the dislike is tahrimi (prohibited-degree). Identify the source (al-Durr).
Understand that 'makruh' here means haram in practical effect.
3
Identify the proof for wailing prohibition
The hashya quotes al-Siraj that there is consensus (ijma) on the prohibition of wailing. Recognize this as a strong dalil.
Consensus is qati' in transmission and meaning.
4
Distinguish between weeping and wailing
Weeping (buka) with tears is mubah; wailing (nawah) with voice is haram. Note the exception for listening to weepers to soften the heart.
The term 'buka' is limited to tears, not sound.
5
Recognize the ruling on walking with a wailing woman
If a wailing woman is not deterred, walking with her is not prohibited but is khilaf al-awla. One should disapprove in the heart.
This shows practical guidance when dealing with sin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكره اتباع النساء الجنائز وإن لم تنزجر نائحة فلا بأس بالمشي معها، وينكره بقلبه ولا بأس بالبكا بدمع في منزل الميت ويكره النوح والصياح وشق الجيوب قوله : ( ويكره اتباع النساء الجنائز) أي تحريماً كما في الدر قوله : (وإن لم تتزجر تائحة الخ) قال في السراج : وقد أجمعت الأمة على تحريم النوح، والدعوى بدعوى الجاهلية، وفي البحر عن المجتبى إذا استمع باكية ليرق قلبه ويبكي فلا بأس به إذا أمن الوقوع في الفتنة لاستماعه لبواكي حمزة ا هـ . قوله : فلا بأس بالمشي معها أفاد أنه خلاف الأولى. قوله: (ولا بأس بالبكا) بالقصر لأنّ المراد خروج الدمع قوله : (بدمع) أي لا بصوت فإنه مكروه. قوله: (في منزل الميت) ليس بقيد فيما يظهر. قوله : ( ويكره النوح) أي يحرم لما تقدم عن السراج .
It is disliked for women to follow funerals. Even if a wailing woman is not deterred, there is no harm in walking with her, and he should disapprove in his heart. There is no harm in weeping with tears in the house of the deceased, but wailing, screaming, and tearing garments are disliked. His saying: 'It is disliked for women to follow funerals' meaning with tahrim, as in al-Durr. His saying: 'Even if a wailing woman is not deterred...' al-Siraj said: The ummah has unanimously agreed on the prohibition of wailing and the claim of the pre-Islamic era. In al-Bahr from al-Mujtaba: If one listens to a weeping woman to soften his heart and weep, there is no harm if he is safe from falling into fitnah, because of listening to the weeper of Hamzah. His saying: 'There is no harm in walking with her' indicates it is contrary to the better. His saying: 'There is no harm in weeping' with qasr, because the intended meaning is the flow of tears. His saying: 'with tears' meaning not with voice, for that is disliked. His saying: 'in the house of the deceased' is not a condition, apparently. His saying: 'wailing is disliked' meaning it is prohibited as mentioned from al-Siraj.
Source pages p. 607

Commentary
This passage deals with the rulings on women's involvement in funeral processions, weeping, and wailing. The matn states it is disliked (makruh) for women to follow funerals, and if a wailing woman is not deterred, one may walk with her while disapproving in the heart. Weeping with tears is permissible, but wailing, screaming, and tearing garments are disliked. The hashya clarifies that the dislike for women following is tahrimi (prohibited) based on al-Durr. It quotes al-Siraj that there is consensus on the prohibition of wailing. Listening to a weeping woman to soften the heart is allowed if free from fitnah. Walking with a wailing woman is frowned upon (khilaf al-awla). The term 'buka' here means shedding tears without sound; sound is disliked. The phrase 'in the house of the deceased' is not restrictive.

Key Terms
النوح (al-nawah): Wailing, specifically loud lamentation with a voice expressing grief in a ritualistic manner.
البكا (al-buka): Weeping, here limited to shedding tears without a loud voice.
شق الجيوب (shaqq al-juyub): Tearing of garments, a practice of pre-Islamic mourning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a woman following a funeral according to this passage?
A) It is recommended for women to follow.
B) It is permissible but disliked.
C) It is disliked with tahrim (prohibited-degree).
D) It is completely forbidden without exception.

Key Takeaway
Women following funerals is makruh tahrimi; weeping with tears is mubah; wailing, screaming, and tearing garments are haram/makruh tahrimi by consensus.

Ruling on Standing and Sitting During a Funeral Procession
Ruling on standing for a funeral and sitting before placement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on standing for a funeral and sitting before the corpse is placed, and identify the proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Standing for a funeral is abrogated; sitting before placement is makruh due to explicit prophetic command.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies two related rulings: the abrogation of the command to stand for a passing funeral, and the prohibition of sitting before the corpse is placed. After studying this lesson, you will understand the evidence and the Hanafi position that both actions are makruh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What are the two actions being ruled upon? What is the hukm level for each according to the Hanafi school?
The text mentions standing for a funeral and sitting before placement.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? Identify the hadith and its source.
The hadith: 'Whoever follows a funeral should not sit until it is placed.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? What phrase indicates prohibition?
The explicit command 'لا يجلس' indicates prohibition.
4
Understand the abrogation
Why is standing for a funeral abrogated? What evidence is given for the abrogation?
The practice of the Prophet sitting to contradict the Jews.
5
Apply the ruling
What is the practical implication for a Hanafi today?
It is makruh to stand when a funeral passes by unless following, and makruh to sit before the bier is set down.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يقوم من مرت به جنازة ولم يرد المشي معها، والأمر به منسوخ (و) يكره (الجلوس قبل وضعها) لقوله عليه السلام : من تبع الجنازة فلا يجلس حتى توضع قوله : (ولا يقوم الخ) فهو مكروه كما في القهستاني قوله : ( ولم يرد) بضم الياء وكسر الراء والواو للحال قوله : (قبل وضعها أي عن أعناق الرجال لقوله : من تبع الجنازة فلا يجلس حتى توضع وفي الجلوس قبل وضعها ازدراء بها ا هـ من الشرح ، ويكره القيام بعده كما في الدر لما روى عبادة بن الصامت أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان لا يجلس حتى يوضع الميت في اللحد فكان قائماً . أصحابه على رأس قبر فقال يهودي : هكذا نصنع في موتانا فجلس ، وقال لأصحابه : خالفوهم يعني في القيام بعد وضعه عن الأعناق فلذاكره كذا في البحر .
One should not stand if a funeral passes by him and he does not intend to walk with it; the command to stand is abrogated. And it is disliked to sit before it is placed, because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever follows a funeral should not sit until it is placed.' His saying: 'He should not stand...' so it is disliked, as in al-Qahistani. His saying: 'and he did not intend' with dammah on the ya and kasr on the ra, and the waw is for the state. His saying: 'before its placement' i.e., from the necks of the men, because of his saying: 'Whoever follows a funeral should not sit until it is placed.' In sitting before placement is disrespect. It is also disliked to stand after placement, as in al-Durr, because of what Ubadah ibn al-Samit narrated: The Prophet would not sit until the deceased was placed in the niche, so he was standing. His companions stood at the head of the grave. A Jew said: 'We do this for our dead,' so he sat and said to his companions: 'Contradict them,' meaning in standing after placing it from the necks. So it is disliked. Thus in al-Bahr.
Source pages p. 607

Commentary
This passage discusses two rulings: standing for a funeral procession and sitting before the corpse is placed on the ground. The matn states it is abrogated (mansukh) to stand for a funeral if one does not intend to follow; it is disliked to sit before the corpse is laid down. The hashya clarifies that both are disliked. It provides a hadith that the follower should not sit until the corpse is placed. Standing after placement is also disliked, as the Prophet sat when Jews stood, to contradict them. The phrase 'before its placement' refers to before being set down from the shoulders of the carriers.

Key Terms
منسوخ (mansukh): Abrogated; the command to stand for a funeral has been repealed.
ازدراء (izdira'): Disrespect; sitting before placement is considered a sign of disrespect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why did the Prophet sit after standing at a grave?
A) Because he was tired.
B) To contradict the Jewish practice of standing.
C) Because the burial was complete.
D) He never sat during funerals.

Key Takeaway
It is makruh to stand for a funeral or to sit before the corpse is placed, as the command to stand is abrogated.

Rulings on Digging the Grave and Its Depth
Ruling on the depth of the grave: half a qama or to the chest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended depth of a grave according to the Hanafi school and explain the reason for the prescribed depth.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school recommends a grave depth of half a qama for preservation of the deceased from predators and odor.

When digging a grave, what depth is sufficient? The Hanafi school provides a clear guideline based on the transmission of Imam Abu Hanifa. This lesson explores the recommended depth, its proof, and the wisdom behind it, ensuring the deceased is properly protected.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on grave depth
State the recommended depth: half a qama (the height of a person) or to the chest. Determine the hukm level (sunnah muakkadah).
The depth is not obligatory; increasing it is considered good (mustahabb).
2
Locate the proof
The text cites a narration from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad from Imam Abu Hanifa. Identify the book (al-Hujjah) and the authoritativeness of this riwayah.
This narration is from the nawadir (rare transmissions) but widely accepted.
3
Understand the reason (illah)
The depth is intended for preservation (hifz): protecting the body from wild animals and preventing odor from emerging.
This reason explains why the depth is recommended and why increasing it is also good.
4
Note the authority level
The ruling is based on a transmission (riwayah) from Abu Hanifa, classified as nawadir. Evaluate its weight in Hanafi fiqh.
Despite being nawadir, it is the mufta bihi position.
5
Contrast with potential misunderstandings
Some may think the depth is obligatory; clarify that it is sunnah muakkadah and increasing it is permissible and good.
The text explicitly says 'for one who increases it, it is good'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويحفر القبر نصف قامة أو إلى الصدر ولمن يزد كان حسناً لأنه أبلغ في الحفظ قوله: (ويحفر القبر نصف قامة في الحجة روى الحسن بن زياد عن الإمام رحمه الله تعالى قال طول القبر على قدر طول الإنسان وعرضه قدر نصف قامة كذا في الشرح عن التتارخانية. قوله : (لأنه أبلغ في الحفظ) أي حفظ الميت من السباع وحفظ الرائحة من الظهور
The grave should be dug half a qama or to the chest, and for one who increases it, it is good, because it is more effective for preservation. His saying: 'The grave should be dug half a qama' in al-Hujjah: al-Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Imam (may Allah have mercy on him) that he said: The length of the grave is according to the length of the person, and its width is half a qama. Thus in the sharh from al-Tatar Khaniyyah. His saying: 'because it is more effective for preservation' meaning preservation of the deceased from predators and preservation of the smell from emergence.
Source pages p. 607

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on the dimensions of a grave. The matn states that the grave should be dug half a qama (a qama is about the height of a person) or to the chest. Increasing the depth is considered good. The hashya explains that the length of the grave matches the height of the deceased, and the width is half a qama, based on a transmission from Abu Hanifa by al-Hasan ibn Ziyad. The reason for the depth is to protect the body from wild animals and to prevent odor from escaping.

Key Terms
قامة (qama): A unit of length equal to the height of a person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main purpose of digging the grave half a qama deep according to the text?
A) To save space.
B) For preservation from predators and smell.
C) To make it easier to fill.
D) To follow a specific hadith.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a grave depth of half a qama is recommended for preservation, and increasing it is considered good.

Ruling on Grave Construction: Lahd vs. Shaq
Ruling on using lay (niche) in hard soil and shaq (trench) in soft soil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on lahd and shaq, and identify when each method is applicable based on soil type.

Core Idea
Lahd (niche) is sunnah in hard soil; shaq (trench) is permissible in soft soil.

The proper construction of a grave is a sunnah that reflects respect for the deceased. This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi clarifies the preferred method—a lateral niche (lahd) facing the qibla—and when a central trench (shaq) is an acceptable alternative. It also addresses the manner of placing the deceased and records the practice of some Companions who chose a simpler burial.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general ruling
Recognize that the passage discusses how to construct the grave after digging it. The default ruling for hard soil is to make a lahd (niche) from the qibla side.
Lahd is the sunnah based on the Prophet's practice.
2
Identify the exception for soft soil
Find the clause 'except in soft soil' which permits shaq (trench) when the soil is too loose for a niche.
The exception is practical: in soft soil, a niche would collapse.
3
Understand the method of placing the deceased
Note that the deceased should be placed straight (head first) into the lahd, not inverted. This preserves the sunnah and avoids inauspiciousness.
Inverting the body is contrary to sunnah and potentially harmful.
4
Recognize the optional practice of Companions
Some Companions preferred burial without a niche or trench, using bricks to keep earth off the face. This shows that while lahd is sunnah, simpler methods are not prohibited.
Their practice is reported but not mandatory.

ويلحد في أرض صلبة من جانب القبلة (ولا يشق) بحفيرة في وسط القبر يوضع فيها الميت إلا في أرض رخوة فلا بأس به فيها قوله: (ويلحد) يقال لحد القبر أي جعل فيه لحد أو الحد الميت وضعه في اللحد بفتح اللام كفلس، ويضمها كقفل، الأول الحود والثاني الحاد، وهو حفيرة تجعل في جانب القبلة من القبر يوضع فيها الميت، وينصب عليها اللبن ،قهستاني والسنة أن يدخل الميت فيه بالسواء، ولا يدخل فيه منكوساً على رأسه لمخالفة السنة، ولأنه قد تنزل المواد إلى فمه وأنفه ولأن فيه تشاؤماً بإنزاله أول منزل من منازل الآخرة منكوساً على رأسه ذكره ابن الحاج في المدخل. قوله : (يوضع فيها الميت بعد أن یبنی حافتاه باللبن، أو غيره، ثم يوضع الميت بينهما، ويسقف عليه باللبن، أو السقف الميت وأوصى كثير من الصحابة أن يرموا في التراب من غير لحد، ولا شق، وقال: ليس أحد جنبي أولى بالتراب من الآخر، ويوقي وجهه التراب بلبنتين، أو ثلاث.
And he should make a lateral niche in hard soil from the direction of the qibla, and he should not make a trench (shiq) – a digging in the middle of the grave in which the deceased is placed – except in soft soil; there is no harm in it there. His saying: 'yulhid' – it is said: alhada al-qabra, i.e., he made a niche in it, or alhada al-mayyita: he placed him in the niche. 'Al-lahd' is with fatha on the lam (like 'falas') and can be with dammah (like 'qufl'): the former is 'lahd', the latter 'lahd'. It is a pit made in the qibla side of the grave in which the deceased is placed, and bricks are set over it. According to al-Qahistani: The sunnah is to enter the deceased straight (head first), not inverted on his head, because that contradicts the sunnah, and because fluids may descend to his mouth and nose, and it is inauspicious to enter the first of the stages of the afterlife inverted on his head, as mentioned by Ibn al-Hajj in al-Madkhal. His saying: 'in which the deceased is placed after its edges are built with bricks or other material, then the deceased is placed between them, and covered with bricks or wood...' Many Companions instructed that they be thrown into the dirt without a niche or trench, saying: 'One side is no more entitled to the dirt than the other,' and they would protect his face from dirt with two or three bricks.
Source pages p. 607

Commentary
This passage discusses two methods of grave construction: a lateral niche (lahd) and a central trench (shaq). The matn states that in hard soil, one should dig a niche in the qibla side; in soft soil, a trench is permissible. The hashya defines 'lahd' and explains the sunnah method: the deceased should be placed straight (head first), not inverted. It also reports that many Companions preferred to be buried without a niche or trench, placing bricks to protect the face from soil. This indicates that while the sunnah is to dig a niche, simple burial is also acceptable.

Key Terms
لحد (lahd): A lateral cavity in the side of the grave facing the qibla to place the deceased.
شق (shaq): A trench dug in the middle of the grave to place the deceased, used in soft soil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is it permissible to use a central trench (shaq) instead of a lateral niche (lahd)?
A) In hard soil.
B) In soft soil.
C) Always.
D) For women only.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a lateral niche (lahd) is sunnah in hard soil, but a central trench (shaq) is permissible in soft soil.
